Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
Definition and Rejection of Ittiraad as a Valid 'Illah
Definition and refutation of ittiraad as a proof for 'illah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ittiraad, distinguish it from ta'thir, and explain why it is not a valid indicator of 'illah in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Mere correlation (ittiraad) does not prove causation; the 'illah must have revealed effect (ta'thir).

In this lesson, we examine the concept of ittiraad (co-rotation) as discussed in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author defines it and then rejects it as a valid method for identifying the effective cause ('illah) in qiyas. You will learn that the Hanafi school requires a manifest effect (ta'thir) from the Lawgiver, not mere coincidence. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Define ittiraad
Start by extracting the definition from the text: ittiraad is the co-rotation of a ruling with a description in both existence and non-existence, or only in existence.
Some scholars restrict it to existence-only; others require both.
2
Identify the disagreement about its meaning
Note the two interpretations: (1) the ruling exists when the description exists and is absent when the description is absent; (2) the ruling exists when the description exists, without requiring absence when the description is absent.
The author acknowledges this ikhtilaf but moves on to the ruling.
3
Understand the Hanafi rejection
The text states that ittiraad is not a proof because the existence of a ruling alongside a description may be coincidental, like a condition (shart) which is not a cause. Non-existence has no role in establishing causality.
Coincidence (ittifaq) undermines any causal inference from co-extension.
4
Apply the principle: ta'thir vs. ittiraad
Recognize that for a description to be a valid 'illah, there must be evidence of its effect (ta'thir) from the Lawgiver, typically via nass or qiyas with a manifest illa. The example of minority (sighar) in the commentary illustrates this: it is considered effective because of revealed reasoning (hardship/necessity), not mere correlation.
This step internalizes the key lesson: correlation is not causation in usul.

And it is called al-mu'thiriyya (causative) without al-it.tiraad, and it is named al-t.ardiyya. The meaning of it.tiraad is the co-rotation of the ruling with the description in existence and non-existence, or only in existence. He said that only because they disagreed about its meaning. Some said: the existence of the ruling at the existence of the description, and its non-existence at its non-existence. And some said: its existence at its existence, but they did not require its non-existence at its non-existence. In any case, it is not a proof for us - a ruling whose effect is manifest - because existence may be coincidental, like the existence of the ruling at the condition. So it does not indicate being a cause. And non-existence has no role in causation, obviously, and because of its obviousness he did not address it. [Urdu: Because helplessness and constraint are attached to it. A minor girl is incapable of transacting in her own self, she does not know how to conduct properly. And the effect of non-bulugh in the mother's wilayah is manifest by consensus, so by qiyas the guardian should have the right of wilayah of marriage. So al-saghir (minority) is effective in establishing wilayah, just as tawaf is effective for the purification of the cat (surra), because hardship and necessity are present in both. So, as tawaf became a necessary necessity for the purification of the cat, similarly minority became a necessary necessity for the wilayah of marriage. Ittiraad and tard are not proof. The author's statement 'salahiyya wa 'adalah' relates to ittiraad, which is called tardiyya. The meaning of ittiraad is the rotation of the ruling with the description: whenever the description is present, the ruling is present; and when the description is absent, the ruling is absent. But some said: existence only, without requiring absence. In any case, it is not a proof for us until the effect of the description is manifest from the Lawgiver. Because existence may be coincidental, like the existence of a ruling at the existence of a condition. So their co-existence does not prove causality. So how can non-existence be a proof? Since this is obvious, the author did not pay attention to it.]
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a definition and refutation of ittiraad (co-extension) as a basis for establishing a legal cause ('illah) in qiyas. The author begins by defining ittiraad as the rotation of the ruling with a description in both existence and non-existence, or only in existence. The Hanafis hold that ittiraad alone is not a proof because the existence of a ruling alongside a description may be purely coincidental, like a condition (shart) which is not a cause. For a description to be a valid 'illah, there must be evidence of its effect (ta'thir) from the Lawgiver. The commentary illustrates with the example of minority (sighar) and the need for a guardian in marriage: minority is effective because of the associated hardship and necessity. The author then reiterates that ittiraad, being mere correlation, is insufficient. The passage clearly distinguishes between valid 'illah (which requires revealed ta'thir) and mere co-extension (which can be accidental).

Key Terms
الاطراد (al-ittiraad): The co-rotation of a ruling with a description in existence and/or non-existence
الطردية (al-tardiyya): Synonym for ittiraad; the state of being co-extensive
التاثير (al-ta'thir): The manifest effect of a description on the ruling, established by revealed evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, is ittiraad alone sufficient to establish a description as a valid 'illah?
A) Yes, it is always sufficient
B) No, it is not sufficient because it may be coincidental
C) Yes, but only in penal law
D) No, it is sufficient only if supported by ijma

Key Takeaway
Ittiraad (co-rotation) is not a valid proof for 'illah; the description must have a manifest effect (ta'thir) from the Lawgiver.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Invalidity of Ta'lil bi al-Nafi and the Marriage Witness Dispute
Explains ta'lil bi al-nafi with a Shafi'i-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that negating a specific cause does not negate the ruling, identify the exception, and apply the rule to evaluate the Shafi'i argument on marriage witnesses.

Core Idea
Negating one possible cause does not negate a ruling; only when the cause is exclusive does its negation negate.

This lesson explores a fundamental Hanafi usul principle: reasoning by negation (ta'lil bi al-nafi) is generally invalid. Using the classic dispute on marriage witnesses, the author illustrates how the Shafi'i argument fails because negating maliyya (property status) does not preclude other causes for female testimony. The lesson also explains the exception when the negated cause is the only possible cause, as in Imam Muhammad's example of the usurper's child.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of ta'lil bi al-nafi
The passage states that just as ittiraad (consistent correlation) is not a valid proof, the negation of a particular cause cannot prove the negation of the ruling. This is because a ruling may arise from multiple causes; the absence of one does not prove the absence of all.
The key statement: 'لأن استقصاء العدم لا يمنع الوجود من وجه آخر' (Because the complete enumeration of non-existence does not prevent existence from another aspect).
2
Analyze the Shafi'i argument as an example of ta'lil bi al-nafi
Al-Shafi'i argues that marriage is not property (mal), and everything that is not property does not contract with female witnesses; therefore marriage requires two male witnesses. This is a classic ta'lil bi al-nafi: negating maliyya to negate female witnesses.
The Shafi'i dalil: 'كُلَّ مَا هُوَ لَيْسَ بِمَالٍ لا يَنْعَقِدُ بِشَهَادَةِ النِّسَاءِ' (Everything that is not property does not contract with female witnesses).
3
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafis reject the Shafi'i inference. They argue that marriage is not like hudud or qisas (which are dropped by doubts), and that marriage is actually of a lower degree than property (adna darajah min al-mal). Since property accepts female witnesses, marriage is even more deserving.
The Hanafi argument uses qiyas: property accepts female witnesses; marriage is adna darajah, so it should too. Also, the cause for female testimony in marriage is its immunity from doubt, not its property status.
4
Identify the exception to the rule
The passage notes that ta'lil bi al-nafi is accepted only when the negated cause is the exclusive cause (sabab mu'ayyan). In that case, its absence does negate the ruling, as in Imam Muhammad's example of the usurper's child.
Example: If a usurper's slave gives birth, the child is not liable because the usurpation was only on the mother, not the child. The cause for liability (usurpation) is specific to the mother.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (that marriage can be witnessed by one man and two women) is relied upon because the Shafi'i argument is based on a flawed ta'lil bi al-nafi. The correct method is to consider all possible causes.
The mufta bihi position: marriage is valid with one man and two women (Hanafi view).

And similar to it is ta'lil bi al-nafi, like ittiraad, meaning just as the ittiraad of a description is not capable of being a proof, similarly the negation of a particular cause cannot be a proof for the negation of the ruling. In some copies of Kitab al-Manazil, instead of 'mithluhu al-ta'lil', the words 'wa min jinsihi al-taqlil' occur, but there is no difference in meaning. Because the complete enumeration of non-existence does not prevent existence from another aspect, since the ruling may occur due to multiple causes. So it does not necessarily follow from the negation of one cause that all causes in the world are negated, such that the negation of the cause would indicate the negation of the ruling. Like the statement of al-Shafi'i concerning marriage: regarding the non-contract of marriage with the testimony of women along with men, that it is not property, and everything that is not property does not contract with the testimony of women along with men; therefore its establishment requires two men, not one man and two women. According to us, the non-existence of maliyya (property status) has no effect on its non-validity with female witnesses, because the cause for the validity of female testimony is that it (marriage) is something that is not dropped by doubt, unlike hudud and qisas which are dropped by doubts, and they are not established by female testimony at all. Also, marriage is of a lower degree than property, as evidenced by the fact that it can be established by property, which property itself cannot be established by. So since property is established by female testimony, it is more fitting that marriage be established by it. This is except when the cause is specific, as an exception from his statement 'and similar to it is ta'lil bi al-nafi', meaning ta'lil bi al-nafi is not accepted in any case except when the cause is specific. For then its negation prevents the existence of the ruling from another aspect, as in Muhammad's statement concerning the child of the usurper: that he is not liable because he did not usurp. But if someone usurped a pregnant slave-girl and she gave birth in the usurper's hand, and then they died, he is liable for the value of the slave-girl but not the child, because the usurpation only occurred on
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage discusses ta'lil bi al-nafi (reasoning by negation) and its invalidity as a method for establishing a ruling. The author states that just as ittiraad is not a valid proof, similarly negating a specific cause does not prove the negation of the ruling, because a ruling may have multiple causes. The Shafi'i argument that marriage is not property and therefore requires two male witnesses is given as an example. The Hanafi response is that marriage is of a lower degree than property (adna darajah min al-mal), and since property can be established by female witnesses, marriage should also be established by them. Moreover, the Hanafis argue that the cause for accepting female testimony in marriage is that marriage is not like hudud or qisas, which are dropped by doubts. The passage also notes an exception: if the specific cause is the only possible cause, then its negation does negate the ruling. An example is given from Imam Muhammad on the liability of a child born to a usurped slave-girl. This nuanced discussion shows the Hanafi method of qiyas and the rejection of simplistic reasoning by negation.

Key Terms
التعليل بالنفي (al-ta'lil bi al-nafi): Reasoning by negation: using the absence of a specific 'illah to prove the negation of a ruling
المالية (al-maliyya): The status of being property (mal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, does the absence of maliyya (property status) in marriage prove that it cannot be established by female witnesses?
A) Yes, because marriage is not property
B) No, because marriage is of a lower degree than property and property accepts female witnesses
C) Yes, but only if there is no other evidence
D) No, because marriage is like hudud

Key Takeaway
Negating one possible cause is insufficient to negate a ruling; the Hanafi school rejects ta'lil bi al-nafi except when the cause is exclusive, as demonstrated in the marriage witness dispute.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Ta'lil bi al-Nafy – Reasoning by Negation of Cause
Explaining the method of ta'lil bi al-nafy with conditions and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which ta'lil bi al-nafy is valid and apply it to new cases using the Hanafi requirements.

Core Idea
Negating a ruling by negating its cause works only when the cause is specified and exclusive.

In the previous passage, we saw how legal rulings are derived from their causes. But can we conclude that a ruling is absent simply because one possible cause is absent? Imam Muhammad's ruling on the child of usurpation shows that this reasoning is valid only when the cause is the sole possible cause. Let's examine the conditions and limits of this method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the method
Recognize that ta'lil bi al-nafy is the reasoning that negates a ruling by negating its cause. The author presents this as a valid method only under strict conditions.
Arabic term: التعليل بالنفي
2
Locate the condition
Find the phrase 'إلا أن يكون السبب معيناً' – 'Except when the cause is specified'. This is the key condition: the cause must be mu'ayyan (exclusive).
3
Study the example
Analyze Imam Muhammad's example of the usurped slave-girl's child. The cause of liability is only usurpation; since the child was not usurped, liability is negated. Confirm that no other cause could impose liability in this specific case.
The example of pearls and amber from the sea also illustrates: no khums because the cause (military conquest) is absent.
4
Contrast with invalid application
Examine al-Shafi'i's argument about marriage and women's testimony. The Hanafis reject it because the cause for accepting women's testimony is not property-nature but immunity from doubt. Thus, negating property-nature does not negate the ruling.
This shows that if multiple causes could produce the ruling, negating one does not negate the ruling.

الإِطِرَادِ الإحْتِجَاجُ بِاسْتِصْحَابِ الْحَالِ فِي عَدَمٍ صَلاحِيتِه لِلدَّلِيلِ وَمَعْنَاهُ طَلَب صُحْبَةِ الْحَالِ لِلْمَاضِي بِأَنْ يَحْكُمَ عَلَى الْمَالِ بِمِثْلِ مَا حَكِمَ فِي الْمَاضِي وَحَاصِلُهُ إِبْقَاءُ مَا كَانَ عَلَى مَا كَانَ بِمُجَرَّدِ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يُوْجَدْ لَهُ دَلِيلٌ مُزِيْلٌ وَهُوَ حُجَّةٌ عِنْدَ الشَّافَعِى اِسْتِدْلالاً بِبَقَاءِ السَّرَائِعِ بَعْدَ وَفَاتِهِ وَعِنْدَ نَاهُوَ لَيْسَ بِحُجْةٍ لأَن المُثْبِت لَيْسَ بِمُيْقٍ فَلا يَلْزَمُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الدَّليلُ الَّذِى أَوْجَبَهُ ابْتِدَاءٌ فِي الزَّمَانِ الْمَاضِي مُبْقِيًا لَهُ فِي زَمَانِ الْحَالِ لاِنَّ الْبَقَاءَ عَرْضٌ حَادِتْ غَيْرَ الْوُجُوْرِ وَلَا يُدْ لَهُ مِنْ سَبب عَلى حِدَةٍ وَأَمَّا بَقَاءُ السَّرَائِعِ فَلَقِيَام الأدلَّةِ عَلَى كَوْنِهِ خَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّينَ وَلَا يَبْعَثُ بَعْدَهُ أَحَدٌ يَنْسِحُهَا إِلا بِمُجَرْدٍ استصحَابِ الْحَالِ وَذَالِكَ إِلا اسْتِصْحَابُ بِالْحَالِ يَتَحَقَّقَ فِي كُلِّ حُكْم عُرِفَ وُجُوْبَهُ بِدَلِيْلِ ثُمَّ وَقَعَ السَّكُ فِى زَوَالِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَقُوْمَ دَلِيْلُ بَقَائِهِ أَوْ عَدَمِهِ مَعَ التامل والاجتهاد فِيهِ فَكَانَ استصحاب حال الْبَقَاءِ عَلى ذالك الْوُجُودِ مُوجِبًا عِنْدَ الشَّافَعِي أَي حُجَّةٌ مُلْزِمَةٌ عَلَى الْخَصمِ وَعِنْدَنَا لاَ يَكُونُ حُجَةٌ مُوْجِبَةً وَلَكِنَّهَا حُجَّةٌ دَافَعَةُ لإِلْوَامِ الْخَصْمِ عَلَيْهِ فَائِدَةُ الْخِلَافِ تَظْهَرُ فِيْمَا ذَكَرَهُ بَقَوْلِهِ. وَهَكَذَا فِي الْمُسْتَخرج مِنَ البَحْرِ
Regarding the slave-girl but not the child: Muhammad here reasoned by negation, saying that the cause of liability in this case is only usurpation, so when it ceases, liability necessarily ceases. Because the full extent of the foot does not prevent existence... it does not follow that the ruling does not exist due to another cause, since sometimes a ruling is established by multiple different causes, so the negation of one specific cause does not necessitate the non-existence of all causes in the world, such that the negation of one cause would indicate the non-existence of the ruling. Like the argument of al-Shafi'i regarding marriage, i.e., regarding its non-conclusion: by the testimony of women with men, saying that the marriage contract is not property, and any transaction that is not property is not concluded by the testimony of women with men. According to us, the lack of property nature has no effect on the ruling that marriage is not valid through women's testimony. The reason is that the cause for considering women's testimony valid in it is not that it is a financial transaction, but rather that marriage is not nullified by doubt (shubha). (Whatever is not nullified by doubt, women's testimony is valid in it; so in marriage, their testimony is valid.) Unlike hudud and qisas, for both of these are nullified by doubts. For this reason, women's testimony is not considered in them. The second proof for the validity of women's testimony in marriage is that the rank of marriage is even lower than property, because marriage can be concluded in jest and play with offer and acceptance, but in jest, the right of property is not established by making an offer. So when property can be established by women's testimony, then a fortiori marriage can be established by women's testimony. Except when the cause is specified. This is an exclusive exception to the author's statement 'specifically', and similarly reasoning by negation. Its meaning is that reasoning by negation is accepted only when the cause of the ruling is specified, because then its non-existence prevents the ruling from existing through another cause. (That is, when besides this cause there is no other cause for the ruling, there remains no possibility of the ruling's existence through another cause. Therefore, when the specified cause is negated, the ruling necessarily ceases.) Like Muhammad's statement regarding the child of usurpation: that the usurper is not liable for it because he did not usurp the child. Because when he usurped a pregnant slave-girl, and she gave birth to the child at the usurper's place, then both (the slave-girl and the child) perished. So the usurper is liable for the value of the slave-girl but not for the child, because usurpation occurred regarding the slave-girl, not the child. In this issue, Muhammad reasoned by negation, saying that the cause of liability in this case is only usurpation, so by its cessation, liability also necessarily ceases. And similarly his statement regarding what is extracted from the sea, like pearls and amber, that there is no khums (one-fifth) on it because the Muslims did not cause the horses to gallop upon it. For the cause of the obligation of khums in war booty is only the galloping of Muslim horses, which is absent here. And the argument by istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity) is connected to reasoning by negation, i.e., it is like uniformity (itrad) in that it is not valid as a proof. Its meaning is to seek the company of the past state, i.e., to judge a thing in the present with the same ruling it had in the past. Its essence is to keep what was as it was, merely because no evidence has been found to remove it. It is a proof according to al-Shafi'i, using as evidence the continuity of the Shari'ah after his death. According to us, it is not a proof, because what establishes is not what preserves. So it does not necessarily follow that the evidence that initially established a ruling in the past time would preserve it in the present time, because continuance (baqa') is an accidental occurrence distinct from existence (wujud) and requires a separate cause. As for the continuity of the Shari'ah, it is due to the proofs that he is the Seal of the Prophets and that no one after him will be sent to abrogate it, not merely by istishab al-hal. That istishab al-hal applies to every ruling whose obligation was known by evidence, then doubt occurred about its lapse, without evidence for its continuance or cessation, after deliberation and ijtihad. So the istishab of continuance on that existence is binding according to al-Shafi'i, i.e., it is a binding proof against the opponent. According to us, it is not a binding proof, but it is a defensive proof to rebut the opponent's argument. The practical difference appears in what he mentioned by his statement: 'And similarly regarding what is extracted from the sea'.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Anwaar discusses two important usul al-fiqh topics: reasoning by negation of a cause (ta'lil bi al-nafy) and the presumption of continuity (istishab al-hal). The author first explains that simply negating one cause does not prove the ruling's absence unless that cause is the exclusive cause. He illustrates with Imam Muhammad's ruling on the liability for a child born to a usurped slave-girl: the usurper is liable for the mother because he usurped her, but not for the child because he did not usurp it. The only cause of liability is usurpation, so when usurpation is absent (for the child), liability is absent. This reasoning is valid only because the cause is specified. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i's argument that marriage cannot be proved by women's testimony because it is not property is rejected by Hanafis, since the cause for accepting women's testimony in marriage is not its property nature but its immunity from nullification by doubt. The passage then turns to istishab al-hal, defined as maintaining a previous ruling in the absence of evidence to change it. The author states that according to al-Shafi'i, istishab is a binding proof, citing the continuity of Islamic law after the Prophet's death. However, the Hanafi position is that istishab is not a binding proof because existence (wujud) and continuance (baqa') are distinct; continuance requires a separate cause. Nevertheless, Hanafis accept istishab as a defensive argument to rebut an opponent's claim. The practical difference is illustrated by the example of items extracted from the sea: Imam Muhammad rules no khums because the cause (military conquest) is absent; this follows the principle of ta'lil bi al-nafy. The Shafi'i might use istishab to argue for khums, but Hanafis do not accept that.

Key Terms
التعليل بالنفي (al-ta'lil bi al-nafy): Reasoning that negates a ruling by negating its cause; valid only when the cause is specified (mu'ayyan) and no other cause can produce the ruling.
علة (illa): The effective cause (ratio legis) that brings about a legal ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, when is ta'lil bi al-nafy valid?
A) Always valid whenever a cause is negated.
B) Only when the cause is the exclusive cause of the ruling.
C) Only in cases of usurpation.
D) Only when the ruling is about financial matters.

Key Takeaway
Ta'lil bi al-nafy is a valid method only when the negated cause is the exclusive cause of the ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Istishab al-Hal – Presumption of Continuity vs. Binding Proof
Explaining istishab al-hal and the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over its validity as a proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on istishab al-hal, and apply the Hanafi view that it is a defensive argument, not a binding proof.

Core Idea
Istishab al-hal preserves a past ruling but does not establish it as binding proof.

Now that we have seen how reasoning by negation works, we turn to another method: istishab al-hal, the presumption of continuity. This principle holds that a state of affairs existing in the past continues to exist until evidence shows otherwise. But is this a binding proof? The Hanafi school says it is not, while the Shafi'i school says it is. Let's examine the arguments and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Define istishab al-hal
Understand its meaning: maintaining a previous ruling in the present merely because no evidence of change has appeared. The Arabic phrase is 'إبقاء ما كان على ما كان'.
Literal: 'presumption of the continuation of the state'.
2
Identify the Hanafi objection
Learn the Hanafi critique: continuance (baqa') is a separate accident from existence (wujud) and requires a separate cause. The original evidence that established the ruling does not automatically preserve it.
Key phrase: ' المُثْبِت لَيْسَ بِمُبْقٍ ' – what establishes is not what preserves.
3
Contrast with Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i argues that istishab is a binding proof, using the continuity of Shari'ah after the Prophet's death as evidence. The Hanafis respond that this continuity is proven by other proofs (seal of prophethood), not istishab.
This difference is not just theoretical; it has practical consequences.
4
Determine the practical difference
The passage gives the example of items from the sea (pearls, amber). The Hanafi ruling (no khums) is based on ta'lil bi al-nafy, not istishab. The Shafi'i might use istishab to argue for khums, but Hanafis do not accept that.
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical outcome of the disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْجَارِيَةِ دُونَ الْوَلَدِ فَقَدْ عَلَّلَ مُحَمَّدٌ ههنا بالنفي بأَنْ عِلَّةَ الضيِّمَانِ فِي هَذِهِ الصُّوَرَةِ لَيْسَتْ إِلا الْغَصَبَ فَبِانْتِقَائِهِ يَنْتَفِي الصَّحَانُ ضَرُورَةٌ لأنَّ اسْتِقْصَاءَ الْقَدَم لَا يَمْنَعُ الْوُجُودَ يوتك مطلوب ملت کے معدوم ہونے سے یہ لازم ترجمه تشریح نہیں آتا کہ حکم کسی دوسری علت سے موجود نہ ہو کیونکہ کبھی کبھی ایک حکم متعدد اور مختلف علتوں سے ثابت ہوتا ہے تو کسی خاص علت کے نہ ہونے سے دنیا کی تمام علتوں کا نہ پایا جانا لازم نہیں آتا۔ تاکہ ایک علت کی نفی حکم کے نہ پائے جانے پر دلالت کرے۔ کقول الشافعی جیسے امام شافعی کا استدلال نکاح کے بارے میں یعنی منعقد نہ ہونے کے بارے میں۔ بشهادةِ النِّسَاءِ مَعَ الرِّجَالِ الخ مرد کے ساتھ عورتوں کی گواہی سے یہ کہہ کر عقد نکاح مال نہیں ہے۔ اور جو معاملہ مال کا نہ ہو وہ معاملہ (مردوں کے ساتھ عورتوں کی شہادت سے منعقد نہیں ہوتا ہمارے نزدیک عورتوں کی شہادت کے ذریعہ نکاح صیح نہ ہونے کے حکم میں عدم مالیت کا کوئی اثر نہیں ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کہ عورتوں کی شہادت اس میں معتبر ہونے کی علت یہ نہیں ہے کہ یہ بھی معاملہ مالیہ ہے۔ بلکہ نکاح شبہ سے ساقط نہ ہونا علت ہے ( جو چیز شبہ سے ساقط نہ ہو اس میں عورتوں کی شہادت معتبر ہے۔ لہذا نکاح میں بھی ان کی شہادت معتبر ہو گی) بخلاف حدود اور قصاص کے کہ یہ دونوں شبہات سے ساقط ہو جاتے ہیں۔ اس وجہ سے ان میں عورتوں کی شہادت کا بھی اعتبار نہیں کیا جاتا۔ نکاح میں عورتوں کی شہادت کے معتبر ہونے کی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نکاح کا مر تبہ تو مال سے بھی بہت کم ہے۔ کیونکہ ہنسی ہنسی اور مذاق میں بھی ایجاب و قبول ہو جائے۔ تو نکاح منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ مگر نداق میں ایجاب کر لینے سے مال کا حق ثابت نہیں ہو تا۔ لہذا جب مال کا ثبوت عورتوں کی شہادت سے ہو جاتا ہے۔ تو بدرجہ اولی عورتوں کی شہادت سے نکاح کا ثبوت ہو جائے گا۔ الأ أَنْ يَكُونَ السَّبَبُ معنا البتہ اگر کسی حکم کا سبب متعین ہو ۔ یہ استثناء مفرغ ہے مصنف کے مُعَيْناً قول ومثله التعليل بالضی ہے اور مطلب اس کا یہ ہے کہ کسی حالت میں تعلیل ہاتھی مقبول لیکن جب حکم کا متعین ہو تو تعلیل بالھی مقبول ہو گی اس وجہ سے کہ اس کا عدم حکم کے وجود کو دوسرے سبب سے مانع ہوتا ہے۔ ( یعنی اس سب کے علاوہ جب حکم کا دوسرا کوئی سب ہی نہیں ہے دوسرے سبب کے ذریعہ حکم کے وجود کا احتمال ہی نہیں رہتا۔ اس بنا پر سب معین کے منتفی ہونے سے حکم کا انتقاء ضروری ہوتا ہے۔ كَقَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ فِی وَلَدِ الْغَضب جیسے امام محمد کا قول ولد مخصوبہ کے بارے میں کہ غاصب اس کا ضامن نہیں ہو گا کیونکہ اس نے بچہ کو غصب نہیں کیا ہے کیونکہ جب کی نے حاملہ باندی کو غصب کر لیا۔ یوں اس نے غاصب کے یہاں بچہ جنا پھر دونوں (جاریہ اور لڑکا) ہلاک ہو گئے تو غاصب جاریہ کی قیمت کا تاوان ادا کر نے کال کر کے کا نہیں۔ کیونکہ غصب جاریہ میں واقع ہوا ہے نہ لڑکے ہیں۔ اس مسئلے میں امام محمد نے تعلیل بالھی کی ہے۔ کہ ضمان کی علت اس صورت میں عرق غصب ہے لہذا غصب کے انتقاء سے ممان بھی ابداعیہ متقی ہو جائے گا۔ وَهَكَذَا قَوْلُهُ فِي الْمُسْتَخرج مِنَ الْبَحْرِ كَاللُّؤْلُو وَالْعَنْبَرِ أَنَّهُ لَأَخَمْسَ فِيْهِ لأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُرْجِفُ عَلَيْهِ الْمُسْلِمَوْنَ فَإِنَّ عِلَّةَ وُجُوْبِ خَمْسِ الْغَنِيمَةِ لَيْسَتْ إِلَّا ايُجَافُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ بِالْخَيْلِ وَهُوَ مُنْتَفٍ هَهُنَا وَالْاحتجاج بِاسْتِصْحَابِ الْحَالِ عَطْفٌ عَلَى التَّعْلِيْلِ بِالنَّفْيِ أَي مِثْلُ الإِطِرَادِ الإحْتِجَاجُ بِاسْتِصْحَابِ الْحَالِ فِي عَدَمٍ صَلاحِيتِه لِلدَّلِيلِ وَمَعْنَاهُ طَلَب صُحْبَةِ الْحَالِ لِلْمَاضِي بِأَنْ يَحْكُمَ عَلَى الْمَالِ بِمِثْلِ مَا حَكِمَ فِي الْمَاضِي وَحَاصِلُهُ إِبْقَاءُ مَا كَانَ عَلَى مَا كَانَ بِمُجَرَّدِ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يُوْجَدْ لَهُ دَلِيلٌ مُزِيْلٌ وَهُوَ حُجَّةٌ عِنْدَ الشَّافَعِى اِسْتِدْلالاً بِبَقَاءِ السَّرَائِعِ بَعْدَ وَفَاتِهِ وَعِنْدَ نَاهُوَ لَيْسَ بِحُجْةٍ لأَن المُثْبِت لَيْسَ بِمُيْقٍ فَلا يَلْزَمُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الدَّليلُ الَّذِى أَوْجَبَهُ ابْتِدَاءٌ فِي الزَّمَانِ الْمَاضِي مُبْقِيًا لَهُ فِي زَمَانِ الْحَالِ لاِنَّ الْبَقَاءَ عَرْضٌ حَادِتْ غَيْرَ الْوُجُوْرِ وَلَا يُدْ لَهُ مِنْ سَبب عَلى حِدَةٍ وَأَمَّا بَقَاءُ السَّرَائِعِ فَلَقِيَام الأدلَّةِ عَلَى كَوْنِهِ خَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّينَ وَلَا يَبْعَثُ بَعْدَهُ أَحَدٌ يَنْسِحُهَا إِلا بِمُجَرْدٍ استصحَابِ الْحَالِ وَذَالِكَ إِلا اسْتِصْحَابُ بِالْحَالِ يَتَحَقَّقَ فِي كُلِّ حُكْم عُرِفَ وُجُوْبَهُ بِدَلِيْلِ ثُمَّ وَقَعَ السَّكُ فِى زَوَالِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَقُوْمَ دَلِيْلُ بَقَائِهِ أَوْ عَدَمِهِ مَعَ التامل والاجتهاد فِيهِ فَكَانَ استصحاب حال الْبَقَاءِ عَلى ذالك الْوُجُودِ مُوجِبًا عِنْدَ الشَّافَعِي أَي حُجَّةٌ مُلْزِمَةٌ عَلَى الْخَصمِ وَعِنْدَنَا لاَ يَكُونُ حُجَةٌ مُوْجِبَةً وَلَكِنَّهَا حُجَّةٌ دَافَعَةُ لإِلْوَامِ الْخَصْمِ عَلَيْهِ فَائِدَةُ الْخِلَافِ تَظْهَرُ فِيْمَا ذَكَرَهُ بَقَوْلِهِ. وَهَكَذَا فِي الْمُسْتَخرج مِنَ البَحْرِ
Regarding the slave-girl but not the child: Muhammad here reasoned by negation, saying that the cause of liability in this case is only usurpation, so when it ceases, liability necessarily ceases. Because the full extent of the foot does not prevent existence... it does not follow that the ruling does not exist due to another cause, since sometimes a ruling is established by multiple different causes, so the negation of one specific cause does not necessitate the non-existence of all causes in the world, such that the negation of one cause would indicate the non-existence of the ruling. Like the argument of al-Shafi'i regarding marriage, i.e., regarding its non-conclusion: by the testimony of women with men, saying that the marriage contract is not property, and any transaction that is not property is not concluded by the testimony of women with men. According to us, the lack of property nature has no effect on the ruling that marriage is not valid through women's testimony. The reason is that the cause for considering women's testimony valid in it is not that it is a financial transaction, but rather that marriage is not nullified by doubt (shubha). (Whatever is not nullified by doubt, women's testimony is valid in it; so in marriage, their testimony is valid.) Unlike hudud and qisas, for both of these are nullified by doubts. For this reason, women's testimony is not considered in them. The second proof for the validity of women's testimony in marriage is that the rank of marriage is even lower than property, because marriage can be concluded in jest and play with offer and acceptance, but in jest, the right of property is not established by making an offer. So when property can be established by women's testimony, then a fortiori marriage can be established by women's testimony. Except when the cause is specified. This is an exclusive exception to the author's statement 'specifically', and similarly reasoning by negation. Its meaning is that reasoning by negation is accepted only when the cause of the ruling is specified, because then its non-existence prevents the ruling from existing through another cause. (That is, when besides this cause there is no other cause for the ruling, there remains no possibility of the ruling's existence through another cause. Therefore, when the specified cause is negated, the ruling necessarily ceases.) Like Muhammad's statement regarding the child of usurpation: that the usurper is not liable for it because he did not usurp the child. Because when he usurped a pregnant slave-girl, and she gave birth to the child at the usurper's place, then both (the slave-girl and the child) perished. So the usurper is liable for the value of the slave-girl but not for the child, because usurpation occurred regarding the slave-girl, not the child. In this issue, Muhammad reasoned by negation, saying that the cause of liability in this case is only usurpation, so by its cessation, liability also necessarily ceases. And similarly his statement regarding what is extracted from the sea, like pearls and amber, that there is no khums (one-fifth) on it because the Muslims did not cause the horses to gallop upon it. For the cause of the obligation of khums in war booty is only the galloping of Muslim horses, which is absent here. And the argument by istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity) is connected to reasoning by negation, i.e., it is like uniformity (itrad) in that it is not valid as a proof. Its meaning is to seek the company of the past state, i.e., to judge a thing in the present with the same ruling it had in the past. Its essence is to keep what was as it was, merely because no evidence has been found to remove it. It is a proof according to al-Shafi'i, using as evidence the continuity of the Shari'ah after his death. According to us, it is not a proof, because what establishes is not what preserves. So it does not necessarily follow that the evidence that initially established a ruling in the past time would preserve it in the present time, because continuance (baqa') is an accidental occurrence distinct from existence (wujud) and requires a separate cause. As for the continuity of the Shari'ah, it is due to the proofs that he is the Seal of the Prophets and that no one after him will be sent to abrogate it, not merely by istishab al-hal. That istishab al-hal applies to every ruling whose obligation was known by evidence, then doubt occurred about its lapse, without evidence for its continuance or cessation, after deliberation and ijtihad. So the istishab of continuance on that existence is binding according to al-Shafi'i, i.e., it is a binding proof against the opponent. According to us, it is not a binding proof, but it is a defensive proof to rebut the opponent's argument. The practical difference appears in what he mentioned by his statement: 'And similarly regarding what is extracted from the sea'.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Anwaar discusses two important usul al-fiqh topics: reasoning by negation of a cause (ta'lil bi al-nafy) and the presumption of continuity (istishab al-hal). The author first explains that simply negating one cause does not prove the ruling's absence unless that cause is the exclusive cause. He illustrates with Imam Muhammad's ruling on the liability for a child born to a usurped slave-girl: the usurper is liable for the mother because he usurped her, but not for the child because he did not usurp it. The only cause of liability is usurpation, so when usurpation is absent (for the child), liability is absent. This reasoning is valid only because the cause is specified. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i's argument that marriage cannot be proved by women's testimony because it is not property is rejected by Hanafis, since the cause for accepting women's testimony in marriage is not its property nature but its immunity from nullification by doubt. The passage then turns to istishab al-hal, defined as maintaining a previous ruling in the absence of evidence to change it. The author states that according to al-Shafi'i, istishab is a binding proof, citing the continuity of Islamic law after the Prophet's death. However, the Hanafi position is that istishab is not a binding proof because existence (wujud) and continuance (baqa') are distinct; continuance requires a separate cause. Nevertheless, Hanafis accept istishab as a defensive argument to rebut an opponent's claim. The practical difference is illustrated by the example of items extracted from the sea: Imam Muhammad rules no khums because the cause (military conquest) is absent; this follows the principle of ta'lil bi al-nafy. The Shafi'i might use istishab to argue for khums, but Hanafis do not accept that.

Key Terms
استصحاب الحال (istishab al-hal): Presumption of continuity: maintaining a previous ruling in the absence of evidence to change it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is the function of istishab al-hal?
A) It is a binding proof that obliges the opponent to accept the presumption.
B) It is a defensive argument to rebut the opponent's claim, but not a binding proof.
C) It is not accepted in any form as a proof.
D) It is only valid in cases of doubt about ritual purity.

Key Takeaway
Istishab al-hal is a presumption of continuity that is defensive, not binding, in the Hanafi school.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Conflict of Similarities is Not a Valid Proof
Refuting argument from conflicting similarities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why ta'arud al-ashbah is rejected as a proof in Hanafi usul and apply the refutation to similar arguments.

Core Idea
Conflict of similarities creates doubt, but doubt requires evidence – it is not itself proof.

This passage addresses a specific argumentative technique in usul al-fiqh: using conflicting similarities to challenge a clear ruling. The Hanafis reject this method, as demonstrated through a detailed refutation of Imam Zufar's reasoning regarding the obligation of washing the elbows in wudu. We will dissect the logical structure of this refutation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed method
Recognise that 'ta'arud al-ashbah' (conflict of similarities) is being criticised as an invalid proof. Understand that it refers to situations where two different analogies apply to the same case, creating doubt.
This is an usul rule: such conflict cannot establish a ruling.
2
Examine Zufar's argument
Zufar uses the ambiguity of the preposition 'ila' (ghayah): some limits are inclusive, some exclusive. He leverages this to argue that washing the elbows might not be obligatory.
His doubt is based on a linguistic pattern, not on specific evidence for the wudu case.
3
Trace the refutation's first move
The author asserts that doubt itself is a new claim that requires evidence. Zufar's argument, starting from doubt, lacks a basis.
‘Doubt establishes nothing at all.’
4
Follow the dialectical response
If Zufar claims that the conflict of similarities is his evidence, that too needs proof. If he points to the existence of both inclusive and exclusive ghayah as evidence, he must know which category the disputed matter falls into. If he knows, doubt is resolved; if not, he admits ignorance.
This is a logical refutation: each step demands a definitive answer.
5
Conclude the invalidity
Since Zufar cannot resolve the doubt without clear evidence, his argument fails. The Hanafi position (that elbows must be washed) stands on stronger proofs.
The method of ta'arud al-ashbah is deemed 'acting without evidence'.

وَالاِحْتِجَاجُ بِتَعَارُضِ الأَشْبَاهِ عَطْفٌ عَلَى مَا قَبْلَهُ أَيْ وَمِثْلُ الإِطْرَادِ فِي عَدَمِ صَلاَحِيَتِهِ لِلدَّلِيلِ الاِحْتِجَاجُ بِتَعَارُضِ الأَشْبَاهِ فِي عَدَمِ صَلاَحِيَتِهِ لِلدَّلِيلِ وَهُوَ عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ تَنَافِي أَمْرَيْنِ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِمَّا يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَلْحَقَ بِهِ الْمُتَنَازَعُ فِيهِ كَقَوْلِ زُفَرَ فِي عَدَمِ وُجُوبِ غُسْلِ الْمَرَافِقِ أَنْ مِنَ الْغَايَاتِ مَا يَدْخُلُ فِي الْمُغَيَّا كَقَوْلِهِمْ قَرَأْتُ الْكِتَابَ مِنْ أَوَّلِهِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ وَمِنْهَا مَا لاَ يَدْخُلُ كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى ثُمَّ أَتِمُّوا الصِّيَامَ إِلَى اللَّيْلِ فَلاَ تَدْخُلُ الْمَرَافِقُ فِي وُجُوبِ غَسْلِ الْيَدِ بِالشَّكِّ؛ لأَنَّ الشَّكَّ لاَ يُثْبِتُ شَيْئًا أَصْلاً وَهَذَا عَمَلٌ بِغَيْرِ دَلِيلٍ أَيْ هَذَا الاِحْتِجَاجُ الَّذِي احْتَجَّ بِهِ زُفَرُ عَمَلٌ بِغَيْرِ دَلِيلٍ فَيَكُونُ فَاسِدًا إِلاَّنَّ الشَّكَّ أَمْرٌ حَادِثٌ فَلاَ بُدَّ لَهُ مِنْ دَلِيلٍ فَإِنْ قَالَ دَلِيلُهُ تَعَارُضُ الأَشْبَاهِ قُلْنَا هُوَ أَيْضًا حَادِثٌ لاَ بُدَّ لَهُ مِنْ دَلِيلٍ فَإِنْ قَالَ دَلِيلُهُ دُخُولُ بَعْضِ الْغَايَاتِ مَعَ عَدَمِ دُخُولِ بَعْضِهَا قُلْنَا لَهُ هَلْ تَعْلَمُ أَنَّ الْمُتَنَازَعَ فِيهِ مِنْ أَيِّ الْقَبِيلِ فَإِنْ قَالَ أَعْلَمُ فَقَدْ زَالَ الشَّكُّ وَجَاءَ الْعِلْمُ وَإِنْ قَالَ لاَ أَعْلَمُ فَقَدْ أَقَرَّ بِجَهْلِهِ وَعَدَمُ الدَّلِيلِ مَعَهُ وَهُوَ لاَ يَكُونُ حُجَّةً عَلَيْنَا.
And the argument by conflict of similarities is conjoined to what preceded it, i.e., similar to al-itrad in its lack of suitability as a proof is the argument by conflict of similarities in its lack of suitability as a proof. It is the conflict of two matters each of which it is possible that the disputed matter be attached to it. Like the statement of Zufar regarding the non-obligation of washing the elbows: that among the ends (ghayat) there are those that enter into the thing ended (al-mughayya), as when they say 'I read the book from its beginning to its end,' and among them there are those that do not enter, like His statement Exalted: 'Then complete the fast until the night.' So the elbows are not included in the obligation of washing the hand due to doubt; because doubt establishes nothing at all, and this is acting without evidence. That is, this argument with which Zufar argued is acting without evidence, so it is invalid, because doubt is a new matter, so it must have evidence. If he said: its evidence is the conflict of similarities, we say: that too is new, it must have evidence. If he said: its evidence is the entering of some ends and the non-entering of some others, we say to him: Do you know which category the disputed matter belongs to? If he says: I know, then the doubt has gone and knowledge has come. If he says: I do not know, then he has admitted his ignorance, and lack of evidence applies to him, and it is not a proof against us.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage refutes the use of 'ta'arud al-ashbah' (conflict of similarities) as a valid proof in usul al-fiqh. The author explains that just like al-itrad (coincidence) is not a proof, similarly, when two things resemble the disputed matter in different ways and conflict, this cannot serve as evidence. The example is Imam Zufar's argument that washing the elbows in wudu is not obligatory. He uses the fact that some prepositions of end (ghayat) include the thing they end (like 'from beginning to end' includes the end), while some exclude it (like 'fast until night' excludes night). He applies this doubt (shakk) to the verse on wudu (Quran 5:6) which says 'wash your hands up to the elbows' – perhaps elbows are excluded. The author refutes this by stating that doubt itself is a new occurrence and requires evidence. If Zufar says the conflict of similarities is his evidence, we respond that this conflict is also a new matter needing proof. If he claims that the existence of both types of ghayat (inclusive and exclusive) is his evidence, we ask whether he knows which category the disputed matter falls into. If he knows, then the doubt is resolved; if he does not know, he admits ignorance, and his argument cannot stand. This aligns with the Hanafi position that wudu requires washing the elbows based on the explicit command and consensus.

Key Terms
تَعَارُضُ الأَشْبَاهِ (taʿāruḍ al-ashbāh): A conflict between two or more similarities that could each be analogically applied to the case in question, creating doubt.
الغَايَة (al-ghāyah): The endpoint of an action, signified by the preposition 'ila' (to/up to). The ruling on whether the limit is included or excluded is based on context.
زُفَر (Zufar): Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a prominent early Hanafi jurist known for his independent reasoning (ijtihad) and occasional dissenting views.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider Imam Zufar's argument about the elbows to be 'acting without evidence'?
A) Because Zufar relied on a hadith that is weak.
B) Because doubt (shakk) is a new occurrence that itself requires evidence.
C) Because elbows are clearly outside the obligation of washing.
D) Because Zufar's analogy was based on a single similarity.

Key Takeaway
Conflict of similarities (ta'arud al-ashbah) is not a valid proof because doubt requires evidence, and a method that relies on unresolved doubt is legally invalid.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Invalidity of Proof by Contradiction of Similarities
Refuting proof by contradiction of similarities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why contradiction of similarities (taʿāruḍ al-ashbāh) is invalid as a proof in Hanafi usul and refute an argument based on it.

Core Idea
Contradictory similarities create doubt, not certainty; a proof must resolve the issue, not rely on unresolved doubt.

This lesson examines a fundamental Hanafi usul principle: that contradictory similarities (taʿāruḍ al-ashbāh) cannot serve as a valid proof. We will explore the reasoning behind this rule through Imam Zufar's argument about washing the elbows in wudu—a case often cited to illustrate the fallacy of relying on ambiguous similarities. By understanding the refutation, you will sharpen your ability to evaluate qiyas arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Recognize the Hanafi position that contradiction of similarities (taʿāruḍ al-ashbāh) is not a valid proof. Just like itṭirād (parallelism) alone is insufficient, contradictory similarities cannot establish a ruling.
This is a key limitation on qiyas.
2
Define the concept
Understand what taʿāruḍ al-ashbāh means: two matters that each resemble the disputed case but point to different rulings, creating doubt.
The doubt is unresolved; no distinguishing feature is present.
3
Analyze the example
Examine Imam Zufar's argument: in wudu, the end (ghāyah) 'to the elbows' may or may not include the elbows, based on examples from Arabic usage. The doubt leads him to claim non-obligation.
Zufar uses the ambiguity to question the obligation.
4
Apply the refutation
See how the Hanafi refutation works: doubt itself is an occurrence (ḥādith) requiring proof. If Zufar knows which usage applies, doubt resolves; if not, he admits ignorance. Either way, the argument fails.
Thus, taʿāruḍ al-ashbāh cannot establish a ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بے شمار مسائل اختلافی کتب فقہ میں درج ہیں۔ والاحتجاج بِتَعَارُض الاشتباه (۴) اور استدلال تعارض اشباہ و نظائر سے اس جملہ کا بھی ماسبق پر عطف ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح اطراد دلیل بننے کے قابل نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح کسی چیز سے مشابہت رکھنے والی دو نظیروں کا تعارض بھی دلیل بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا اور مراد تعارض اشباہ سے یہ ہے کہ ایسے دو امور کا تقاضہ ایک دوسرے سے مختلف ہو۔ اور ان دونوں امور میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے یہ ممکن ہو کہ وہ متنازع فیہ کے ساتھ ملحق ہو ۔ كَقَوْلِ زُفَرَ فِي عَدَمَ وَجُوْبِ غُسلِ الْمَرَافِقِ جیسے امام زفر فرماتے ہیں کہ وضو میں مرافق کہنیوں کے دھونے کے واجب نہ ہونے پر اس دلیل سے استدلال کیا جاتا ہے کہ بعض عنایت منیا میں داخل ہوتی ہے جیسے محاورہ ہے کہ میں نے اس کتاب کو شروع سے آخر تک پڑھا لیا ہے اس مثال میں غایت معیا میں داخل ہے یعنی پڑھنے والے نے کتاب کا آخر پڑھ لیا ہے۔ وَمِنْهَا مَا لَا يَدْخُلُ اور بعض نمایت وہ ہوتی ہے جو معیا میں داخل نہیں ہوتی۔ جیسے اللہ تعالی کا قول ہے "ثُمَّ أَتِمُّوا الصِّيَامَ إِلَى اللَّيْلِ" اور پھر تم روزے کو رات تک پورا کرو۔ فَلاَ تَدْخُلُ الْمَرَافِقُ فِي وُجُوْبِ غَسْلِ الْيَدِ بِالشَّكِّ [؟] تو وجوب غسل ید میں مرافق داخل نہ ہوئی۔ اس وجہ سے کہ شک کسی چیز کو ثابت نہیں کرتا - وَهَذَا عَمَلٌ بِغَيْرِ دَلِيْلٍ اور یہ عمل بغیر دلیل کے ہے۔ یعنی یہ استدلال جو جناب امام زفر نے کہا ہے کہ وہ عمل بلادلیل کے ہے لہذا فاسد ہے کیونکہ شک امر حادث ہے (بعد میں واقع ہوا ہے ) اس لئے اس شک کے لئے دلیل کی ضرورت ہے۔ اگر امام زفر جواب دیں کہ اشباہ کا تعارض اس کی دلیل ہے تو ہم جواب دیں گے کہ یہ تعارض اشباہ بھی امر حادث ہے اس کے لئے دلیل کیا ہے۔ اگر امام زفر جواب دیں کہ غایت دو ہیں یہ ایک غایت مغیا کے تحت داخل ہوتی ہے اور دوسری غایت مغیا کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوتی تو ہم جواب میں ان سے دریافت کریں گے کہ مسئلہ متنازع فیہ کس قبیل سے ہے تو اگر امام زفر جواب دیں کہ ہاں میں جانتا ہوں تو بات صاف ہے کہ شک زائل ہو گیا۔ اور علم حاصل ہو گیا۔ استدلال کی بنیاد شک پر تھی جب وہ زائل ہو گیا تو استدلال ہی فاسد ہو گیا اور اگر جواب میں فرمائیں کہ میں متنازع فیہ کو نہیں جانتا تو انہوں نے اپنی جہالت اور اپنے پاس استدلال کی دلیل نہ ہونے کا اعتراف و اقرار کر لیا۔ مگر یہ اعتراض دوسروں کے لئے حجت نہیں بنے گا۔
Innumerable issues of disagreement are recorded in books of fiqh. And the proof by contradiction of similarities (4) — and this statement is also conjoined to what preceded. Just as parallelism (itṭirād) is not fit to be a proof, similarly the contradiction of two similar matters that resemble something is also not capable of being a proof. The meaning of contradiction of similarities is that two matters have different requirements, and it is possible for each of them to be attached to the disputed case. Like the saying of Zufar regarding the non-obligation of washing the elbows: he argues that some ends (ghāyāt) enter into the limit (mughayyā), as in the proverb 'I read the book from beginning to end' where the end is included. And some ends do not enter, like Allah's saying 'then complete the fast until night' — so the elbows do not enter into the obligation of washing the hand due to doubt, because doubt does not establish anything. And this is action without proof — that is, this argument of Imam Zufar is action without proof, hence it is invalid, because doubt is an occurrence that requires a proof. If Imam Zufar answers that the contradiction of similarities is its proof, we say that this contradiction of similarities is also an occurrence requiring a proof. If he says that there are two ends, one entering and one not, we ask him: does he know which category the disputed matter belongs to? If he says he knows, then doubt is removed and knowledge is attained, and the argument was based on doubt, so it becomes invalid. If he says he does not know, then he admits ignorance and lack of proof, but this objection is not a proof against us.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule explaining why contradiction of similarities (ta'arrud al-ashbah) is not a valid proof. The author first states that just as parallelism (itṭirād) is insufficient, similarly contradictory similarities cannot serve as evidence. The example is Imam Zufar's argument about the obligation of washing the elbows in wudu. Zufar claimed that because some prepositions like 'to' (ilā) can include the limit and sometimes exclude, doubt arises, and therefore the obligation is not established. The refutation: doubt itself is an occurrence that requires proof. If Zufar knows which case applies, doubt is resolved; if not, he admits ignorance. Thus his argument is invalid. The commentary follows the logical progression of the original text, preserving the internal Hanafi reasoning.

Key Terms
اطراد (itṭirād): consistent application of a common attribute without exception as a requirement for valid qiyas
تعارض الاشتباه (taʿāruḍ al-ashbāh): contradiction of similarities where two similar matters conflict in their indication to the ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul discussed, why is Imam Zufar's argument using ta'arrud al-ashbah invalid?
A) Because it relies on doubt, which is an occurrence requiring proof.
B) Because it is based on a Quranic verse that has been abrogated.
C) Because it uses a distinguishing feature that is absent in the branch.
D) Because it contradicts the consensus of the companions.

Key Takeaway
Contradiction of similarities (taʿāruḍ al-ashbāh) is invalid as a proof because it relies on unresolved doubt; a valid proof must provide certainty or a clear distinguishing feature.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Refutation of the Shafi'i Qiyas on Touching the Private Part
Refuting the Shafi'i qiyas on touching the private part

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the validity of a qiyas by identifying circular reasoning and missing conditions, and explain the Hanafi counter-dalil from the Quran.

Core Idea
A qiyas that compares a thing to itself or ignores a necessary condition is invalid.

In this lesson, we examine a classic usul dispute: does touching the private part invalidate wudu? The Shafi'is argue by qiyas to touching while urinating. The Hanafis expose the logical flaw in that qiyas and support their position with a Quranic verse. You will learn to recognize invalid analogies and see how textual and rational arguments interact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i qiyas
State the original case (asl): touching the private part while urinating invalidates wudu (agreed upon). The new case (far'): touching the private part without urinating. The proposed common cause (illa): the act of touching the private part.
This qiyas is the basis of the Shafi'i position.
2
Examine the common cause
Ask: Does the illa 'touching the private part' add anything beyond what is already in the asl? If the illa is identical to the asl, the analogy is circular (comparing a thing to itself).
Circular qiyas is invalid because it does not extend to a new case.
3
Consider the condition of urine
If we assume that urine is a necessary condition for the hukm in the asl, then the asl includes an element absent in the far' (urine). This creates a difference (farq) that invalidates the analogy.
The Hanafi critique offers a dilemma: either the illa is insufficient (circular) or the asl has a missing condition.
4
Analyze the Hanafi counter-dalil
The Hanafis cite Quran 9:108 praising those who purify themselves, which involves touching the private part. If touching invalidated wudu, Allah would not praise them. This is an indirect textual indication (dalil iqtirani) that touching does not break wudu.
This counter-argument is described in the text as 'countering invalid with invalid' but serves as a rhetorical refutation.
5
Evaluate the overall ikhtilaf
Compare the strength of each position: the Shafi'i rely solely on qiyas which is logically flawed; the Hanafi have a textual indication and a logical refutation. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that touching does not invalidate wudu.
Practical consequence: a Hanafi need not repeat wudu after touching, while a Shafi'i must.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالاحْتِجَاجُ بِمَا لَا يَسْتَقِلُ إِلَّا بِوَصْفٍ يَقَعُ بِهِ الْفَرْقُ (۵) اور استدلال کرنا ایسے وصف سے جو مستقل نہ ہو سکے جب تک کہ اس کے ساتھ کسی دوسرے وصف کو نہ ملایا جائے لیکن اس کے ملانے سے اصل اور فرع کے درمیان فرق پیدا ہو جائے۔ یہ جملہ بھی اپنے ما سبق پر عطف ہے یعنی جس طرح اطراد دلیل بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا۔ اسی طرح ایسی علت سے استدلال کرنا درست نہیں ہے جو اثبات حکم میں مستقل نہ ہو۔ بجز ایسے وصف کے جو علت کے ساتھ ملائے جس کے ذریعہ فرق واقع ہو جائے بین الاصل اور فرع کے درمیان یعنی فرع میں وہ وصف منظم نہ پایا جائے اور صرف اصل میں موجود ہو۔ كَقَوْلِهِمْ فِي مَسِّ الذَّكَرِ یعنی شوافع کا قول مس ذکر کے ناقض وضو قرار دینے میں اس طرح استدلال کرنا کہ انه مس الفرج فكان حدثاً كَمَا إِذَا مَسَّهُ وَهُوَ يَبُولُ کہ اس میں شرمگاہ کا مس ہے اس لئے یہ ناقض وضو ہو گا جس وقت پیشاب کرتے وقت ذکر کا چھونا بالاتفاق ناقض وضو ہے۔ یہ قیاس فاسد ہے۔ کیونکہ مقیس علیہ یعنی پیشاب کرتے وقت ذکر کے ناقض وضو ہونے میں بول (پیشاب) کی قید کا اعتبار نہ کیا جائے تو شے کا قیاس اپنے نفس پر قیاس ہوگا یعنی مس ذکر کا قیاس مس ذکر پر لازم آئے گا اور یہ باطل ہے۔ اور بالفرض مان بھی لیں کہ مقیس علیہ میں بول کی قید معتبر ہے تو بھی اصل اور فرع کے درمیان فرق ہے کیونکہ مقیس علیہ میں پیشاب موجود ہے جبکہ فرع میں نہیں۔ وَقَدْ عَارَضَ هَذَا الْقِيَاسَ الْحَنَفِيَّةُ مُعَارَضَةَ الْفَاسِدِ بِالْفَاسِدِ فَقَالُوا إِنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى مَدَحَ الْمُسْتَنْجِيْنَ بِالْمَاءِ فِي قَوْلِهِ {فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا} وَلَا شَكَّ أَنَّ فِيهِ مَسَّ الْفَرْجِ فَلَوْ أَنَّ كَانَ حَدَثًا لَمَا مَدَحَهُمْ بِهِ. وَهَذَا كَمَا تَرَىٰ.
The proof by something that does not stand except with a description that creates a distinction (5). And the argument using a description that cannot stand alone until another description is joined to it, but joining it creates a difference between the original and the branch. This sentence is also conjoined to what preceded: just as parallelism is not fit as proof, similarly it is not correct to argue with a cause that is not independent in establishing the ruling, unless it is joined with a description that creates a distinction between the original and the branch, meaning that description is not found systematically in the branch but only in the original. Like their saying regarding touching the private part: the Shafi'is argue that touching the private part invalidates wudu by analogy to when one touches it while urinating, which is unanimously invalidating. This analogy is invalid because if the condition of urine is not considered in the original, then the analogy is of a thing to itself (circular). And if we suppose the condition of urine is considered, then there is a difference between the original (urine present) and the branch (urine absent). The Hanafis countered this invalid analogy with another invalid analogy by saying that Allah praised those who purify themselves with water in His saying 'In it are men who love to purify themselves', and there is no doubt that this involves touching the private part; if it were an invalidator of wudu, He would not have praised them. And this is as you see.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage presents point (5) from the usul text: an argument based on a description that is not independently sufficient is invalid unless it is joined with another description that creates a distinction between the original and the branch. The example is the Shafi'i claim that touching the private part invalidates wudu, analogized to touching while urinating. The Hanafi critique: either the urine is considered (making the analogy invalid because the branch lacks urine) or not considered (making it an analogy of a thing to itself, which is circular). The Hanafis then counter with a different argument (criticized as 'countering invalid with invalid') by citing the Quranic verse praising those who purify themselves, implying that touching the private part is not an invalidator. This passage is a dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on the validity of this qiyas, with the Hanafi position that touching the private part does not invalidate wudu, supported by textual evidence and logical refutation.

Key Terms
قياس فاسد (qiyās fāsid): An invalid analogy that fails to meet the conditions of sound qiyas, such as comparing a thing to itself or missing a necessary condition.
مس الذكر (mass al-dhakar): Touching the male private part, which is a point of ikhtilaf regarding nullification of wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the Hanafis consider the Shafi'i qiyas on touching the private part invalid?
A) Because it relies on a weak hadith.
B) Because it compares the same thing to itself unless urine is considered as a condition.
C) Because it contradicts the consensus of all scholars.
D) Because it uses istihsan which is not recognized by the Shafi'i school.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i qiyas on touching the private part demonstrates how logical analysis (naqd al-qiyas) and textual evidence combine to establish a sound ruling.

The Method of Muāraḍa: Countering an Invalid Proof with Another
Hanafis counter Shafi'i proof with Quranic praise of those who use water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hanafi method of mu'aradat al-fasid bi al-fasid and explain how it functions as a refutation tactic in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Countering an invalid proof with an invalid proof exposes the opponent's inconsistency but does not prove your own case.

In Hanafi usul, refutation does not always require a valid counter-proof. Sometimes, the mujtahid demonstrates that the opponent's evidence is flawed by producing an equally flawed argument that leads to an absurd conclusion. This passage illustrates that tactic: the Shafi'is argue that touching the private part invalidates wudu based on a weak analogy (qiyas to urine); the Hanafis respond with a weak Quranic argument to expose the weakness of the analogy. This lesson will help you deconstruct the method and evaluate its purpose in juristic debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shāfiʿī claim and its proof
First, determine what the Shafi'is assert and what evidence they present. They claim touching private part invalidates wudu, citing a hadith (من مس فرجه فليتوضأ) and analogizing to urine exit.
This proof is considered fasid (invalid) by Hanafis because the hadith is interpretable and the qiyas is weak.
2
Recognize the Ḥanafī counter-proof
The Hanafis cite Quran 9:108, praising those who perform istinja with water. Since istinja involves touching the private part, if touching were a hadath, Allah would not praise them.
This counter is also fasid because praise is for the overall purification, not specifically for the act of touching.
3
Analyze the method: muᶜāraḍat al-fāsid bi al-fāsid
The Hanafis are not claiming their proof is strong. They are demonstrating that the Shafi'i analogy leads to a contradiction with a clear Quranic text. By showing an equally invalid proof, they expose the opponent's inconsistency.
This is a dialectical refutation, not a positive proof. The actual Hanafi position rests on stronger evidences.
4
Evaluate the strength of the refutation
The text itself acknowledges the weakness: 'wa hadha kama tara' (this is as you see). The mu'arada method is limited; it only shows that the opponent's proof is not superior, not that the Hanafi position is correct.
A strong refutation would require a valid counter-argument (e.g., other ahadith or qiyas).
5
Distinguish the actual Ḥanafī position from this weak refutation
The Hanafis do not rely on this verse to prove that touching does not invalidate wudu. Their actual position is based on authentic hadith that treat touching as not a hadath (e.g., the Prophet touched his relatives' private parts without renewing wudu) and on the principle that only events (ahdath) break wudu.
This passage is purely dialectical; the real evidence is elsewhere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْحَنَفِيَّةُ مُعَارِضة الْفَاسِدِ بِالْفَاسِدِ فَقَالُوا إِنَّ الله تَعَالَى مَدَحَ الْمُسْتَنْجِيْنَ بالْمَاءِ فِى قَوْلِهِ فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا وَلاشك أن فِيهِ مَسَ الْفَرْجِ فَلَوْ أَنَّ كَانَ حَدَثًا لَمَا مَدَحَهُمْ بِهِ وَهَذَا كَمَا تَرَىٰ.
The Hanafis counter the invalid with the invalid, so they said: Indeed Allah Almighty praised those who perform istinja (cleansing after relieving oneself) with water in His saying: 'In it are men who love to purify themselves.' There is no doubt that in this there is touching of the private part. So if it were a hadath (impurity), He would not have praised them for it. This is as you see.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This is a Hanafi example of responding to invalid reasoning with an equally invalid one (mu'arada al-fasid bi al-fasid). The Shafi'is argued that touching the private part invalidates wudu, using qiyas to urine exit. The Hanafis counter by pointing to the Quranic verse praising those who use water for istinja, which involves touching the private part. If touching were an impurity event (hadath), Allah would not have praised them. However, this reasoning is itself flawed because praise may be for the overall act of purification, not the specific touch. The text concludes that this proof is weak ('wa hadha kama tara'). This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of refuting weak analogies.

Key Terms
مُعَارِضَة الْفَاسِدِ بِالْفَاسِدِ (mu'aradat al-fasid bi al-fasid): Responding to an invalid proof with another invalid proof, often used to show inconsistency in the opponent's reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is the Shafi'i proof that touching the private part invalidates wudu considered invalid?
A) Because there is no evidence that touching is a hadath.
B) Because Allah praised those who perform istinja with water, which involves touching, implying it is not a hadath.
C) Because the Shafi'is use a weak analogy.
D) Because the Hanafis have a different hadith.

Key Takeaway
Mu'aradat al-fasid bi al-fasid is a dialectical tool to expose the weakness of an opponent's proof; it does not constitute a valid positive proof for one's own position.

Five Invalid Types of Reasoning in Qiyas
Lists five invalid types of istidlal with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five types of invalid reasoning in qiyas according to Hanafi usul and apply the conditions of ittirād and istiqlāl to evaluate a proposed 'illah.

Core Idea
Reasoning with a description that lacks ittirād, istiqlāl, or is disputed, obviously invalid, or baseless is rejected in Hanafi qiyas.

This passage classifies five invalid forms of istidlal that are not accepted as valid qiyas in Hanafi usul. Understanding these invalid types is crucial for constructing sound analogies and for critiquing flawed arguments from other schools. The list covers descriptions that fail because they are inconsistent, dependent, contested, self-evidently invalid, or entirely unsupported.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first invalid type: inconsistent description
A description that is not consistently applicable (la yatirid) cannot serve as a valid 'illah because it lacks a universal rule in all cases.
Example: not including the elbows in the obligation of washing the hand (Hanafi ruling on wudu).
2
Identify the second invalid type: non-independent description
A description that is not independently valid (la yastaqill) requires another description to prove the ruling, but adding another creates a difference between the original case and the new case.
The text states that joining them necessitates afrāq between asl and far'.
3
Identify the third invalid type: disputed description
A description whose 'illiyyah is disputed among scholars (mukhtalaf fīh) cannot be used as a proof against an opponent.
Example: Shafi'i argument that immediate kitabah is invalid because it does not prevent expiation, analogizing to a contract for wine.
4
Identify the fourth invalid type: obviously invalid description
A description that is self-evidently invalid (mā lā yushak fī fasādihi) leads to an analogy that is obviously flawed.
Example: analogizing prayer with three verses less than seven to prayer with less than one verse.
5
Identify the fifth invalid type: reasoning without proof
Reasoning with no evidence at all (bi lā dalīl) is simply an assertion and is rejected.
This is annexed to the previous types in invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَلا تَدْخُلُ الْمَرَافِقُ فِي وُجُوْبِ غَسْلِ الهَد بالشنك تو وجوب نسل ید میں مرافق داخل ترجمہ تشریح نہ ہوئی۔ جب واقع ہو جانے کے جب سے اس وجہ سے کہ جنک کسی چیز کو ثابت نہیں شک کرتا - وَهَذَا عَمَل بِغیر دلیل اور یہ عمل بغیر دلیل کے ہے۔ یعنی یہ استدلال جو جناب امام زفر نے کہا ہے کہ وہ عمل بلادلیل کے ہے لہذا فاسد ہے کیونکہ شک امر حادث ہے (بعد میں واقع ہوا ہے ) اس لئے اس شک کے لئے دلیل کی ضرورت ہے۔ إذا کان الأمر کذلک فلا یصح الاحتجاج بوصف لا یطرد، أی لا یستقیم و لایکون منتظما لیس له ضابط کلي في جميع الصور، لأنه لا يصلح للعلية، أی لا یصلح أن یکون علة الحکم. و الاحتجاج بوصف لا یستقل، أي لا یصلح مستقلاً للإثبات إلا إذا يضم إليه وصف آخر، و يلزم من ضمه افتراق الأصل والفرع. و کذلک الاحتجاج بالوصف المختلف فيه، أی الذي وقع الخلاف في کونه علة، کقول الشافعية في عدم جواز الکتابة الحالة: إنه عقد لا یمنع من التکفیر، فکان فاسداً کالکتابة بالخمر. فإن هذا القیاس غیر تام لأن فساد الکتابة بالخمر إنما هو لأجل الخمر لا لعدم منعها من التکفیر. و الاحتجاج بما لا یشک في فساده، کقولهم في وجوب الفاتحة و عدم جواز الصلاة بثلاث آیات ناقص العدد عن السبع: إنه لا یتجزی به الصلاة کما دون الآية. فإن هذا القیاس بدیهي الفساد إذ لا أثر للنقصان عن السبع في فساد الصلاة، وإنما لم تجز بما دون الآیة لأنه لا یسمى قرآناً في العرف. و الاحتجاج بلا دلیل، عطف على ما قبله أي مثل الإطراد في البطلان.
Thus the elbows are not included in the obligation of washing the hand with water? [Then Urdu explanation]. And this is acting without proof. ... If the matter is thus, then reasoning with a description that is not consistently valid (la yatiridu) is not valid, i.e., it is not upright and regular and has no universal rule in all cases, because it is not suitable for causality. Also reasoning with a description that is not independent (la yastaqill), i.e., it is not independently valid for proof unless another description is added to it, and joining them necessitates a difference between the original and the branch. Likewise reasoning with a disputed description (al-mukhtalif fihi), i.e., about which there is disagreement whether it is a cause, like the Shafi'is' statement about the invalidity of immediate emancipation contract (kitabah halah): that it is a contract that does not prevent expiation, so it is invalid like a contract for wine. For this analogy is incomplete because the invalidity of a contract for wine is due to wine itself, not due to its not preventing expiation. And reasoning with that which is undoubtedly invalid (ma la yushak fi fasadihi), like their statement about the obligation of al-Fatihah and the impermissibility of prayer with three verses less than seven: that prayer is not valid with it just as prayer is not valid with less than a verse. For this analogy is obviously invalid since the deficiency from seven has no effect on the invalidity of prayer; rather, prayer with less than a verse is not valid because it is not called Quran in custom, even if it is called Quran linguistically. And reasoning without any proof (bi la dalil), annexed to what preceded, i.e., like al-itrad in invalidity.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage lists several types of invalid reasoning in qiyas, each illustrated with an example. (1) Reasoning with an inconsistent description (al-ihtijaj bi wasf la yatirid): a description that does not hold in all cases cannot be a valid 'illah. The example of not including elbows in hand-washing is mentioned (Hanafi ruling on wudu). (2) Reasoning with a non-independent description: a description that needs another to be effective, and adding another creates a difference between original and branch. (3) Reasoning with a disputed description (al-mukhtalif fihi): the Shafi'is argue that an immediate kitabah is invalid because it does not prevent expiation, analogizing to kitabah with wine, but the analogy fails because wine's invalidity is due to its substance. (4) Reasoning with an obviously invalid description (ma la yushak fi fasadihi): the Shafi'is claim that reciting Three verses less than seven (i.e., less than al-Fatihah) invalidates prayer by analogy with less than one verse, but the invalidity of less than a verse is because it is not Quran by custom, not because of count. (5) Reasoning without any proof (bi la dalil): simply asserting without evidence. All these are examples of fasid (invalid) reasoning according to Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
اطراد (itṭirād): Consistent applicability of a description across all relevant cases; a necessary condition for a valid 'illah.
الوصف المختلف فيه (al-waṣf al-mukhtalaf fīh): A description whose validity as a cause is disputed among scholars; reasoning with it is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of invalid reasoning is illustrated by the Shafi'i claim that an immediate kitabah (emancipation contract) is invalid because it does not prevent expiation, analogizing to a contract for wine?
A) Reasoning with an inconsistent description (la yatirid).
B) Reasoning with a non-independent description (la yastaqill).
C) Reasoning with a disputed description (mukhtalaf fihi).
D) Reasoning with an obviously invalid description (ma la yushak fi fasadihi).

Key Takeaway
The five types of invalid reasoning—inconsistent description, non-independent description, disputed description, obviously invalid description, and baseless reasoning—are all rejected in Hanafi qiyas.
