The Invalidity of Arguing with a Disputed Attribute
Explains invalidity of using a disputed attribute as proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a disputed attribute in a qiyas argument and explain why the Hanafi school rejects it as a valid proof.

Core Idea
An attribute whose causal status is disputed cannot serve as the illa in qiyas; the analogy fails.

In this lesson, we examine a key principle of Hanafi usul: arguing with an attribute whose causality (illiyya) is contested between schools is invalid. The passage from Nur al-Anwar illustrates this through the Shafi‘i argument that immediate kitaba (contract of manumission where the slave pays the whole amount immediately) is invalid because it does not prevent expiation, drawing an analogy to kitaba with wine. The Hanafi response exposes why this reasoning is flawed, showing that the attribute 'non-prevention of expiation' is itself disputed and that the original case (kitaba with wine) is invalid for a different reason.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed attribute
In the Shafi‘i argument, what attribute is being used as the illa for the invalidity of immediate kitaba? It is 'non-prevention of expiation' (عقد لا يمنع من التكفير).
2
Understand why the attribute is disputed
Why do the Hanafis dispute this attribute? Because according to them, kitaba (whether immediate or deferred) never prevents freeing the slave for expiation. So the attribute does not distinguish immediate from deferred kitaba; it exists in both types.
The dispute is over whether the attribute is a valid illa: Shafi‘is claim it is; Hanafis deny it.
3
Analyze the flawed analogy
The Shafi‘is compare immediate kitaba to kitaba with wine, claiming both share the attribute of non-prevention of expiation, so immediate kitaba should also be invalid. But the Hanafi response points out that the invalidity of kitaba with wine is due to wine being non-mutaqawwim (not valuable property for a Muslim), not because of non-prevention of expiation. Thus the attribute is not the cause (illa) in the original case.
This is a classic example of a false analogy: the asl (kitaba with wine) has a different illa.
4
Determine the burden of proof
The Hanafi text argues that the Shafi‘i must first prove that deferred kitaba prevents expiation, so that immediate kitaba can be distinguished by the lack of that preventive effect. Without that proof, the non-prevention attribute is not a valid differentiator.
The burden is on the one claiming the analogy to establish the illa's validity.
5
Conclude the ruling on this type of istidlal
Therefore, arguing with a disputed attribute (al-istidlal bi al-wasf al-mukhtalaf fihi) is invalid as a method of proof in Hanafi usul. The qiyas is not accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإحتجاج بِالْوَصفِ الْمُخْتَلَفِ فِيهِ عَطْفٌ عَلى مَا قَبْلَهُ أَي مِثْلَهُ الإِبْرَادِ فِي عدم صلاحيته للدليل احتجاج بالوَصْفِ الذى أختلف في كونه علةٌ فَانَّهُ أَيْضًا فَاسِدٌ كَقَوْلِهِمْ فِى الْكِتَابَةِ الْحَالة أي الشافعية فِى عَدَم جَوَارِ الْكِتَابَةِ الحالة أَنْها عِقْد لا يُمْنَعُ مِنَ التَكْفِيرِ أَى مِنْ إعْتَاقِ هَذَا الْعَبْدُ الْمُكَاتَبِ بِالتَّكْفِيرَ فَكَانَ فَاسدًا كالكِتابَةِ بالحَمَر فَإِنْ هذ القياس غَيْرُ تَام لأن فَسَتادَ الكِتَابَةِ بالْحُمْرِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ لأَجْلِ الْخَمْرِ لأَلِعَدَم مَنْعِهَا مِن التكفيرِ وَالْكِتَابَةُ عِنْدَنَا لا تَمْنَعُ من التكفير مطلقًا سَوَاءٌ كَانَتْ حَالاً أَوْ مُوْجَلَة فَلَا بُدْ لِلْخَصْمِ مِنْ إقَامَةِ الدَليل على أن الكِتَاب الْمُوَلَةَ تَمْنَعُ مِنْ التَّكْفِيرِ حَتَّى تَكُونَ الْحَالَةُ فَاسدَةُ لأجل عَدَم المَنْعِ مِنَ التَّكْفِيرِ
And arguing with the disputed attribute is conjoined to what precedes it, i.e., like al-ibrād (cooling) in lacking suitability as evidence: arguing with an attribute whose being a cause is disputed is also invalid, like their statement (the Shāfiʿīs) regarding the immediate kitāba (contract of manumission) — that it is a contract that does not prevent expiation, i.e., from freeing this mukātib (slave) for expiation, so it is invalid just like kitāba with wine. But this analogy is incomplete because the invalidity of kitāba with wine is only because of the wine, not because it does not prevent expiation. And kitāba according to us does not prevent expiation at all, whether immediate or deferred. So the opponent must provide evidence that deferred kitāba prevents expiation, so that the immediate one becomes invalid due to not preventing expiation.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar, discusses the second type of invalid istidlāl (arguing with a disputed attribute). The author explains that using an attribute whose causality is disputed (i.e., whether it is the effective cause of a ruling) is invalid as a proof, similar to the previously discussed 'ibrād' (cooling) which is not suitable as evidence. The example given is the Shāfiʿī argument that immediate kitāba (where the slave pays the whole amount immediately) is invalid because it does not prevent freeing the slave for expiation (kafāra). They compare it to kitāba with wine (which is invalid because wine is not valuable property to a Muslim). The Hanafi response is twofold: first, kitāba with wine is invalid due to the wine's non-value, not because of any attribute concerning expiation; second, according to the Ḥanafī school, kitāba does not prevent expiation at all, whether immediate or deferred. Therefore, the Shāfiʿīs first need to prove that deferred kitāba prevents expiation, only then could the non-prevention of immediate kitāba make it invalid. Since they have not done so, their analogy is incomplete and the reasoning is unsound.

Key Terms
الاستدلال بالوصف المختلف فيه (al-istidlāl bi al-waṣf al-mukhtalaf fīh): Arguing using an attribute whose status as a cause (ʿilla) is disputed between schools.
الكتابة الحالة (al-kitāba al-ḥāla): A contract of kitāba where the slave pays the entire amount immediately (in cash).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ḥanafī school, why is the Shāfiʿī analogy comparing immediate kitāba to kitāba with wine invalid?
A) Because kitāba with wine is invalid due to wine being non-mutaqawwim, not due to non-prevention of expiation.
B) Because immediate kitāba prevents expiation, unlike kitāba with wine.
C) Because both types of kitāba are invalid according to Ḥanafīs.
D) Because the Shāfiʿīs have no proof for the validity of deferred kitāba.

Key Takeaway
A qiyas based on a disputed attribute is invalid; the illa must be agreed upon or proven to be the actual cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Arguing with a Self-Evidently Invalid Attribute (Badīhī al-Fasād)
Shows invalidity of using an attribute clearly not a cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an attribute that is self-evidently invalid (badīhī al-fasād) in a qiyās argument, explain why it cannot serve as a valid cause, and apply the Ḥanafī usūl principle that ʿurf determines the basis for legal rulings.

Core Idea
An attribute whose causal irrelevance is obvious cannot be used in qiyās—ʿurf, not arbitrary numbers, determines validity.

In the Ḥanafī uṣūl al-fiqh, not every analogy is valid. One type of invalid istidlāl is arguing with an attribute that is clearly not a cause—its invalidity is self-evident (badīhī al-fasād). This lesson examines such an argument through the example of the Shāfiʿī position on minimum Qur'an recitation in prayer. The Ḥanafī response reveals that the cause for invalidity lies in customary usage (ʿurf), not in numerical thresholds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling and its basis
The Shāfiʿī school holds that Sūrat al-Fātiḥa (seven verses) is obligatory for prayer; praying with only three verses is invalid. Their analogy: just as less than one verse invalidates prayer, so does less than seven (i.e., three) because both are 'less than' a benchmark.
The benchmark for the Shāfiʿīs is Sūrat al-Fātiḥa (seven verses).
2
Pinpoint the attribute used in the analogy
The Shāfiʿī analogy relies on the attribute 'deficiency from seven' (al-nuqṣān ʿan al-sabʿa). They assume this is the effective cause (ʿilla) for invalidating prayer when less than one verse is recited.
3
Analyse the Ḥanafī response
The Ḥanafīs counter that the deficiency from seven is not the real cause. The actual reason less than one verse invalidates prayer is that such a small amount is not considered 'Qur'an recitation' in common custom (ʿurf). Linguistically it may be Qur'an, but customarily it is not.
ʿurf overrides the linguistic definition in determining legal validity.
4
Classify the attribute as self-evidently invalid
Since the attribute 'deficiency from seven' has no causal connection to the invalidity of prayer (the cause is ʿurf, not number), it is badīhī al-fasād—obviously not a valid ʿilla. Thus the analogy is rejected outright.
Self-evident invalidity means no further proof is needed to refute the attribute's causal relevance.
5
Apply the rule to other potential cases
Now test a similar argument: claiming that a 2% profit margin is ribā because anything above 0% is excess. The attribute 'excess above zero' is too broad; the real cause for ribā is the specific condition of increase in certain exchanges. Such an argument would be badīhī al-fasād.
Always verify the ʿilla against known causative factors from sharīʿa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإحتجاج بما لأنك فِي فَسَيَادِهِ عَطَفٌ عَلَى مَا قَبْلَهُ أَى مثْلُ الإِبْرَادِ فِى البطلان الاحتجاج بوصف لايُشك فِي فَسادِهِ بَلْ هُوَ بَدِيهِى كَقَوْلِهِمْ أَى الشَّافَعِيةِ فِي وُجُوبِ الْفَاتِحَةِ وَعَدَم جَوَاز الصلوة بثلث آيات نَاقِصَ الْعَدِدِ عَنِ السَّبْعَةِ أَى عَنْ سُورَةِ الْفَاتِحَةِ فَلا يَتَادَى بِهِ الصَّلَوَةٍ كَمَا دُونَ أَيُّ الآية لايَتَادى به الصلوة لأجلِ ذَالِكَ فَإِنْ هَذَ القَيَاسَ بَدِيهِيُّ الفَسَادِ إِذْلا أثر النُّقْصَانِ عَنِ السَّبْعَةِ فِي فَسَادِ الصَّلَوَةِ وَإِنَّما لَمْ تَجْرٌ بِمَا دُونَ الآيَةِ لأنَّه لايُسمى قُرْآنًا فِي الْعُرْفِ وَانْ سَمِنْ بِهِ فِى اللَّغَةِ
And arguing with that which is unquestionably invalid is conjoined to what precedes it, i.e., like al-ibrād in falseness: arguing with an attribute whose invalidity is not doubted but is self-evident, like their statement (the Shāfiʿīs) regarding the obligation of al-Fātiḥa and the impermissibility of prayer with three verses whose number is less than seven, i.e., less than Sūrat al-Fātiḥa, so prayer is not performed with it just as with less than one verse prayer is not performed. For this analogy is self-evidently invalid, since the deficiency from seven has no effect on the invalidity of prayer; rather, prayer is not valid with less than one verse because it is not called Qur'an in common usage, even if it is called so linguistically.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage discusses the third type of invalid istidlāl: arguing with an attribute that is clearly not a cause—so obvious that no one doubts its invalidity. The author gives the example of the Shāfiʿī argument that Sūrat al-Fātiḥa (seven verses) is obligatory, and prayer with three verses (fewer than seven) is invalid, claiming that just as less than one verse invalidates prayer, so too a number less than seven (like three) should invalidate it. The Ḥanafī response is that this analogy is self-evidently false because the deficiency from seven has no bearing on the validity of prayer; the reason less than one verse invalidates prayer is that such a small amount is not considered Qur'an recitation in customary usage (ʿurf), even though linguistically it might be called Qur'an. Therefore, the attribute 'less than seven' is clearly not a cause for invalidity, making the analogy baseless.

Key Terms
الاحتجاج بما لاشك في فساده (al-iḥtijāj bi-mā lā shakka fī fasādih): Arguing with an attribute that is clearly and indisputably not a valid cause (badīhī al-fasād).
بَدِيهِيّ الفَسَاد (badīhī al-fasād): Self-evidently invalid: an attribute whose lack of causal effect is obvious without need for proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the text consider the Shāfiʿī analogy (prayer with three verses is invalid because it is less than seven, just as less than one verse is invalid) to be self-evidently invalid?
A) Because three verses are always sufficient in Ḥanafī fiqh.
B) Because the number seven has no causal connection to the validity of prayer; the real reason for invalidity with less than one verse is that it is not considered Qur'an in ʿurf.
C) Because the Shāfiʿīs have no proof for the obligation of al-Fātiḥa.
D) Because the Qur'an does not mention the number seven.

Key Takeaway
An analogy that uses an attribute whose causal irrelevance is obvious (badīhī al-fasād) is invalid; the effective cause must be verified against sharʿī principles and ʿurf.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Invalid Qiyas: Refuting Two Shafi'i Analogies
Refuting Shafi'i analogies on kitaba and minimal qira'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an invalid qiyas (qiyas fasid) by analyzing whether the attribute used as the cause (illa) is effective (mu'aththir) in the ruling, and apply the Hanafi critique to refute flawed analogies in kitaba and salat recitation.

Core Idea
An analogy is invalid when the attribute used as the cause is not effective in producing the ruling—it must be specific and exclusive to the original case.

In the study of usul al-fiqh, not all analogies are valid. The Hanafi school rigorously examines the cause (illa) to ensure it is genuinely effective. This lesson examines two Shafi'i analogies that the Hanafis reject as qiyas fasid: one concerning the contract of kitaba hala (immediate payment manumission), and one concerning the minimum recitation in prayer. By analyzing these examples, you will learn how to detect a flawed analogy and understand the Hanafi method of tarjih (preference).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i claim and its basis
What is the specific ruling the Shafi'is are trying to prove through analogy? For kitaba hala, they claim it is invalid. For salat, they claim reciting three verses is insufficient.
These are the far' cases (new cases) in the analogy.
2
Extract the attribute used as the cause (illa)
Which property of the original case (asl) are they analogizing? For kitaba: 'does not prevent kaffara'. For salat: 'number of verses less than seven'.
The asl for kitaba is kitaba with wine; for salat, reciting less than one verse.
3
Examine the Hanafi objection
Why does the Hanafi school argue that this attribute is not effective (ghayr mu'aththir)?
The Hanafis point to a different cause for the asl's ruling, or show that the attribute is not distinctive.
4
Apply the test of universality
Does the attribute apply to valid cases as well? If yes, it cannot be a valid cause because it would invalidate cases that are known to be valid.
In kitaba, the attribute 'does not prevent kaffara' applies to all kitaba, including valid deferred kitaba. In salat, the number of verses is not the real cause.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the Hanafi position and the Shafi'i position?
Hanafis permit kitaba hala and consider three verses sufficient; Shafi'is do not.

Ashraf al-Anwar, Urdu commentary of Nur al-Anwar, volume three. The case is like their statement about kitaba hala (immediate payment kitaba). That is, the Shafi'i statement regarding kitaba hala is: making a slave a mukatab on condition of immediate payment is not valid according to the Shafi'is. Their proof is that it is a contract that does not prevent using the slave for kaffara (expiation). That is, freeing this mukatab slave for kaffara (e.g., zihar, yamin) is not prohibited, whereas if the kitaba contract were valid, the mukatab could not be used for kaffara according to the Hanafis. So it is invalid (fasid) like kitaba with wine? [unclear] Making a slave a mukatab becomes absolutely invalid, as kitaba for wine is invalid. But this analogy is not valid in our view, because the invalidity in our view is due to wine, not because freeing for kaffara is prohibited. Rather, wine is not a mutaqawwim property for a Muslim, so the contract is invalid due to the consideration being invalid. Therefore the basis of the analogy is entirely wrong. Second, in this analogy, a non-effective attribute is taken as the cause, but it is not an effective cause in our view. Moreover, kitaba (mukatab) whether done in any manner — immediate payment or deferred — does not prevent freeing for kaffara. So how can the fact that freeing a mukatab is not prohibited be taken as evidence for the invalidity of the contract? Therefore the Shafi'i scholars must first prove that kitaba mu'ajjala (deferred payment) prevents freeing for kaffara, so that it can be established that kitaba hala (immediate payment) is invalid because it does not prevent kaffara. (7) And arguing by something whose invalidity is beyond doubt: that is, arguing by an attribute that is undoubtedly invalid as a cause. This is also linked to the preceding. Just as al-ittarad (a non-reciprocal attribute) is not a valid argument, similarly arguing by an attribute whose being a cause is indisputably invalid is also void. For example, their statement that the obligation of reciting Surah al-Fatiha and that reciting less than three verses in prayer is not valid — that three is less than seven, i.e., less than Surah al-Fatiha, and Surah al-Fatiha consists of seven verses, so prayer is not valid with it? [unclear] Therefore, reciting three verses — three verses in prayer is the minimum obligatory amount according to the Hanafis, and prayer would not be valid if less is recited, just as reciting less than one verse is not valid. But this analogy is invalid because the invalidity of prayer has nothing to do with the number being less than seven. And the invalidity of reciting less than one verse is because such recitation is not called recitation of Quran in common usage, so it is not considered part of the Quran, even though in linguistic terms it could be called recitation.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of two invalid analogies (qiyas fasid) proposed by the Shafi'i school, as explained by the commentator. The first analogy concerns kitaba hala (immediate payment kitaba). The Shafi'is argue that this contract is invalid because it does not prevent the slave from being used for kaffara, whereas a valid kitaba would. The Hanafi response rejects this reasoning: the invalidity of kitaba with wine is due to wine not being valuable property (mal mutaqawwim), not because of the kaffara issue. Moreover, the attribute 'not preventing kaffara' applies to all forms of kitaba, so it cannot be a cause for invalidity. The Shafi'is should first prove that deferred kitaba prevents kaffara. The second analogy concerns the minimum recitation in prayer: the Shafi'is argue that reciting three verses (less than Surah al-Fatiha's seven) is insufficient, analogizing to the case of less than one verse. The Hanafi response is that the attribute 'being less than seven' is not relevant; the real cause is that less than one verse is not considered Quranic recitation in custom ('urf). These examples illustrate the principle that an analogy is invalid when the attribute used as the cause has no effective connection to the ruling.

Key Terms
الكتابة الحالة (al-kitāba al-ḥāla): A contract of manumission where the slave pays the consideration immediately (in cash).
القياس الفاسد (al-qiyās al-fāsid): An analogy that is invalid because the attribute used as the cause (illa) is not effective or is not properly established.
التكفير (al-takfīr): Expiation (kaffara) for certain sins such as zihar or broken oaths, which may require freeing a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi refutation, why is the Shafi'i analogy on kitaba hala invalid?
A) Because the attribute 'not preventing kaffara' is not an effective cause, as it applies to all forms of kitaba.
B) Because the Shafi'i school does not accept qiyas at all.
C) Because kitaba hala is actually invalid in the Hanafi school.
D) Because the analogy is based on a Qur'anic verse that is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
An invalid analogy (qiyas fasid) arises when the attribute used as the cause is not the effective cause of the original ruling; the Hanafi school insists on a mu'aththir illa to establish sound analogy.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Four Purposes of Legal Reasoning (Ta'līl) in Hanafī Qiyas
Enumerating the categories of what ta'līl aims to establish in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the four categories of what ta'līl establishes in Hanafī qiyas and explain why the fourth category (the original case) is considered the most correct.

Core Idea
Ta'līl in Hanafī qiyas establishes cause, condition, ruling, or the original case – only the fourth is correct.

This lesson introduces a foundational taxonomy in Hanafī uṣūl al-fiqh: the four purposes for which legal reasoning (ta'līl) is employed within qiyas. Understanding these categories is essential to grasp how the Hanafī school extends rulings from original cases to new ones. The text from Ashraf al-Anwār clarifies that while ta'līl can aim at establishing a cause, condition, or ruling, the most sound purpose is establishing the original case (aṣl) itself – a key insight of Hanafī methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
From the text, list the four things that ta'līl aims to establish: (1) the effective cause (mūjib) or its description, (2) the condition (shart) or its description, (3) the ruling (hukm) or its description, and (4) the original case (aṣl) – though the fourth is only mentioned as 'the fourth' in the text.
The fourth is not described in this passage due to a cut-off; it will come later.
2
Distinguish each category
For each category, state what exactly is being established. For cause: proving that a specific attribute (e.g., intoxication) is the cause for a ruling (e.g., prohibition). For condition: proving that something (e.g., purity) is a condition for a ruling (e.g., prayer). For ruling: proving that an act is legally prescribed. For aṣl: establishing the original case with its correct ruling and cause.
The aṣl is the basis for extending rulings to new cases via qiyas.
3
Identify the Hanafī preference
The text explicitly states: 'as-saḥīḥu ʿindanā huwa ar-rābiʿ' – the fourth is correct according to us (Hanafīs). Understand why: Because establishing the aṣl is prior to any extension; without a sound aṣl, qiyas is baseless.
Other schools may differ on which category is primary.
4
Correct the common misunderstanding
The author refutes the claim that this section explains the ruling of qiyas itself. Instead, it explains what ta'līl establishes. The ruling of qiyas (that it yields predominant opinion) is a separate topic.
This avoids confusion between the purpose of ta'līl and the epistemological outcome of qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما فرغ عن بيان التعليلات الصحيحة والفاسدة شرع في بيان ما يؤتى التعليل لأجله صحیحًا وفاسدًا فقال وجملة ما يعلل له أربعة الأأن الصحيح عندنا هو الرابع على ماسياتي َوقال بعض الشارحين أنه بيان لحكم القياس بعد الفراغ من شرطه وركنه وهو خطاء فاحس بل بيان حكمه الذي سيجي في ما بعد في قوله وحكمه إلا صابة بغالب الراء وهذا بيان ما ثبت بالتعليل. الْأَوَّلُ إِثْبَات الْمُوْجِبِ أَوْوَصفِهِ أَى إِثْبَات أَنَّ الْمُوْجِبَ لِلْحُرْمَةِ أَوْ وَصْفِهِ هَذَا أَوْوَصفِه وَالثَّانِي اثْبَات الشرْطِ أَوْ وَصفِهِ أَىٰ إِثْبَاتُ أَنْ شَرْطَ الحُكْم أوْ وَصْفِه هذا وَالثَّالِث اثبات الحُكْم أوْ وصْفه أى إِثْبَات أَنْ هَذَا حُكُمْ مَشْرُوعُ أَمْوَصَفُهُ فَلَا بُدَّ
When he finished explaining the correct and corrupt taʿlīlāt, he began to explain what taʿlīl is brought for, correctly and corruptly. He said: The total of what is reasoned for are four, but the correct one according to us is the fourth as will come later. Some commentators said that this is an explanation of the ruling of qiyās after finishing its condition and pillar, but that is a gross error. Rather, it is an explanation of its ruling that will come later in his statement: 'And its ruling is correctness by predominant opinion.' And this is an explanation of what is established by taʿlīl. The first: establishing the effective cause (mūjib) or its description, i.e., establishing that the cause for prohibition or its description is this or its description. The second: establishing the condition or its description, i.e., establishing that the condition of the ruling or its description is this. The third: establishing the ruling or its description, i.e., establishing whether this is a prescribed ruling or its description. So it is necessary...
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of a new section in Ashraf al-Anwār. After completing the discussion on correct and invalid forms of taʿlīl (legal reasoning), the author turns to the purposes for which taʿlīl is undertaken. He states that there are four categories of things that can be established through taʿlīl, but the fourth (which will be explained later) is the only correct one according to the Hanafīs. He corrects a mistaken interpretation by some commentators who thought this section dealt with the ruling of qiyās itself, clarifying that the ruling of qiyās (that it yields predominant opinion) will come later. The first three categories are: (1) establishing the effective cause (mūjib) or its description – e.g., proving that a specific attribute is the cause for a ruling like prohibition; (2) establishing the condition or its description – e.g., proving that something is a condition for a ruling; (3) establishing the ruling itself or its description – e.g., proving whether an act is legally prescribed. The text cuts off at 'فلا بد' (so it is necessary), suggesting the fourth category is forthcoming. This parsing exercise requires careful attention to the distinctions between cause, condition, and ruling in Hanafī qiyas theory.

Key Terms
التعليل (al-taʿlīl): Legal reasoning to establish a cause, condition, or ruling as part of qiyas.
الموجب (al-mūjib): The effective cause (ʿilla) that necessitates a ruling, e.g., the property that necessitates zakāh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Three Categories of Ta'lil: Mujib, Shart, and Hukm
Classifies the purposes of qiyas into three categories with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three categories of ta'lil (mujib, shart, hukm) and apply the Hanafi principle that these must be established by text, not by opinion or qiyas.

Core Idea
Foundational rulings in qiyas must be established by explicit text, not by analogy or opinion.

This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar classifies the legitimate purposes of ta'lil (causal reasoning) into three categories: establishing the cause (mujib), the condition (shart), or the ruling (hukm) itself. The Hanafi school insists that these foundational elements must be derived from direct textual sources, not from qiyas or personal opinion. We will walk through each category with its examples and see how the Hanafi position contrasts with the Maliki view on specific issues.

Guided Path
1
Classify the three categories
Distinguish between establishing the cause (mujib), the condition (shart), and the ruling (hukm). Each has a distinct role in legal reasoning.
2
Recognize the textual basis requirement
Note that Hanafis require explicit textual evidence (Quran or hadith) for establishing these elements, not mere qiyas or opinion.
3
Analyze the examples
For each category, examine the given example: jinsiyyah for prohibitions (mujib), sawm for zakat (description of mujib), and witnesses for marriage (shart). Identify the textual proof cited.
4
Compare with Maliki view
Note where the Maliki school differs: on the condition of sawm and on witnesses. Understand the different textual readings.
5
Apply the principle
Consider a new case: can the prohibition of marriage to a niece be derived by qiyas? Apply the principle that the cause itself must be textually established.

قیاس کا حکم بیان کرنا مقصود ہے۔ قیاس کے ارکان اور شرائط کو بیان کرنے کے بعد ان کا یہ قول غلط ہے بلکہ قیاس کے حکم کا بیان عنقریب صراحتا آرہا ہے۔ مصنف نے فرمایا ہے وَحُكْمَة الأَصابَةُ بغالب الرائے غالب هَذَا حُكُمْ مَشْرُوعُ أَمْوَصَفُهُ فَلَا بُدَّ . فيْنَا مِنْ اِمْثِلَةٍ سبتُ وَقَدْ بَيْنَهَا بِالتَّرْتِيبِ فَقَالَ كَالْجِنْسِيَةِ لِحُرْمَةِ النِّساءِ مِثال لإثْبَاتِ الْمُوْجِب فَاثْبَات أَنْ الْجِنْسِيَةَ وَحْدَهَا مُوجِبَةٌ لِحُرْمَةِ النِّساءِ مِمَّا لا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَثْبُتَ بِالرّائ وَالتَّعْلِيْلِ وَإِنْمَا أَثْبَتْنَاهُ بِإِشَارَةِ النَّص لأَن رِيَوْ الفَضْلِ لَمَّا حُرِمَ بِمَجْمَوْعِ الْقَدْرِ وَالْجِنْسِ فَشَبْهَةُ الْفَضلِ وَهِيَ النَّسيَلةُ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ تُحْرِمَ بشبهة العِلْةِ أعْنِى الْجِنْسَ وَحْدَهُ أَوِ الْقَدْرُ وَحْدَهُ وَصِفَةُ السَّوْمِ فِي زَكَوةِ الأَنْعَامِ مِثَالُ لإِثْبَاتِ وَصفِ الْمُوْجِبِ فَإِنْ الأَنْعَامَ مُوجِبَةٌ لِلزَّكَوةِ وَوَصفُهَا وَهُوَ السَّوْمُ مما لا يَنْبَغِي أَن يَتَكَلَّمَ فِيْهِ وَيُثْبَتُ بِالتَّعْلِيلِ وَإِثْماً إِثْبَتْنَاهُ بِقَوْلِهِ فِي خَمْسِ مِنَ الإبل السَّائِمَةِ شَاءَةٌ وَعِنْدَ مَالِكِ لا تُشْتَرَطَ الاسامَةُ لِإِطْلَاقِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى خُذُ مِنْ أمْوَالِهِمْ صَدَقَةٌ تُطَهِّرُهُمْ وَتُزَكِّيهِمْ بِهَا وَالشَّهُودُ فِي النِّكَاحَ مِثَالُ الشَّرْطِ فَإِنْ الشهود شرْطَ فِي النِّكَاحِ وَلَا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَتَكَلَّمَ فِيهِ بِالرَّائ وَالْعِلَّةِ إِنَّمَا نُثْبِتُهُ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلاَمُ لاَنكَاحَ إِلا بِشهُودٍ وَقَالَ مَالِكَ لا يَسْتَرِطُ فِيْهِ الإِسْمَادُ بَلْ الإعلان بَقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلاَمُ أَعْلِنُوا النِّكَاحَ وَلَوْ بِالدُّفْ.
And the total of what is made the object of ta'lil (causal attribution) is four categories. However, in our view, only the fourth category is correct, as will come soon. And some other commentators said that the intended purpose here is to explain the ruling of qiyas. After explaining the pillars and conditions of qiyas, their statement is wrong; rather, the ruling of qiyas will come explicitly soon. The author said: 'And its ruling is correctness by predominant opinion.' So here the author does not intend to explain the ruling of qiyas, but rather what is established by ta'lil. The first: establishing the cause (mujib) or its description, i.e., establishing that the cause for prohibition or its description is this. The second: establishing the condition (shart) or its description, i.e., establishing that the condition of the ruling or its description is this. The third: establishing the ruling (hukm) or its description, i.e., establishing that this is a legislated ruling or its description, so it is necessary. We have six examples, and he arranged them in order. He said: Like jinsiyyah (consanguinity) for the prohibition of women is an example of establishing the cause. So establishing that jinsiyyah alone is a cause for the prohibition of women is not something that should be established by opinion and ta'lil; rather, we established it by indication of the text, because riba al-fadl was prohibited due to the combination of quantity and genus, so the resemblance of excess (shubhat al-fadl) which is nasa' (deferred sale) should be prohibited by the resemblance of the cause, i.e., the genus alone or the quantity alone. And the description of being grazing (sawm) in the zakat of livestock is an example of establishing the description of the cause: livestock is a cause for zakat, and its description, which is grazing, is not something that should be discussed and established by ta'lil; rather, we established it by his saying: 'In five grazing camels, one sheep.' According to Malik, grazing is not a condition, due to the absolute nature of the verse: 'Take from their wealth a charity to purify and sanctify them.' And witnesses in marriage are an example of the condition: witnesses are a condition in marriage, and it should not be discussed by opinion and cause; rather, we establish it by his saying, peace be upon him: 'No marriage except with witnesses.' Malik said: 'He does not require privacy there, rather announcement, by his saying: Announce the marriage, even with a duff.'
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage defines the categories of what can be established by ta'lil (causal reasoning) in qiyas. The author first notes that there are four categories but only the fourth is correct, though he doesn't elaborate here. He then explains the first three: (1) establishing the cause (mujib) or its description, (2) establishing the condition (shart) or its description, (3) establishing the ruling (hukm) or its description. For each, he provides examples. For the first, jinsiyyah (consanguinity) is the cause for prohibition of marriage (e.g., mother, sister) — this is established by textual indication, not by opinion. The example of riba shows that jinsiyyah alone can be a cause. For the second, the description of being 'sawm' (grazing) in zakat of livestock is established by hadith, and the author contrasts with Imam Malik who does not consider it a condition. For the third, witnesses in marriage are a condition established by hadith, again contrasting with Malik who requires announcement instead. The passage emphasizes that such foundational matters must be based on text, not on qiyas or opinion.

Key Terms
إثبات الموجب (ithbat al-mujib): Establishing the cause that necessitates a ruling
إثبات الشرط (ithbat al-shart): Establishing a condition for a ruling
إثبات الحكم (ithbat al-hukm): Establishing the ruling itself or its description

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The three categories of ta'lil—mujib, shart, and hukm—must all be established by textual sources, not by qiyas or opinion, according to the Hanafi school.

The Fourth Purpose of Qiyas: Extending the Ruling
Explanation of the fourth purpose of qiyas: extending the ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of ta'diyat al-hukm (extending the ruling) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and state why it is based on ghalib al-ra'y (predominant opinion) rather than certainty.

Core Idea
Qiyas extends a ruling by predominant opinion, not certainty — and this extension is essential for qiyas to be valid.

This lesson unpacks the fourth purpose of qiyas in Hanafi legal theory: extending a ruling from a textually established case (asl) to a new case (far') that lacks direct textual evidence. We will explore why this extension relies on predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y) rather than certainty, and why it is a necessary component of valid qiyas. The passage also includes a garbled line about conditions for witnesses, which we will set aside as likely a textual corruption.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourth purpose
Open by stating the fourth purpose: ta'diyat al-hukm, meaning the extension of a ruling from a text (nass) to a case without textual evidence. This is the core function of qiyas.
The Arabic term ta'diyyah literally means 'making pass over' — transferring the ruling.
2
Understand the epistemological basis
Note that this extension is based on ghalib al-ra'y (predominant opinion), not qat' (certainty) or yaqin (conviction). This reflects the Hanafi view that qiyas yields zann (probability), not certainty.
This distinguishes qiyas from textual evidence (nass) which provides certainty.
3
Recognize the necessity of the extension
The text states 'al-ta'diyyah fihi hukm lazim 'indana' — the extension is a necessary ruling according to us. Qiyas is not valid without it. The extension is as necessary as the reasoning (ta'lil) itself.
Both the illah (cause) and the extension (hukm) are integral to qiyas.
4
Address the garbled ending
The phrase 'wa shurtitat al-adala wa al-dhukuriyyah fiha' appears to be a stray repetition from earlier discussion about witnesses. Ignore it for the purpose of understanding this lesson.
OCR corruption likely; original text may have ended after 'fi al-wujud'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالرَّابِعُ مِنْ جُمْلَةِ مَا يُعَلَّلُ لَهُ تَعْدِيَةُ حُكْمِ النَّصِّ إِلَى مَا لَا نَصَّ فِيهِ لِيَثْبُتَ فِيهِ الْحُكْمُ. مَا لَا نَصَّ فِيهِ بِغَالِبِ الرَّأْيِ دُونَ الْقَطْعِ وَالْيَقِينِ. فَالتَّعْدِيَةُ فِيهِ حُكْمٌ لَازِمٌ عِنْدَنَا لَا يَصِحُّ الْقِيَاسُ بِدُونِهِ وَالتَّعْلِيلُ يُسَاوِيهِ فِي الْوُجُودِ. وَشُرِطَتِ الْعَدَالَةُ وَالذُّكُورَةُ فِيهَا.
And the fourth of the total purposes for which qiyas is performed is the extension (ta'diyyah) of the ruling of the text to a case for which there is no text, so that the ruling may be established in it. [This is done] with predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y), not with certainty and conviction. So the extension in it is a necessary ruling according to us; qiyas is not valid without it, and the reasoning (ta'lil) is equal to it in existence. And the conditions of uprightness and maleness are conditioned in it.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage describes the fourth purpose of qiyas in Islamic legal theory: extending the ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') for which there is no direct textual evidence. The author clarifies that this extension is based on predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y), not on certainty. This is a necessary component of qiyas; without it, qiyas would not be valid. The phrase 'wa shurtitat al-adala wa al-dhukuriyyah fiha' appears to be a stray insertion, possibly a correction or repetition from earlier discussion about witnesses. The passage emphasizes that qiyas operates on probability, not proof, and is a legitimate method of deriving rulings when texts are silent.

Key Terms
تعدية الحكم (ta'diyat al-hukm): The extension of a ruling from an original case to a new case through qiyas.
غالب الرأي (ghalib al-ra'y): Predominant opinion, as opposed to certainty (qat') or conviction (yaqin).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Qiyas extends a ruling by predominant opinion, not certainty, and this extension is a necessary part of qiyas.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

12 min
The Necessity of Ta'diya in Qiyas
Explaining necessity of ta'diya in qiyas and refuting Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that ta'diya is essential for valid qiyas and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding the restricted cause.

Core Idea
Qiyas without transferring the ruling is like a key that fits no lock.

When the sacred texts are silent on a new case, the Hanafi school uses qiyas (analogical reasoning) to extend the ruling. But mere causation (ta'lil) is not enough—the cause must be transmissible (muta'diyah) to new cases. This lesson unpacks why the Hanafis insist on ta'diya, and where Imam al-Shafi'i differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
The author states that when there is no explicit text, qiyas operates by predominant opinion, and ta'diya is a necessary condition. Without it, qiyas is invalid. Locate this claim in the passage.
2
Examine the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi proof: legal proofs must lead to action. If ta'lil only explains the original ruling without extending it, it has no benefit. The cause must exist in the branch as well.
This is a teleological argument—purpose drives the structure.
3
Understand the Shafi'i position
Shafi'i permits a cause restricted to the original (e.g., silver and gold for riba). For him, ta'lil is about explaining wisdom, not necessarily extending. He also warns of circularity if ta'diya is required for the cause's validity.
The circularity argument: if the cause's validity depends on ta'diya, and ta'diya depends on the cause, then a loop arises.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the cause's validity depends on its existence in the branch, not on the act of ta'diya. So no circularity. Causation without transference is useless.
The response reframes the dependence—existence, not operation.
5
Apply to the examples
Work through the marriage witness and witr examples to see how each school's principle yields different rulings.
These examples illustrate the practical consequence (thamarah) of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَالَا نَصَّ فِيْهِ بِغَالِبِ الرَّأْي دُونَ الْقَطْعِ وَالْيَقِيْنِ فَالتَّعْدِيَةٌ فِيْهِ حُكْمٌ لَآزَمٌ عِنْدَنَا لا يَصْحُ القَيَاسُ بِدُوْنِهِ وَالتَّعْلِيلِ يَسبَاوِيْهِ فِي الْوُجُودِ. اور نکاح کے گواہ کے لئے عدالت اور زکواۃ کی ترجمه و تشریح شرط یہ وصف شرط ثابت کرنے کی مثال ہے کیونکہ شہادت تو شرط ہے اور عادل ہونا، اور نہ کر ہو نا گواہ کا وصف ہے۔ مناسب نہیں ہے کہ اس میں رائے سے قیاس کیا جائے۔ بلکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا قول مطلق ہے " لا نكاح المشهود " نكاح بغیر گواہوں کے منعقد نہیں ہوتا۔ اس بات پر دال ہے نہ کہ عدالت شرط ہے اور نہ مذکر ہونا اور امام شافعی اس کی شرط لگاتے ہیں کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے لا نكاح الابولى وشاهدى عدل نكاح بغیر ولی اور عادل گواہوں کے بغیر منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔ اور چونکہ مال کی شہادت نہیں ہے اس لئے عورتوں کی شہادت معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ لہذ انذکر ہونا شرط جیسا کہ امام شافعی کا استدلال ہے ہم پہلے نقل کر چکے ہیں۔ وَالْبُنَيْر : (۵) اور تیراء یہ متراء کی تصغیر ہے جو ابتر کی مؤنث ہے۔ اس سے مراد ہے ایک رکعت والی نماز یہ حکم ثابت کرنے مثال ہے۔ یعنی یہ ثابت کرنا کہ یہ نماز (ایک رکعت والی) مشروع ( شرعا جائز ہے یا نہیں۔ مناسب نہیں کہ اس میں رائے اور قیاس کا دخل دیا جائے۔ اس لئے اس کے مشروع نہ ہونے کو حضور کی حدیث سے ثابت کرتے ہیں کہ نہی عن الببيراء آپ نے صلوة بتیراہ سے منع فرمایا ہے اور امام شافعی اس کو جائز کہتے ہیں۔ وہ حضور کی اس حدیث پر عمل فرماتے ہیں کہ ان احشى أحَدُكُمُ الصُّبْحَ فَلْيُو اذا برُ بِرَكْفة - تمجید کا پڑھنے والا جب صبح صادق کا خوف کرے تو ایک رکعت کی وتر پڑھ لے۔ وصفة الوثر (۲) اور وتر نماز کی صفت یہ صفت حکم ثابت کرنے کی مثال ہے کیونکہ مصلوۃ وتر کا حکم شریعت سے ثابت ہے مگر اس وتر کا سنت یا واجب ہو نا رائے اور قیاس سے ثابت نہیں ہونا چاہیے۔ اس لئے کہ ہم نے وتر کا واجب ہونا حدیث سے ثابت کیا۔ حدیث آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ان الله تَعَالَى زَادَكُمُ صَلوةَ وَهِيَ الْوثر بے شک اللہ تعالی نے تمہاری نمازوں میں ایک نماز کا اضافہ فرمایا ہے۔ سن لو وہ وتر کی نماز ہے۔ (فرائض خمسہ میں اضافہ کے ذکر کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ یہ بھی فرض ہے۔ ورنہ سنت کے ذریعہ فرض میں اصافہ نہیں ہوتا۔ مگر امام شافعی و تر کو سنت کہتے ہیں۔ دلیل ان کی تو آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ و سلم کا فرمان ہے کہ لا الا ان تطوع ( اور کوئی نماز فرض نہیں ہے۔ ہاں نفل پڑھ سکتے ہو) یہ آپ نے اس وقت ارشاد فرمایا تھا۔ جب کہ ایک اعرابی کو تعلیم دیتے ہوئے رات و دن میں پانچ نمازوں کا حکم سنایا ) تو اس نے سوال کیا کیا میرے اوپر ان نمازوں کے علاوہ اور بھی کوئی نماز فرض ہے۔ والرابع (۴) اور چوتھی غرض ان اعراض میں سے جن کے لئے قیاس کیا جاتا ہے ، پھل نہ جس کے لئے ملت کا استنباط کیا جاتا ہے۔ یعنی قیاس کیا جاتا ہے۔ تَعْدِيَةُ حُكم النص إلى مالا نم له نص کے حکم کو ایسی فرع کی طرف متعدی کرنا جس میں نص وارد نہیں ہو تا۔ تاکہ اس میں بھی حکم ثابت کیا جائے یعنی جس فرع میں نص نہیں ہے اس میں غلبہ رائے سے حکم کو ثابت کرنا ۔ قطعیت کے ساتھ نہیں فالتغدية حكم لَأَزِمٌ عِنْدَنَا تو حکم کا تعدیہ کرنا ہمارے نزدیک ضروری امر ہے جس کے بغیر قیاس صحیح نہیں ہوتا اور تعلیل وجوب میں اس کے مساوی ہے۔ جَائِرٌ عِنْدَ الشافعى لأنه يَجُوزُ التَّعْلِيلُ بِالْعِلَّةِ الْقَاصِرَةِ كَالتَّعْلِيلِ بالثمنية في الذَّهَب وَالْفِضة لِحُرُمَةِ الرِّبوا فَإِنَّهَا لا تَتَعِدَى مِنْهَا فَالتَّعْلِيلُ عِنْدَهُ لِبَيَان لِمية الْحُكْمِ فَقَط وَلَا يَتَوَقَّفُ عَلَى التَّعْدِيَةِ لأَنْ َصحَةَ التَّعْدِيَةِ مَوْقُوقَةٌ عَلَى صِحَتِهَا فِي نَفْسِهَا فَلَوْ تَوَقَفْتُ صِحَتُهَا فِي نَفْسِهَا عَلى صِبحَةِ تَعْدِيَقِهَا لَزِمَ الدَّورُ وَالْجَواب أنَّ صِحَتِهَا فِي نَفْسِهَا لا تَتَوَقْف عَلَى صَحَةٍ تَعْدِيَتِهَا بَلْ عَلَى وُجُوْدِهَا فِي الفَرْعِ فَلا دَورَ وَالدَّلِيلُ لَنَا أَنْ دَلِيل الشرْعَ لأبُدْ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُوجِبًا لِلْعِلْم أَي الْعَمَلِ والتعليل لايفيد العلم قطعًا وَلَا يُفِيدُ العمل أيضا فى المنصوص عَلَيْهِ لأنه ثابت بالتمن فَلا فَائِدَةَ لَه إِلا تُبُوتُ الْحُكْمِ فِى الْفَرْعِ وَهُوَ مَعْنَى التَّعْدِيَةِ وَالتَّعْلِيلُ للأقسام الثَّلَثَةِ الأولِ وَنَقْيُها باطل أَن سَل شَرْطٍ أَوْ حُكْم ابْتِدَاءً بالرأي وَكَذَا نَفْيُهَا بَاطِلُ إِنْ لاَ اخْتِيَارَ وَلاَوِلايَةَ لَلْعَبْدِ فِيْهِ وَإِنَّمَا هُوَ إِلَى الشارع وَأَمَّا لَوْ ثُبَت سَبَبٌ أَوْ شَرْطُ أَوْ حُكْمٌ مِنْ نِص أَوْ إِجْمَاعِ وَأَرَدْنَا أَنْ تُعَدِيْهِ إِلَى مَحَلَّ آخَرَ فَلا شك أنْ ذَالِكَ فِي الحُكْمِ جَائِرُ بِالاِتِّفَاقِ إِذْلَهُ وَضِعَ الْقِيَاسُ وَأَمَّا فِي السَّبَبِ وَالشَّرْطِ فَلا يَجُوزُ عِنْدَ الْعَامَّةِ وَيَجُورُ عِنْدَ فخر الاسلام مَثَلاً إِذَا قِسْبُنَا اللَّوَامَةَ عَلى الزَّنَا في كَوْنِهِ سَيِّبًا لِلْحَدْ بِوَصَفٍ مُسْتَرَك بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ النّوَاطِةِ لِيُمْكِن جَعَل اللواطة أيضا سَبَبًا لِلْحَذَ يَجُوزُ عِنْدَهُ لأَعِنْدَهُمْ فَإِنْ كَانَ الْمُصَتَّفٌ تَابِعًا لِفَكْرِ الاسلام كَمَا هُوَ الظَّاهِرُ فَمَعْنَى كَوْنِهِ باطِلاً أنَّهُ بِاطِلُ إِبْتَدَاءً لَا تَعْدِيَةٌ وَإِلا فَالْمُرَادُ بِهِ الْبُطْلَانُ مُطْلَقًا اِبْتِدَاء وَتُعْدِيَةً. جَائِرٌ عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لأَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ التَّعْلِيلُ بالعِلْةِ الْقَاصرة - لیکن امام شافعی کے ترجمه و تشریح امزد یک تعدیہ بغیر بھی تعلیل جائز ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ وہ اصل کے ساتھ مخصوص علت سے تعلیل حکم جائز رکھتے ہیں جیسا کہ شمنیع کو علت قرار دیتا۔ سونے چاندی میں ریوا کے حرام ہونے کی کیونکہ یہ علت اصل کے علاوہ کسی اور فرع میں نہیں پائی جاتی۔ لہذا تعلیل ان کے نزدیک فقط حکم کی علت بیان کرنے کے لیئے کے بعد یہ کے صبح ہونے پر تیل کا میچ ہوتا ہے تعدیہ کے سی تقلیل کا صحیح موقوف نہیں ہے۔ اس وجہ سے تعدیہ کا صحیح ہونا بالاتفاق علت کے صحیح ہونے پر موقوف ہے۔ اگر علت کا صحیح ہونا
What has no text (nass) [is decided] by predominant opinion without certainty and conviction. So transference (ta'diya) in it is a necessary ruling according to us; qiyas is not valid without it, and ta'lil (causation) is equal to it in existence. And for the witnesses of marriage, 'adala (uprightness) and masculinity are conditions. This is an example of establishing a condition by description, because witnessing is a condition, and being upright and male are descriptions of the witness. It is not appropriate to use opinion-based qiyas here. Rather, we say that the absolute statement of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, "No marriage without witnesses," indicates that marriage is not contracted without witnesses, but does not indicate that 'adala is a condition nor masculinity. Imam al-Shafi'i makes them conditions because the Prophet ﷺ said, "No marriage except with a guardian and two upright witnesses." And since it is not a financial testimony, women's testimony is not acceptable. Therefore masculinity is a condition, as is the evidence of Imam al-Shafi'i, which we have already transmitted. And al-Bunayr (5): It is the diminutive of 'abtar, meaning a one-rak'ah prayer. This is an example of establishing a ruling. It is not appropriate to introduce opinion and qiyas into it. So we establish its non-legitimacy by the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ prohibiting al-batira'. Imam al-Shafi'i considers it permissible based on the hadith, 'When one of you fears the dawn, let him pray witr with one rak'ah.' And the description of witr (2): This is an example of establishing a ruling by description, because the ruling of witr prayer is established from Shari'ah, but whether it is sunnah or obligatory should not be established by opinion and qiyas. Because we have established the obligation of witr by hadith: 'Indeed Allah has added a prayer for you, which is witr.' (The meaning of mentioning addition to the five obligatory prayers is that this is also obligatory; otherwise, addition to the obligatory through sunnah is invalid. Imam al-Shafi'i says witr is sunnah. His evidence is the Prophet's statement, 'No prayer except the five, unless you wish to volunteer,' when an Arab asked if there were any other obligatory prayers besides the five.) And the fourth (4): The fourth purpose among the categories for which qiyas is performed, then for which inference is made. That is, transference of the ruling of the text to a branch for which there is no text, to establish the ruling in it. That is, to establish the ruling by predominant opinion in a branch for which there is no text, not with certainty. So ta'diya is a necessary ruling for us; qiyas is not valid without it, and ta'lil is equal to it in obligation. It is permissible according to al-Shafi'i because he allows causation with a restricted cause (al-illa al-qasira), like causation with the attribute of silver and gold for the prohibition of riba, for it does not transfer from them. So causation for him is only to explain the rationale of the ruling and does not depend on ta'diya, because the validity of ta'diya depends on its validity in itself. If its validity in itself depended on the validity of its ta'diya, circularity would result. The answer is that its validity in itself does not depend on the validity of its ta'diya, but on its existence in the branch, so no circularity. The evidence for us is that the legal proof must lead to knowledge, i.e., action. And causation does not produce certain knowledge, nor does it produce action concerning the text because it is established by the text, so it has no benefit except establishing the ruling in the branch, which is the meaning of ta'diya. And causation for the first three categories and their negation is invalid, because [negating] a condition or a ruling initially by opinion, and likewise negating them is invalid if there is no choice or authority for the servant in it; it is up to the Lawgiver. As for when a cause, condition, or ruling is established by text or consensus, and we want to transfer it to another locus, there is no doubt that this is permissible by agreement concerning the ruling, for it is for this that qiyas was established. As for cause and condition, it is not permissible according to the general scholars, but it is permissible according to Fakhr al-Islam, for example, if we compare sodomy to zina in being a cause for the hadd penalty by a shared attribute between it and zina, to make sodomy also a cause for hadd, then it is permissible according to him, not according to them. If the author follows Fakhr al-Islam, as appears, then the meaning of its being invalid is that it is invalid initially, not as ta'diya; otherwise, what is meant is absolute invalidity, both initial and transference. It is permissible according to al-Shafi'i because he allows causation with a restricted cause. But for Imam al-Shafi'i, in translation and commentary, causation is permissible without ta'diya. This is why he allows causation with a cause specific to the original, such as making the quality of silver and gold a cause for the prohibition of riba, because this cause is not found in any other branch besides the original. Therefore causation for him is only to explain the reason for the ruling, after which ta'diya is not required for the validity of causation. For this reason, the validity of ta'diya is unanimously dependent on the validity of the cause itself. If the cause is valid...
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, a Hanafi usul commentary, addresses a core methodological dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the nature of qiyas and the role of ta'diya (transference of ruling to new cases). The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: when there is no explicit text (nass), qiyas operates through predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y), not certainty. For qiyas to be valid, ta'diya is an essential requirement; without transferring the ruling from the original case (asl) to the new case (far'), the qiyas is unsound. Causation (ta'lil) must also be equal in existence, meaning the cause must be present in both. The author then provides examples. The first example concerns marriage witnesses. The Hanafi school holds that the hadith 'La nikaha illa bi shahid' (no marriage without witnesses) is general and absolute; it does not add conditions of uprightness ('adala) or masculinity (dhukura) for the witnesses. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, cites a different hadith requiring 'two upright witnesses' and also argues that since financial testimony requires masculinity, marriage testimony (which is not financial) might analogously require masculinity. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's words are taken as they are; adding conditions by qiyas is invalid in such matters because the ruling is established by explicit text, not by analogy. The second example is about the 'witr al-bunayr' (one-rak'ah witr). The Hanafis consider it prohibited (or disliked) based on a hadith prohibiting al-batira', while Shafi'i permits it based on another hadith allowing one-rak'ah witr when one fears dawn. The third example is the nature of witr prayer itself. Hanafis consider witr wajib (obligatory) based on the hadith 'Allah has added a prayer for you, which is the witr.' They argue that addition to the five obligatory prayers implies obligation. Shafi'is consider it sunnah, citing the hadith where the Prophet told an Arab that only five prayers are obligatory, and anything else is voluntary. The passage then returns to the general principle: ta'diya is necessary for qiyas. Shafi'i permits causation with a 'restricted cause' (al-illa al-qasira), i.e., a cause that only exists in the original case and does not transfer to new cases. For Shafi'i, the purpose of ta'lil is to explain the wisdom of the ruling, not necessarily to extend it. He argues that if ta'diya were required for the validity of the cause, it would lead to circularity (since ta'diya's validity depends on the cause's validity). The Hanafi refutation, attributed to Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, is that the cause's validity in itself depends on its existence in the branch (i.e., the cause must be present in the new case), not on ta'diya itself, so there is no circularity. The Hanafis argue that legal proofs must lead to action; if causation only explains the original ruling without extending it, it has no practical benefit. The passage concludes by distinguishing between transference of a ruling (which is agreed upon) and transference of a cause or condition (which is debated among Hanafis, with Fakhr al-Islam allowing it in some cases).

Key Terms
تعدية (ta'diyah): Transference of the ruling from the original case (asl) to a new case (far') via qiyas.
تعليل (ta'lil): Causation; identifying the effective cause ('illa) for a ruling.
العلة القاصرة (al-'illa al-qasira): A cause specific to the original case and not found elsewhere.
غلبة الرأي (ghalabah al-ra'y): Predominant opinion; the basis for rulings where no explicit text exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for qiyas to be valid?
A) The cause must be restricted to the original case.
B) The ruling must be transferred (ta'diya) from the original to the new case.
C) The original case must have an explicit text.
D) The new case must be identical to the original in all aspects.

Key Takeaway
For Hanafis, qiyas is valid only when the cause is transmissible; restriction of the cause to the original (Shafi'i view) is rejected because it yields no practical benefit.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
6 min
Ta'diyah in Qiyas: Hanafi Requirement and Shafi'i Dispute
Explains that ta'diyah is essential for qiyas, refutes Shafi'i position on 'illah qasirah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of ta'diyah in qiyas, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument based on 'illah qasirah, and apply the Hanafi rational proof to evaluate the dispute.

Core Idea
Without ta'diyah, qiyas produces neither knowledge nor action—ta'lil is futile.

This lesson unpacks a foundational usul dispute: must the effective cause ('illah) in qiyas be transitive (mut'addiyah) to be valid? The Hanafi school insists on ta'diyah; the Shafi'is permit ta'lil with a non-transitive 'illah (qasirah). We will trace the arguments, the Hanafi proof, and the practical consequences for deriving rulings in new cases.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the requirement: ta'diyah is necessary for the validity of qiyas; ta'lil with a qasirah 'illah is invalid.
The text says: 'فالتعدية حكم لازم عندنا' (transitivity is a necessary condition for us).
2
Present the Shafi'i view
Shafi'is allow ta'lil with a qasirah 'illah, as with thuminiyya for gold and silver. They argue ta'lil only explains wisdom (hikmah) and does not require ta'diyah.
3
Analyse the circularity argument
The Shafi'is claim that requiring ta'diyah for the validity of the 'illah leads to circularity (dawr).
They say: validity of ta'diyah depends on validity of 'illah, and if validity of 'illah depended on ta'diyah, it would be circular.
4
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal
Hanafis respond: the 'illah's validity in itself depends only on its existence in the branch (far'), not on its transitivity. Hence no circularity arises.
The text: 'أن صحتها في نفسها لا تتوقف على صحة تعديتها بل على وجودها في الفرع فلا دور.'
5
Apply the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof: a legal proof must produce knowledge or action. Ta'lil with a qasirah 'illah does neither—in the original, the ruling is already fixed by text; in the branch, no benefit exists without transitivity. Thus the only useful ta'lil is through ta'diyah.
This is the rational dalil cited in the text.

Source Text

نص وارد نہیں ہو تا۔ تاکہ اس میں بھی حکم ثابت کیا جائے یعنی جس فرع میں نص نہیں ہے اس میں غلبہ رائے سے حکم کو ثابت کرنا ۔ قطعیت کے ساتھ نہیں فالتعدية حكم لازم عندنا تو حکم کا تعدیہ کرنا ہمارے نزدیک ضروری امر ہے جس کے بغیر قیاس صحیح نہیں ہوتا اور تعلیل وجوب میں اس کے مساوی ہے۔ جائز عند الشافعي لأنه يجوز التعليل بالعلة القاصرة كالتعليل بالثمنية في الذهب والفضة لحرمة الربا فإنها لا تتعدى منها فالتعليل عنده لبيان لمية الحكم فقط ولا يتوقف على التعدية لأن صحة التعدية موقوفة على صحتها في نفسها فلو توقفت صحتها في نفسها على صحة تعديتها لزم الدور والجواب أن صحتها في نفسها لا تتوقف على صحة تعديتها بل على وجودها في الفرع فلا دور والدليل لنا أن دليل الشرع لابد أن يكون موجباً للعلم أو العمل والتعليل لا يفيد العلم قطعاً ولا يفيد العمل أيضاً في المنصوص عليه لأنه ثابت بالنص فلا فائدة له إلا ثبوت الحكم في الفرع وهو معنى التعدية والتعليل للأقسام الثلاثة الأول ونفيها باطل أن سل شرط أو حكم ابتداءً بالرأي وكذا نفيها باطل إن لا اختيار ولا ولاية للعبد فيه وإنما هو إلى الشارع وأما لو ثبت سبب أو شرط أو حكم من نص أو إجماع وأردنا أن نعديه إلى محل آخر فلا شك أن ذلك في الحكم جائز بالاتفاق إذ له وضع القياس وأما في السبب والشرط فلا يجوز عند العامة ويجوز عند فخر الإسلام مثلاً إذا قسنا اللواطة على الزنا في كونه سبباً للحد بوصف مشترك بينه وبين النواطة ليكن جعل اللواطة أيضاً سبباً للحد يجوز عنده لا عندهم فإن كان المصنف تابعاً لفخر الإسلام كما هو الظاهر فمعنى كونه باطلاً أنه باطل ابتداء لا تعدية وإلا فالمراد به البطلان مطلقاً ابتداء وتعدية. جائز عند الشافعي لأنه يجوز التعليل بالعلة القاصرة - لكن امام شافعی کے ترجمه و تشریح امزد یک تعدیہ بغیر بھی تعلیل جائز ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ وہ اصل کے ساتھ مخصوص علت سے تعلیل حکم جائز رکھتے ہیں جیسا کہ ثمنية کو علت قرار دیتا۔ سونے چاندی میں ریوا کے حرام ہونے کی کیونکہ یہ علت اصل کے علاوہ کسی اور فرع میں نہیں پائی جاتی۔ لہذا تعلیل ان کے نزدیک فقط حکم کی علت بیان کرنے کے لیے کے بعد یہ کے صبح ہونے پر تیل کا میچ ہوتا ہے تعدیہ کے سی تقلیل کا صحیح موقوف نہیں ہے۔ اس وجہ سے تعدیہ کا صحیح ہونا بالاتفاق علت کے صحیح ہونے پر موقوف ہے۔ اگر علت کا صحیح ہونا بھی تعدیہ کے صحیح ہونے پر موقوف ہو جائے تو دور لازم آئے گا۔ والجواب امام شافعی کے استدلال کا جواب ہماری طرف ہے یہ دیا جاتا ہے کہ تعدیہ کی صحت اگر چہ علت کی صحت پر موقوف ہے مگر فی نفسہ علت کی صحت تعدیہ کی صحت پر موقوف نہیں ہے لہذا دور نہیں لازم آئے گا۔ بلکہ تعلیل کا صحیح ہونا فرع میں علت کے وجود پر موقوف ہے۔ والدليل لنا۔ باقی رہی یہ بات کہ قیاس کی صحت کے لیے تعدیہ کی صحت لازم ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دلائل شرعیہ کے لیے مفید للعلم ہوتا یا مفيد للعمل ہونا ضروری ہے ورنہ لغو ہونا لازم آئے گا) اور یہ بات بھی یقینی ہے کہ اجتہاد سے استخراج کی ہوئی تعلیل علم یقین کا فائدہ بالکل نہیں دیتی۔ نیز جمل کا فائدہ منصوص علیہ میں نہیں دیتی کیونکہ حکم منصوص علیہ تو نص سے ثابت شدہ ہے۔ لہذا تعلیل سے کوئی فائدہ نہیں۔ بجز اس کے کہ اس کے ذریعہ اصل کا حکم فرع میں ثابت کیا جائے۔ اور تعدیہ کے یہی معنی ہیں۔ والتعليل للأقسام الثلاثة الأول ونفيها باطل على تین قسموں کو ثابت کرنے یا نفی کرنے کے لیے تعلیل باطل ہے۔ یعنی رائے سے یا قیاس سے ابتداء کسی سبب یا شرط یا حکم کو ثابت کرنا یا ابتداء رائے سے حکم ثابت کرنا ایسے ہی نفی کرنا باطل ہے کیونکہ ان امور کے اثبات یا نفی کا کوئی اختیار بندے کو حاصل نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ یہ شارع کی طرف راجع ہے۔ لیکن اگر کوئی سبب یا شرط حکم کسی نص سے ثابت ہو یا اجماع سے ثابت ہو اور ہم ارادہ کریں کہ ان امور میں سے کسی کو دوسرے محل کی طرف تعدیہ کریں تو حکم میں یہ تعدیہ بالاتفاق جائز ہے اس وجہ سے کہ قیاس اس کام کے لیے وضع کیا گیا ہے۔ اور بہر حال سبب یا شرط کے بارے میں تو ان دونوں میں تعدیہ عام علماء کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام فخر الاسلام کے نزدیک جائز ہے مثلاً ہم لواطت کو زنا پر قیاس کریں۔ اس بارے میں کہ لواطت میں حد جاری ہونے کا سبب ہے اس وصف کی وجہ سے جو اس (زنا) کے اور لواطت کے درمیان مشترک ہے تاکہ لواطت کو بھی حد سبب بنا دیا جائے۔ تو امام فخر الاسلام کے نزدیک یہ قیاس جائز ہے جمہور کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے لہذا اگر مصنف ماتن کے اس مسئلے میں امام فخر الاسلام کے متبع ہوں جیسا کہ بظاہر ایسا ہی معلوم ہوتا ہے تو باطل کے معنی ہوں گے۔ کہ ابتداء باطل ہے۔ تعدیہ کی صورت میں باطل نہیں ہے اور اگر مصنف امام فخر الاسلام کے تابع نہیں ہیں تو باطل سے مراد مطلق بطلان ہے۔ ابتداء ہو یا تعدیہ ہو۔ فلم يبق إلا الرابع يعني لم يبق من فوائد التعليل إلا التعدية إلى مالا نص فيه
If no text is present, to establish a ruling in it by predominant opinion, not definitively. So transitivity (ta'diyah) of the ruling is necessary according to us; without it qiyas is not valid, and ta'lil is equivalent to it in obligation. It is permissible according to al-Shafi'i because he allows ta'lil with a qasirah 'illah, like ta'lil with thuminiyya for gold and silver for the prohibition of riba, for it does not transit from them. For him, ta'lil is only to explain the wisdom of the ruling and does not depend on ta'diyah, because the validity of ta'diyah depends on the validity of the 'illah itself. If the validity of the 'illah itself depended on the validity of its ta'diyah, circularity would arise. The answer: the validity of the 'illah in itself does not depend on the validity of its ta'diyah, but on its existence in the branch, so no circularity. Our proof: a legal proof must be productive of knowledge or action, and ta'lil does not produce knowledge definitively, nor does it produce action in the mansus 'alayh because it is established by text, so it has no benefit except establishing the ruling in the branch, which is the meaning of ta'diyah. And ta'lil for the first three categories and their negation is invalid; establishing a condition or a ruling initially by opinion, and similarly its negation, is invalid because the servant has no choice or authority over them; they belong solely to the Lawgiver. As for when a cause, condition, or ruling is established from text or consensus and we intend to transit it to another locus, there is no doubt that this is permissible by consensus in the case of the ruling, for qiyas is established for this. As for the cause and condition, it is not permissible according to the generality, but it is permissible according to Fakhr al-Islam. For example, if we analogize liwat to zina as a cause for hadd by a common description between them to make liwat also a cause for hadd, it is permissible according to him, not according to them. If the author (matn writer) follows Fakhr al-Islam, as appears, then the meaning of it being invalid is that it is initially invalid, not transitively; otherwise, absolute nullity is intended, whether initial or transitive. It is permissible according to al-Shafi'i because he allows ta'lil with a qasirah 'illah. But the translation and commentary of Imam Shafi'i: ta'lil is permissible even without ta'diyah. That is why he permits ta'lil with an 'illah specific to the original, like making thuminiyya the 'illah for the prohibition of riba in gold and silver, because this 'illah is not found in any other branch besides the original. Therefore, for him, ta'lil is only to explain the wisdom of the ruling, and its validity does not depend on ta'diyah. The validity of ta'diyah is by consensus dependent on the validity of the 'illah. If the validity of the 'illah were also dependent on the validity of ta'diyah, circularity would follow. The answer to Imam Shafi'i's argument is that although the validity of ta'diyah depends on the validity of the 'illah, the validity of the 'illah in itself does not depend on the validity of ta'diyah; thus no circularity. Rather, the validity of ta'lil depends on the existence of the 'illah in the branch. Our proof: the remaining issue is that for the validity of qiyas, the validity of ta'diyah is necessary. Its proof is that legal proofs must be either productive of knowledge or productive of action; otherwise, they would be futile. It is also certain that ta'lil extracted by ijtihad does not produce certain knowledge, and it does not produce action in the mansus 'alayh because the ruling in the mansus 'alayh is already established by text. Therefore, ta'lil has no benefit except to establish the ruling of the original in the branch, and that is the meaning of ta'diyah. And ta'lil for the first three categories and their negation is invalid. That is, establishing or negating any cause, condition, or ruling initially by opinion or qiyas is invalid, as is initial negation, because the servant has no choice in these matters; they belong to the Lawgiver. But if a cause, condition, or ruling is established from text or consensus and we intend to transit it to another locus, then in the case of a ruling, this transitivity is permissible by consensus, because qiyas is established for this purpose. As for the cause or condition, transitivity is not permissible according to the majority; it is permissible according to Imam Fakhr al-Islam. For example, if we analogize liwat to zina concerning its being a cause for hadd by a common description between them to make liwat also a cause for hadd, it is permissible according to him, not according to them. Therefore, if the author of the matn follows Fakhr al-Islam, as appears, then the meaning of 'invalid' is that it is invalid initially, not by way of transitivity. Otherwise, the meaning is absolute nullity, whether initial or transitive. Thus, only the fourth remains, meaning only the benefit of ta'lil is transitivity to where there is no text.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar is a detailed usul dispute. It states the Hanafi position that ta'diyah (transitivity) of the 'illah is a necessary condition for the validity of qiyas. Without it, qiyas is invalid. The discussion then presents the Shafi'i view, which allows ta'lil with a qasirah (non-transitive) 'illah, citing the example of thuminiyya (price) as the 'illah for riba in gold and silver. The Shafi'i argument is that ta'lil is simply to explain the wisdom (hikmah) of the ruling and does not depend on transitivity. They further argue that requiring transitivity for the validity of the 'illah itself would lead to circularity. The Hanafi response refutes this: the validity of the 'illah in itself depends on its existence in the branch, not on its transitivity, so no circularity arises. The core Hanafi proof is that a legal proof must produce either knowledge or action. Ta'lil does not produce knowledge (since it is based on ijtihad), and in the original case the ruling is already established by text, so ta'lil there is useless. Its only benefit is to transfer the ruling to a branch case, which is precisely ta'diyah. The text then addresses whether ta'diyah applies to sabab (cause) and shart (condition) as well. It clarifies that establishing or negating a sabab, shart, or hukm initially by opinion is invalid because such matters belong solely to the Lawgiver. However, if a sabab, shart, or hukm is established from text or consensus, then transitivity is permissible for the hukm by consensus, but for sabab and shart it is not permissible according to the majority. A minority view from Fakhr al-Islam allows transitivity in sabab and shart as well, illustrated by the qiyas of liwat to zina to establish it as a cause for hadd. The passage concludes that only the fourth category of ta'lil remains beneficial: transitivity to a case where there is no text.

Key Terms
تعدية (ta'diyah): The property of the 'illah being transitive, i.e., applicable to branches beyond the original case.
علة قاصرة ('illah qasirah): A non-transitive cause, confined to the original case and not found in other branches.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, why is ta'lil with a qasirah 'illah invalid?
A) Because it leads to circularity.
B) Because it does not produce knowledge or action; in the mansus 'alayh the ruling is already fixed by text, so the only benefit is transitivity.
C) Because the 'illah must be derived from the text.
D) Because the Shafi'is forbid it.

Key Takeaway
For the Hanafis, ta'diyah is the essential benefit of ta'lil; without it, qiyas is legally futile.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Transference of Mutual Oaths Ruling to Heirs and Ijarah
Explaining the ta'diyah of the tahaluf ruling via qiyas khafi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scope of ta'diyah (transference) of the mutual oaths ruling (tahaluf) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, distinguishing the majority position from Imam Muhammad's, and apply the principle that exceptional rulings (ghayr ma'qul al-ma'na) are not extended by qiyas.

Core Idea
A ruling that contradicts rational analogy (qiyas) cannot be extended beyond its immediate context.

This passage examines whether the mutual oath rule (tahaluf) in sale contracts — a departure from normal qiyas — transfers to other contexts like heirs and ijarah. The Hanafis restrict it to situations before possession, except Imam Muhammad who generalises it. Understanding this ta'diyah is crucial for applying the usul principle that exceptional rulings are not extendable by qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling and its dalil
Locate the hadith that establishes mutual oaths when the commodity is still extant. Note that the rule applies before possession according to the majority.
Hadith: 'When the two transactors dispute and the commodity is still extant, they both take oaths and return the transaction.'
2
Recognise the ruling contradicts qiyas
Normal analogy (qiyas) would require only the buyer to swear since he denies the seller's claim. The hadith is an exception, making it 'ghayr ma'qul al-ma'na' (not rationally understood).
3
Determine the scope of ta'diyah pre-possession
The ruling transfers to heirs if both parties die before possession, and to ijarah before the lessee takes possession. This is to prevent harm.
Pre-possession: mutual oath applies.
4
Note the limit after possession
After possession, the ruling does not transfer because the hadith is an exception and cannot be extended. Only the buyer swears.
Post-possession: only buyer's oath.
5
Compare Imam Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad holds the hadith as general, applying it even after possession and to heirs/ ijara. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) restrict it.
Mufta bihi: majority view.

وَهَذَا حُكْمٌ أَنْ تُخَالَفَهُمَا جَمِيعًا مِنْ حَيْثُ الْقَيَاسِ الْخَفِي حُكْمٌ مَعْقُولُ يَتَعَدَّى إلَى الْوَارِثِينَ بأن مَاتَ البَائِعُ وَالْمُسْتَرِى جَمِيعًا وَاخْتَلَفَ وَارِثُهُمَا فِي الثَمَنَ قَبْلَ قَبْضِ الْمَبِيْعِ عَلى وَجْهِ الَّذِي قُلْنَا يَتَحَالِفَانِ وَيَفْسِحُ الْقَاضِي الْبَيْعَ كَمَا كَانَ هَذَا فِى الْمُوْرِثِينَ أوِ الْإِجَارَةِ أَنْ يَتَعَدُّى حُكْمُ البَيْعِ إِلى الإِجَارَةِ بأن اِخْتَلَف المُرْجِرُ وَالْمُسْتَاجِرُ فِي مِقْدَارِ الأُجْرَةٍ قَبْلَ قَيْضِ الْمُسْتَاجِرِ الدَّارَ يَتَحَالَفُ كُلِّ وَاحَدٍ مِنْهُمَا وَتَفْسِيَخُ الإِجَارَةُ لِدفْعِ الضَّرَرِ وَعَقْدُ الإِجَارَةِ يَحْتَمِلُ الْفَسَبْعَ فَأَمَّا بَعْدَ الْقَبْضِ فَلَمْ يَجِبْ يَمْنَ الْيَائِعِ إِلا بالأكرِ فَلَمْ تَصِحُ تَعْدِيَةٌ يَعْنِي إِذَا اخْتَلَفَ الْبَائِعُ وَالْمُسْتَرِى فِى مِقْدَارِ الثَّمَنِ بَعْدِ قَبْضِ الْمُسْتَرِئُ الْمَبَيْعَ فَحِينَئِذٍ كَانَ الْقَيَاسُ مَنْ كُلِّ الْوُجُوْهِ أَنْ يَحْلِفَ الْمُسْتَرِى فَقَط لَأَنَّهُ يُنْكِرُ زِيَادَةَ الثَّمَنِ الَّذِئ يَدْعِيْهِ البَائِعُ وَلَا يَدْعِي عَلَى الْبَائِعِ شَيْئًا لأَنَّ الْمَبِيْعَ سَالِمٌ فِي يَدِهِ وَلَكِنَّ الآثَرَ وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيهِ السلامُ إِذَا أُخْتَلَفَ الْمُتَبَايَعَانِ وَالسَّلْحَةُ قَائِمَةٌ بِعَيْنِهَا تَحَالَفَا وَتَرَادًا يَقْتَضِي وُجُوبَ التَّحَالُفِ عَلَى كُلِّ حَالٍ لأَنَّهُ مُطْلَقَ عَنْ قَبْضِ الْمَبِيْعِ وَعَدَمِهِ فَلَمَّا كَانَ هَذَا غَيْرُ مَعْقُول الْمَعْنَى فَلَا يَتَعَدَى إِلَى الْوَارِثِينَ إِذَا اخْتَلَفَا بَعْدَ مَوْتِ الْمُوْرِثِينَ إِلا عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ ولا إلى الْمُوْجِرِ وَالْمُسْتَاجِرِ إذا اخْتِلْفًا يَعْدَ اسْتِيفَاءِ الْمَعْقُومُ عَلَيهِ مَا عُرِفَ فِي الْفِقْهِ مُفَصَّلاً . وهذا حُكْمٌ اور محکم یعنی نم کورہ بالا مسئلہ میں بائع اور مشتری دونوں کو قسم کھانے کا حکم و ترجمه تشریح قاس نفی کی حیثیت سے (قیاس خفی کے تقاضہ سے ) ایک معقول حکم ہے یعنی معقل اور قیاس دونوں کے مطابق ہے۔ يَتَعَدّى إلى الوارثین ان کے وارثوں کے حق میں بھی متعدی ہوگا۔ بائیں صورت کہ بائع مشتری (ند کور ) دونوں مر جائیں اور دونوں کے ورثہ شمن کے بارے میں اختلاف کریں جب کہ ابھی تک طبیع پر قبضہ نہیں ہوا تھا۔ (جیسا کہ ہم اوپر بیان کر چکے ہیں) تو دونوں کے دری قسم کھا ئیں گے ۔ اور فیصلہ میں قاضی میچ کو فتح کر دے ( توڑ دے گا۔ جس طرح دونوں مورتوں کو بھی یہی حکم تھا۔ او الاجارة اور اجارہ کے معاملہ میں یعنی بیع کا حکم اجارہ کے معاملہ میں بھی متعدی ہو گا بائیں صورت کہ موجر (اجرت پر دینے والا مالک) اور مستاجر (اجرت اور کرایہ پر لینے والا یعنی کرایہ دار) دونوں مقدار اجرت میں اختلاف کریں۔ گھر پر متاجر کے قبضہ کرنے سے پیشتر (یعنی کرایہ دار نے ابھی تک اس گھر پر قبضہ نہیں کیا اور مقدار کرایہ میں اختلاف ہو گیا تو دونوں قسم کھائیں گے۔ اور اجارہ کا معاملہ ختم کر دیا جائے گا۔ نقصان کو رفع کرنے کی غرض سے اور عقد بیع کی طرح صبح کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ فأما بعد القبض فلم يَجِبْ يَمْنَ الْبَائِع - البتہ صحیح پر قبضہ کر لینے کے بعد بائع پر قسم واجب ہوتا محض حدیث سے ثابت ہے۔ اس لئے اس حکم کا تعدیہ نہیں ہو سکتا یعنی جب بائع اور مشتری میں مقدار من میں اختلاف مشتری کے طبع پر قبضہ کر لینے کے بعد واقع ہو۔ تو قیاس کا بالکلیہ تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ صرف مشتری ہی قسم کھائے گا کیونکہ مشتری اس زیادتی شمن کا منکر ہے جس کا بائع مدعی ہے اور مشتری کی طرف سے بائع پر کسی قسم کا کوئی دعوی نہیں ہے کیونکہ مشتری کے قبضہ میں صحیح صحیح سالم موجود ہے مگر چونکہ اثر (حدیث) اور وہ آنحضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا قول ہے کہ إِذَا خَتَلَفَ الْمُتَبَايُمَانِ وَالسِّلْعَةَ قَائِمَةٌ بَعَيْنَهَا تَحَالْفًا وَتُرَادًا ( جب بائع اور مشتری قیمت میں) ایک دوسرے سے اختلاف کریں اور سامان (صبیح) بعینہ (بلا تصرف) کے موجود ہے تو دونوں کے دونوں قسم کھائیں اور میچ کو واپس کر دیں یہ حدیث قسم کے وجوب کا تقاضہ دونوں کردیں سے کرتی ہے ہر حال میں۔ کیونکہ والسلعة قائمة کی شرط تعلق ہے جس سے طبیع پر قبضہ ہونے نہ ہونے دونوں صورتوں میں تحائف کا ( قسم کھانے کا) یہ حکم ہے۔ اور جب کہ یہ حکم قیاس اور عقل دونوں کے خلاف ہے۔ اس لئے بائع اور مشتری دونوں کے مرنے کے بعد اگر وارثین کے درمیان اس قسم کا اختلاف واقع ہو گا تو امام محمد کے علاوہ بقیہ دوسرے علماء احناف کے نزدیک قسم کھانے کا مذکورہ بالا حکم متعدی نہ ہو گا۔ اسی طرح موجد اور متاجر کے درمیان اگر مقدار اجرت پر اختلاف قبضہ کرنے کے بعد واقع ہو تو دونوں فریق پر تم کھانے کا حکم متعد کی نہ ہوگا۔ تفصیلات فقہ کی کتابوں میں ملاحظہ فرمائیے.
And this is a ruling that contradicts both of them entirely from the perspective of hidden analogy: a rational ruling that transfers to the heirs by way of: if the seller and buyer both died and their heirs disputed about the price before possession of the sold item in the manner we said, they both take oaths and the judge rescinds the sale just as this was [the case] for the deceased. Or in ijarah: that the ruling of sale transfers to ijarah by way of: if the lessor and lessee disputed about the amount of rent before the lessee takes possession of the house, each of them takes an oath and the ijarah is rescinded to repel harm, and the ijarah contract is susceptible to rescission. As for after possession, the seller's oath is not obligatory except by the hadith, so transference is not valid. That is: when the seller and buyer dispute about the amount of the price after the buyer has taken possession of the sold item, then the analogy from all aspects is that only the buyer takes an oath because he denies the increase in price that the seller claims and he does not claim anything against the seller because the sold item is intact in his hand. But the hadith — and it is his statement, peace be upon him: 'When the two transactors dispute and the commodity is still extant, they both take oaths and return the transaction' — necessitates the obligation of mutual oath in every case because it is absolute regarding possession and non-possession. Since this is not rationally understood, it does not transfer to the heirs if they dispute after the death of the deceased except according to Muhammad, nor to the lessor and lessee if they dispute after the completion of the benefit, as is known in fiqh in detail. And this is the ruling... [Urdu translation and commentary continues] ...For details, refer to the books of fiqh.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a ruling explaining the scope of the mutual oath rule (tahaluf) in sale contracts. The author states that when a dispute arises between buyer and seller regarding the price before the buyer has taken possession of the item, the mutual oath procedure applies — both parties swear oaths and the sale is rescinded. This ruling, derived from a hadith, contradicts the normal rational analogy (qiyas) which would require only the buyer to swear. The passage then discusses whether this ruling transfers (ta'diyah) to other situations. It transfers to heirs: if both parties die and their heirs dispute the price before possession, the same mutual oath applies. It also transfers to ijarah (lease) contracts: if the lessor and lessee dispute the rent before the lessee takes possession, mutual oath and rescission apply. However, after possession has been taken, the ruling does not transfer — neither to heirs nor to ijarah — because the hadith is not rationally extendable. The only exception is the view of Imam Muhammad, who extends it even after possession. The passage concludes by noting that the detailed fiqh rulings are found in the books of fiqh.

Key Terms
القياس الخفي (al-qiyas al-khafi): Hidden analogy: a reasoning method that is not obvious to the common understanding but is still legally valid.
التعدية (al-ta'diyah): Transference: applying a ruling from one case to another due to shared 'illah.
التحالف (al-tahāluf): Mutual oaths: both parties in a dispute swear oaths regarding the price when the commodity is still in hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, does the mutual oath ruling in a sale contract transfer to the heirs if both parties die and the dispute arises after the buyer had taken possession?
A) Yes, always.
B) No, it does not transfer because the hadith is rationally understood.
C) No, it does not transfer because the hadith is not rationally understood and cannot be extended.
D) Yes, but only according to Imam Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
The mutual oath ruling is an exception to qiyas and is restricted to disputes before possession; it does not transfer to post-possession, heirs, or ijarah after possession, except in Imam Muhammad's view.
