The Effective Cause and Its Immunity to Objections
Explaining the immunity of the effective cause and giving three examples from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a mu'aththira cause and explain why it is immune to fasad al-wad' and true munaqada, and apply the rule to given examples.

Core Idea
A cause proven by Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma cannot be refuted by contradiction or invalidity; only a stronger proof can oppose it.

In Hanafi usul, not all causes are equal. Some causes are so firmly grounded that they become immune to certain objections. This lesson explores the concept of al-‘illah al-mu’aththira—the effective cause—and the protection it enjoys from challenges like munaqada (contradiction) and fasad al-wad‘ (invalidity of position). Through examples from the Book, the Sunnah, and Ijma, you will see how the Hanafi school safeguards the authority of revelation and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key claim
The passage states that the effective cause is immune to munaqada and fasad al-wad' after its effect is shown by Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma. Note the condition 'after its effect is shown'.
2
Understand the rationale
The immunity derives from the sources themselves being immune. Quran, Sunnah, Ijma cannot be truly contradicted or invalidated.
3
Examine the examples
The passage gives three examples: from Quran (excretion from other than two passages), from Sunnah (leftover of domestic animals and cats), from Ijma (thief's hand not cut on third theft). For each, identify the cause and how its effect is shown.
4
Distinguish formal and real munaqada
The passage says munaqada applies in form but not in reality. Understand what that means: a counterexample may appear to contradict but does not truly refute because the cause is sound.
5
Apply the rule
Given a new scenario, determine if a cause is mu'aththira and what objections are permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْمُؤَثِّرَةُ فَلَيْسَ لِلسَّائِلِ فِيهَا بَعْدَ الْمُمَانَعَةِ إِلَّا الْمُعَارَضَةُ. فِيهِ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّهُ تَجْرِي فِيهَا الْمُمَانَعَةُ وَمَا قَبْلَهَا أَعْنِي الْقَوْلَ بِمُوجَبِ الْعِلَّةِ وَلَا يَجْرِي فِيهَا مَا بَعْدَ ذَا لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَحْتَمِلُ الْمُنَافَضَةَ وَفَسَادَ الْوَضْعِ بَعْدَ مَا ظَهَرَ أَثَرُهَا بِالْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ. لِأَنَّ هَؤُلَاءِ الثَّلَاثَةَ لَا تَحْتَمِلُ الْمُنَافَضَةَ وَفَسَادَ الْوَضْعِ فَكَذَا التَّأْثِيرُ الثَّابِتُ بِهَا. أَمَّا مِثَالُ مَا ظَهَرَ أَثَرُهُ بِالْكِتَابِ: مَا قُلْنَا فِي الْخَارِجِ مِنْ غَيْرِ السَّبِيلَيْنِ إِنَّهُ نَجِسٌ خَارِجٌ فَكَانَ حَدَثًا، فَإِنْ طُولِبْنَا بِبَيَانِ الْأَثَرِ قُلْنَا: ظَهَرَ تَأْثِيرُهُ مَرَّةً فِي السَّبِيلَيْنِ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى (أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِنْكُمْ مِنَ الْغَائِطِ). وَمِثَالُ مَا ظَهَرَ أَثَرُهُ بِالسُّنَّةِ: مَا قُلْنَا فِي سَوْرِ سَوَاكِنِ الْبُيُوتِ إِنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِنَجَسٍ فَيُقَاسُ عَلَيْهِ سَوْرُ الْهِرَّةِ بِعِلَّةِ الطَّوَافِ، فَإِنْ طُولِبْنَا بِبَيَانِ تَأْثِيرِهِ لَمَّا ثَبَتَ تَأْثِيرُهُ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ إِنَّهَا مِنَ الطَّوَافِينَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَالطَّوَافَاتِ. وَمِثَالُ مَا ظَهَرَ أَثَرُهُ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ: مَا قُلْنَا بِأَنَّهُ لَا تُقْطَعُ يَدُ السَّارِقِ فِي الْمَرَّةِ الثَّالِثَةِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ تَفْوِيتَ جِنْسِ الْمَنْفَعَةِ عَلَى الْكَمَالِ، فَإِنْ طُولِبْنَا بِبَيَانِ تَأْثِيرِهِ قُلْنَا: إِنَّ حَدَّ السَّرِقَةِ شُرِعَ لِحِفْظِ الْمَالِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ. ثُمَّ إِنْ فَسَادَ الْوَضْعِ لَا يَتَوَجَّهُ عَلَى الْعِلَّةِ الْمُؤَثِّرَةِ أَصْلًا، وَأَمَّا الْمُنَافَضَةُ فَإِنَّهَا تَتَوَجَّهُ عَلَيْهِ صُورَةً وَإِنْ لَمْ يَتَوَجَّهْ عَلَيْهَا حَقِيقَةً.
As for the effective cause, the questioner has after the objection [i.e., after it is established] nothing but opposition. It indicates that objection is applicable to it and what precedes it, i.e., the statement according to the requirement of the cause, but what comes after is not applicable because it does not admit contradiction and invalidation of position after its effect has been made evident by the Book, the Sunnah, and Consensus. Because these three do not admit contradiction and invalidation of position, similarly the effect established by them. As for an example of what its effect was made evident by the Book: what we said concerning the excretion from other than the two passages, that it is impure, an exit, so it is an event. If we are asked to demonstrate the effect, we say: its effect appeared once in the two passages by His statement (or one of you comes from the toilet). And an example of what its effect was made evident by the Sunnah: what we said concerning the leftover of the inhabitants of houses, that it is not impure, so by analogy the leftover of the cat is [judged] by the cause of circumambulation [i.e., frequent movement]. If we are asked to demonstrate its effect, its effect was established by his statement, peace be upon him: 'Indeed they are among those who go around you and go around.' And an example of what its effect was made evident by Consensus: what we said that the hand of the thief is not cut off on the third time because in it is the complete destruction of the type of benefit. If we are asked to demonstrate its effect, we say: the prescribed punishment for theft was legislated for the protection of property by consensus. Then indeed, invalidation of position does not apply to the effective cause at all. As for contradiction, it applies to it in form but not in reality.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage establishes a key usul principle: once a cause (illa) is proven to be mu'aththira (effective) by explicit text (Quran, Sunnah) or consensus (Ijma), it becomes immune to attacks of fasad al-wad' (invalidity of position) and true munaqada (contradiction). The only remaining objection is mu'arada (opposition via a stronger analogy). The reason is that these primary sources are themselves immune to these objections. The passage gives three examples: (1) From Quran: any excretion from non-private parts is impure and breaks wudu, proven by analogizing to the verse about coming from the toilet. (2) From Sunnah: the leftover of domestic animals is pure, analogized to the cat based on the hadith 'they are among those who go around you.' (3) From Ijma: the hand of a thief is not cut on the third theft because that would destroy the benefit of the hand entirely; the effect is shown by consensus that the hadd (punishment) is for property protection. The passage concludes that fasad al-wad' never applies to a mu'aththira cause, while munaqada may appear in form but cannot refute it in reality.

Key Terms
العلة المؤثرة (al-‘illah al-mu’aththirah): The effective cause whose impact on the ruling is established by clear evidence from Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma
المعـارضة (al-mu‘āraḍah): The only permissible objection against a mu'aththira cause, i.e., presenting a stronger opposite analogy or text
المنافضة (al-munāqaḍah): Contradiction, the claim that a cause leads to contradictory rulings
فساد الوضع (fasād al-waḍ‘): Invalidity of position, i.e., the cause is inherently flawed or leads to absurdity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the only valid objection that can be raised against an effective cause (mu'aththira) after it is established?
A) Fasad al-wad' (invalidity of position)
B) Munaqada (contradiction) in reality
C) Mu'arada (opposition via stronger proof)
D) None at all

Key Takeaway
A cause proven by Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma cannot be refuted by contradiction or invalidity; only a stronger proof can oppose it.

8 min
Immunity of the Effective Cause After Proof
Explaining immunity of effective cause after textual proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that an effective cause established by Quran, Sunna, or Ijma cannot be invalidated by naqdh or fasad al-wad', and identify the four methods to repel a seeming naqdh.

Core Idea
Once proven by primary sources, an effective cause is as immune as those sources.

This lesson from Ashraf al-Anwar delves into a core Hanafi usul principle: once an effective cause (al-illa al-mu'aththira) is proven to have an effect via Quran, Sunna, or Ijma, it becomes impervious to certain types of objections. The passage provides three concrete examples and explains the limited ways a seeming contradiction can be addressed.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the immunity principle
Understand that the primary sources (Quran, Sunna, Ijma) are immune to naqdh and fasad al-wad'. Therefore, any cause whose effect is proven by these sources shares that immunity.
This is a key defensive principle in Hanafi usul against weak objections.
2
Examine the Quranic example
The verse 'or one of you comes from the toilet' establishes that exiting from the two passages is a cause of hadath. By analogy, any impure exiting substance causes hadath. The effect is proven by the verse itself.
The cause 'impurity exiting' is established by the text mentioning a specific instance.
3
Examine the Sunna example
The Prophet's statement about cats being among those who go around establishes that their leftover (su'r) is pure, making the cause 'frequent movement in homes' effective.
The hadith provides the basis for the analogy.
4
Examine the Ijma example
Consensus that the hand is not cut in the third theft because it would destroy a whole type of benefit. The cause 'preservation of the type of benefit' is proven by Ijma.
This shows how Ijma can establish the effect of a cause.
5
Identify the four repelling methods
If a seeming naqdh (contradiction) appears, it must be repelled by one of four methods: by description (wasf), by meaning established by description (ma'na thabit bil-wasf), by ruling (hukm), or by objection ('arad).
The text clarifies that not every naqdh requires all four; the method depends on the case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا نَجَاسَةُ الْبَدَنِ فَإِزَالَةُ الْمَاءِ أَمْرٌ مَعْقُولٌ فَلَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى النِّيَّةِ بِخِلَافِ التُّرَابِ لِأَنَّهُ مُلَوَّثٌ فِي نَفْسِهِ غَيْرُ مُطَهِّرٍ بِطَبْعِهِ فَلِذَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى النِّيَّةِ. وَأَمَّا الْمُؤَثِّرَةُ فَلَيْسَ لِلسَّائِلِ فِيهَا بَعْدَ الْمُعَارَضَةِ إِلَّا الْمُعَارِضَةُ. فِيهِ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّهُ تَجْرِي فِيهَا الْمُعَارَضَةُ وَمَا قَبْلَهَا أَعْنِي الْقَوْلَ بِمُوجَبِ الْعِلَّةِ وَلَا يَجْرِي فِيهَا مَا بَعْدَهَا لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَحْتَمِلُ الْمُنَافَضَةَ وَلَا فَسَادَ الْوَضْعِ بَعْدَ مَا ظَهَرَ أَثَرُهَا بِالْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ. لِأَنَّ هَؤُلَاءِ الثَّلَاثَةَ لَا تَحْتَمِلُ الْمُنَافَضَةَ وَلَا فَسَادَ الْوَضْعِ، فَكَذَا التَّأْثِيرُ الثَّابِتُ بِهَا. أَمَّا مِثَالُ مَا ظَهَرَ أَثَرُهُ بِالْكِتَابِ: مَا قُلْنَا فِي الْخَارِجِ مِنْ غَيْرِ السَّبِيلَيْنِ إِنَّهُ نَجِسٌ خَارِجٌ فَكَانَ حَدَثًا، فَإِنْ طُولِبْنَا بِبَيَانِ الْأَثَرِ قُلْنَا ظَهَرَ تَأْثِيرُهُ مَرَّةً فِي السَّبِيلَيْنِ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: أَوْ جَاءَ أَحَدٌ مِنْكُمْ مِنَ الْغَائِطِ. وَمِثَالُ مَا ظَهَرَ أَثَرُهُ بِالسُّنَّةِ: مَا قُلْنَا فِي سُؤْرِ سَوَاكِنِ الْبُيُوتِ إِنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِنَجَسٍ فَقِيسَ عَلَى سُؤْرِ الْهِرَّةِ بِعِلَّةِ الطَّوَافِ، فَإِنْ طُولِبْنَا بِبَيَانِ تَأْثِيرِهِ لَمَّا ثَبَتَ تَأْثِيرُهُ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ: إِنَّهَا مِنَ الطَّوَّافِينَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَالطَّوَّافَاتِ. وَمِثَالُ مَا ظَهَرَ أَثَرُهُ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ: مَا قُلْنَا بِأَنَّهُ لَا تُقْطَعُ يَدُ السَّارِقِ فِي الْمَرَّةِ الثَّالِثَةِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ تَفْوِيتَ جِنْسِ الْمَنْفَعَةِ عَلَى الْكَمَالِ، فَإِنْ طُولِبْنَا بِبَيَانِ تَأْثِيرِهِ قُلْنَا إِنَّ حَدَّ السَّرَقَةِ شُرِعَ لِامْتِنَاعٍ لَا لِاتِّلَافٍ وَالْإِجْمَاعُ. ثُمَّ إِنَّ فَسَادَ الْوَضْعِ لَا يَتَّجِهُ عَلَى الْعِلَّةِ الْمُؤَثِّرَةِ أَصْلًا. وَأَمَّا الْمُنَافَضَةُ فَإِنَّهَا تَتَصَوَّرُ عَلَيْهِ صُورَةً وَإِنْ لَمْ يَتَّجِهْ عَلَيْهِ حَقِيقَةً. وَإِلَيْهِ أَشَارَ بِقَوْلِهِ: لَكِنَّهُ إِذَا تُصُوِّرَ مُنَافَضَةٌ يَجِبُ دَفْعُهَا بِطُرُقٍ أَرْبَعَةٍ. وَهِيَ: الدَّفْعُ بِالْوَصْفِ ثُمَّ بِالْمَعْنَى الثَّابِتِ بِالْوَصْفِ ثُمَّ بِالْحُكْمِ ثُمَّ بِالْعَرْضِ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي. وَلَيْسَ مَعْنَاهُ أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ دَفْعُ كُلِّ نَقْضٍ بِطَرِيقٍ أَرْبَعَةٍ بَلْ يَجِبُ دَفْعُ...
As for bodily impurity, removing it with water is a rational matter, so it does not require intention, unlike earth because it is impure in itself, not purifying by nature, thus it requires intention. As for the effective cause, the objector has after objection only counter-objection. In this is an indication that objection and what precedes it (meaning accepting the implication of the cause) are applicable to it, but what comes after is not applicable because it does not admit of contradiction or invalidity of position after its effect has been established by the Book, the Sunna, and consensus. Because these three do not admit of contradiction or invalidity of position, likewise the effect established by them. As for an example of what has its effect established by the Book: what we said about the exit from other than the two passages [urine and stool] that it is impure exiting, so it is an event; if we are asked for evidence of the effect, we say its effect appeared once in the two passages by His statement: 'or one of you comes from the toilet.' And an example of what has its effect established by the Sunna: what we said about the leftover of domestic animals that it is not impure, and analogy was made to the leftover of a cat due to the cause of frequent movement; if we are asked for evidence of its effect, its effect is established by his statement, peace be upon him: 'They are among those who go around you and go around.' And an example of what has its effect established by consensus: what we said that the hand of a thief is not cut in the third time because it would cause complete loss of the type of benefit; if we are asked for evidence of its effect, we say the punishment for theft was legislated for deterrence, not destruction, and consensus. Then invalidity of position does not attach to the effective cause at all. As for contradiction, it may appear on it in form though not in reality. And this is indicated by his statement: 'But if a contradiction is imagined, it must be repelled by four methods: repelling by description, then by the meaning established by description, then by the ruling, then by the objection as will come. It does not mean that every contradiction must be repelled by four methods; rather it must be repelled...'
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar, a commentary on Nur al-Anwar, discusses the concept of the 'effective cause' (al-illa al-mu'aththira) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It begins with a tangential point about purification: washing off impurity with water is rational, so no intention is needed, unlike tayammum with earth which requires intention because earth is not inherently purifying. Then it turns to the main topic: the effective cause. The text states that once the effect of a cause is established by Quran, Sunna, or Ijma, the cause is immune to objections of naqdh (contradiction) or fasad al-wad' (invalidity of position), because the primary sources themselves are immune to such defects. Three examples are given: 1) For Quran: the exit of impurity from other than the two passages (like urine/stool) causes hadath because it is impure and exiting; its effect is proven by analogy to the Quranic verse mentioning coming from the toilet. 2) For Sunna: the leftover (su'r) of domestic animals (like cats) is pure, established by the Prophet's statement that they are among those who go around, implying they are not unclean. 3) For Ijma: a thief's hand is not cut in the third theft, because that would destroy the entire type of benefit (e.g., using hands for eating), and this ruling is based on consensus that the punishment is for deterrence, not mutilation. After effect is established, fasad al-wad' cannot be alleged against the cause at all. Naqdh may appear in form but not reality; if it does, it must be repelled by four methods: daf' bil-wasf (by description), daf' bil-ma'na al-thabt bil-wasf (by meaning established by description), daf' bil-hukm (by ruling), and daf' bil-'arad (by objection). These will be explained later. The text clarifies that not every contradiction requires all four methods; the method varies.

Key Terms
العلة المؤثرة (al-illa al-mu'aththira): An effective cause that has a proven effect (ta'thir) on a ruling, established by Quran, Sunna, or Ijma, and immune to invalidation.
المنافضة (al-munafada): A contradiction (naqdh) appearing against the cause, which must be repelled if it arises.
فساد الوضع (fasad al-wad'): Invalidity of position; an objection that the cause is improperly constructed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the hand of a thief not get cut in the third theft?
A) Because the third theft is not proven by witnesses
B) Because cutting the hand would completely destroy a type of benefit
C) Because the thief has already been punished twice
D) Because the Prophet forbade cutting in the third theft

Key Takeaway
An effective cause proven by Quran, Sunna, or Ijma is immune to naqdh and fasad al-wad', just as the primary sources are.

Defending an Effective Cause (al-'Illah al-Mu'aththirah) Against Naqd
Explains four methods to defend a mu'aththirah cause from naqd, with a Hanafi fiqh example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four methods of defending a mu'aththirah cause against naqd and apply them to the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on wudu breaking by non-flowing blood.

Core Idea
An effective cause established by text can be defended from inconsistency by denying the description, its meaning, the ruling, or dismissing the objection as a side issue.

After a cause ('illah) is established as mu'aththirah through explicit textual evidence (Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma'), it becomes immune to certain objections but can still face naqd (inconsistency objections) where a case exists with the cause but without the ruling. The Hanafi usul tradition provides four defense methods (dafʿ) against such naqd. This lesson explores these methods through the classical example of whether blood from a wound breaks wudu, illustrating the Hanafi position against a Shafi'i objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the effective cause ('illah)
In the example, the cause for breaking wudu is the exit of impurity (khurūj al-najis) from the body, analogous to urine. This cause is established through istiqrā' (induction) of texts.
The 'illah mu'aththirah is derived from textual evidence, not mere reasoning.
2
Understand the naqd (objection)
The Shafi'i objection is that non-flowing blood is impure (najis) and exits but does not break wudu, contradicting the Hanafi claim that any impure exit breaks wudu.
The objection points to a case where the 'illah seems present but the ruling is absent.
3
Apply the first defense: dafʿ bi al-waṣf
Deny that the description (waṣf) of 'exit' actually exists in the objection case. Non-flowing blood does not truly exit; it merely appears under the skin and does not transfer.
This defense attacks the existence of the assumed 'illah element.
4
Apply the second defense: dafʿ bi al-maʿnā al-thābitu bi al-waṣf
Even if the description existed, deny that the meaning (maʿnā) established by that description—obligation to wash the spot—is present. For non-flowing blood, washing the spot is not obligatory, so the consequential ruling (hadath) does not follow.
This defense attacks the legal effect that would normally follow from the description.
5
Recognize the flexibility of the four methods
The text clarifies that not all four methods must be used for every naqd; different objections may require different combinations. The total number of methods across all defenses is four.
Avoid the common misunderstanding that all four methods are mandatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأنها لا تحتمل المناقضة ولا فساد الوضع. وهِيَ الدَّفْعُ بِالْوَصفِ ثُمَّ بِالْمَعْنى الثَّابِتِ بِالْوَصْفِ ثُمَّ بِالْحُكُم ثُمَّ بِالعَرَضِ على مَايَاتِي وَلَيْسَ مَعْنَاهُ أنه يجبُ دَفْعُ كُلَّ نَقْضَ بِطَرِق أَرْبَعَة بَلْ يَجِبُ دَفْعُ بَعْضَ النُّقُوْضِ بِبَعْضَ الطَّرْقِ وَبَعْضُهَا بِبَعْضٍ آخَرَ مِنْهَا وَالْمَجْمُوعُ يَبلُغَ أَرْبَعَةً فالتعليل بالعِلةِ المُوثَرَةِ وَإِبْرَادُ النَّقْضِ الصُّورِئ عَلَيْهَا وَدَفْعُهُ كَمَا تَقُولُ فِي الخارج مِنْ غَيْرِ السَّبِيلَيْنِ إِنَّهُ نَجسَ خَارِجُ فَكَانَ حَدَثًا كَالْيَوْلِ فَيُوْرَدُ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ عَلى هَذَا التَّعْلِيْلَ بِالنُّقْضِ مِن جَانِبِ السَّافَعِى مَا إِذَا لَمْ يَسَبِلْ فَإِنَّهُ نَجِس خَارِج وَلَيْسَ بِحَدَثٍ فَنَدْفَعَهُ أَوْلاً بِالْوَصْفِ أَى نَدْفَعُ هَدَ النَّقْضَ بِالطَّرِيقَيْنِ الأَولُ بِعَدَمِ الْوَصْفِ وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِخَارِج بِلْ بِادٍ لإِنْ تَحْتَ كُلِّ جَلْدَةٍ دَمًا فَإِذَا زالت أجندة ظهر الدَّمُ فِي مَكَانِهِ وَلَمْ يَخْرُجُ وَلَمْ يَنْتَقِلْ فِى مَوْضع الى موضع يخِلافِ الدَّم السائِلِ فَإِنَّهُ كَانَ فِي الْعُروقِ وَانْتَقَلَ الى فَوقَ الجِلْدِ وَخَرَج مِنْ موضعه ثُمَّ بِالمَعْنى الثَّابِتِ بِالْوَصفِ دَلَالَةَ أنْ كُمْ نَدْفَعَهُ ثَانِيَا بِعَدَمِ الْمَعْنى الثابت بالوصف وَنَقُولُ لَوْ سَلْمُ أَنَّهُ وُجِدَ وَصَفُ الحُرُوج لكِنَّهُ لَمْ يَوْجِدِ الْمَعْنى الثابت بالخروج دَلالَةٌ وَهُوَ وَجُوْبُ غَسَل ذَالِكَ الْمَوْضِعِ فَإِنَّهُ يَجِبُ أَوْلاً غَسْلُ ذالك الموضع ثُمَّ يجبُ غُسْلُ الْبَدَنِ كُلِّهِ وَلِكُنْ نَقْتَصِرُ عَلَى الأَرْبَعَةِ دَفْعًا للحرج فِيْهِ أَى بِسَبَبِ وَجُوْبٍ غَسْلِ ذَالِكَ الْمَوْضِعِ صَارَ الوَصف حُجةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ أن وُجُوبَ التَّطبيبِ فِي البَدَنِ بِاعْتِبَارِ مَا يَكُونَ مِنْهُ لايَا فَلَمَّا وَجَبَ غَسْلُ ذالك الْمَوْضِعِ وَجَبَ غَسْلُ سَائِرِ البَدَنِ البَتْه وهناك لم يَجِبُ غَسْلُ ذَالِكَ الْمَوْضِعِ فَاِنْ عَدَمُ الْحُكْمُ لِعَدَمِ الْعِلْةِ كَأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُوْجَدِ الحُرُوجُ.
Because it does not admit of contradiction nor invalidity of position. And these are: defense by the description, then by the meaning established by the description, then by the ruling, then by presentation, as will come. And it does not mean that it is necessary to defend every rejection by four methods; rather, it is necessary to defend some rejections by some methods and others by other methods, and the total reaches four. So reasoning with the effective cause, and presenting a formal rejection against it, and defending it, as you say regarding discharge from other than the two passages: it is an impure discharge, so it is an event like urine. Then it is objected to that, according to this reasoning, by rejection from the side of the Shafi'i: when it does not flow, for it is an impure discharge and is not an event. So we defend it first by the description, i.e., we defend this rejection by two ways: first by the absence of the description, and that is that it is not a discharge but rather a [blood] welling up, because under every skin there is blood; when the skin is removed, the blood appears in its place and does not exit and does not transfer from place to place, unlike flowing blood, for it was in the veins and transferred to above the skin and exited from its place. Then by the meaning established by the description as evidence: we defend it secondly by the absence of the meaning established by the description, and we say: even if we grant that the description of exit existed, the meaning established by exit as evidence did not exist, and it is the obligation to wash that place, for it is obligatory first to wash that place, then it becomes obligatory to wash the whole body. But we limit ourselves to four methods to avoid hardship in it, i.e., due to the obligation to wash that place, the description became a proof from the aspect that the obligation of purification of the body is by consideration of what comes from it? So when washing that place became obligatory, washing the rest of the body became necessarily obligatory, but there (in the objection) washing that place is not obligatory, so the absence of the ruling is due to the absence of the cause, as if the exit did not occur.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule explaining how to defend an effective cause ('illah mu'aththirah) from objections of inconsistency (naqd). The author first states that after an 'illah's effectiveness is established through Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma', it cannot be attacked by claims of inherent contradiction (munāqaḍah) or invalidity of position (fasād al-waḍʿ). Then he lists four methods of defense against a naqd: (1) dafʿ bi al-waṣf — denying that the description (waṣf) exists in the objection case; (2) dafʿ bi al-maʿnā al-thābitu bi al-waṣf — denying the meaning (maʿnā) that is established by that description; (3) dafʿ bi al-ḥukm — denying the ruling (ḥukm) that would follow; (4) dafʿ bi al-ʿaraḍ — presenting the objection as a side issue (ʿaraḍ). However, he clarifies that not all four methods must be used for every naqd; rather, any one method suffices, and the total number of methods across all defenses is four. He then provides a concrete example from Hanafi fiqh: the issue of najis (impure) discharge from other than the two passages (i.e., not from the front or rear) being a hadath (ritual impurity that breaks wudu). The Hanafi analogy is: such discharge is impure and exits the body, so it breaks wudu like urine. A Shafi'i objection is raised: if blood exits from a wound but does not flow (lam yasil), it is impure but does not break wudu according to them. The Hanafi defense uses the first two methods: first, by denying the description of exit (waṣf al-khurūj) — arguing that when blood does not flow, it is merely appearing under the skin, not truly exiting. Second, by denying the meaning (maʿnā) that is established by exit, namely the obligation to wash that spot. In flowing blood, washing the spot is obligatory and then the whole body must be washed, but for non-flowing blood, washing the spot is not obligatory, so the ruling of hadath does not follow. The author notes that the Hanafis limit themselves to four methods to avoid hardship, not to exhaust all possible defenses.

Key Terms
العلة المؤثرة (al-'illah al-mu'aththirah): An effective cause that is proven to be the effective cause by textual evidence (Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma') such that it cannot be subject to reasonable objection.
النقض (al-naqd): An objection raised against the causal relationship by pointing to a case where the 'illah exists but the ruling does not (or vice versa), aiming to show inconsistency.
دفع بالوصف (dafʿ bi al-waṣf): First method of defense against naqd: denying that the description (waṣf) that constitutes the 'illah is actually present in the objection case.
دفع بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف (dafʿ bi al-maʿnā al-thābitu bi al-waṣf): Second method: denying that the meaning (maʿnā) established by the description (e.g., obligation to wash the spot) is present in the objection case.
دفع بالحكم (dafʿ bi al-ḥukm): Third method: the ruling that would follow from the 'illah (e.g., hadath) is denied to exist in the objection case due to a legal impediment (not elaborated in this passage).
دفع بالعرض (dafʿ bi al-ʿaraḍ): Fourth method: presenting the objection as a side issue (ʿaraḍ) that does not affect the core analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true regarding the defense of a mu'aththirah cause against naqd?
A) The defender must use all four methods (al-waṣf, al-maʿnā, al-ḥukm, al-ʿaraḍ) for every objection.
B) The defender may use any combination, but the total number of methods across all defenses is four.
C) Only the first two methods (al-waṣf and al-maʿnā) are valid for defending a mu'aththirah cause.
D) The defense is only valid if the opposition's argument is first proven to be a formal rejection (naqd ṣūrī).

Key Takeaway
An effective cause established by text can be defended against naqd by any of four methods, not necessarily all at once, and the selection depends on the specifics of the objection.

Refuting a Naqd: Denying the Characteristic or Its Meaning
Explains two methods to refute a counterexample in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the two Hanafi methods of refuting a counterexample (naqd)—daf' bil-wasf and daf' bil-ma'na al-thabit bil-wasf—to defend a legal analogy.

Core Idea
A counterexample is refuted by showing its characteristic is absent or its legal meaning does not follow.

In Hanafi usul, when a muqallid (legal analogy) is challenged by a counterexample (naqd), the scholar can defend it by either denying that the claimed characteristic (wasf) is truly present, or denying that the legal meaning (ma'na) that should arise from that characteristic actually applies. This lesson explains these two methods using the classic example of an impure substance exiting the body from other than the two passages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original qiyas and the counterexample
The Hanafi argues that any impure exit from the body, like urine, nullifies wudu (hadath). The Shafi'i objects with the case of blood that appears under the skin but does not flow—it is impure and exits yet does not nullify wudu.
2
Apply daf' bil-wasf: deny the characteristic
Show that in the counterexample, the characteristic of 'exit' is not truly present; the blood only appears (zuhur) but does not transfer from one location to another. Therefore, the alleged cause is absent, breaking the analogy.
Exit requires movement from its place.
3
Apply daf' bil-ma'na al-thabit bil-wasf: deny the legal meaning
Even if we accept the characteristic of exit, the legal meaning that normally follows—obligation to wash the spot—does not apply in this case, because the blood did not flow to a new site. Without that obligation, the entire body washing (i.e., wudu nullification) does not follow.
The ruling is absent due to absence of the cause.
4
Recognize that only one method is needed
The author clarifies that a counterexample can be refuted by any one of the four methods; the example demonstrates two for illustration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَعْضَ النُّقُوْضِ بِبَعْضَ الطَّرْقِ وَبَعْضُهَا بِبَعْضٍ آخَرَ مِنْهَا وَالْمَجْمُوعُ يَبلُغَ أَرْبَعَةً فالتعليل بالعِلةِ المُوثَرَةِ وَإِبْرَادُ النَّقْضِ الصُّورِئ عَلَيْهَا وَدَفْعُهُ كَمَا تَقُولُ فِي الخارج مِنْ غَيْرِ السَّبِيلَيْنِ إِنَّهُ نَجسَ خَارِجُ فَكَانَ حَدَثًا كَالْيَوْلِ فَيُوْرَدُ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ عَلى هَذَا التَّعْلِيْلَ بِالنُّقْضِ مِن جَانِبِ السَّافَعِى مَا إِذَا لَمْ يَسِبَلْ فَإِنَّهُ نَجِس خَارِج وَلَيْسَ بِحَدَثٍ فَنَدْفَعَهُ أَوْلاً بِالْوَصْفِ أَى نَدْفَعُ هَدَ النَّقْضَ بِالطَّرِيقَيْنِ الأَولُ بِعَدَمِ الْوَصْفِ وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِخَارِج بِلْ بِادٍ لإِنْ تَحْتَ كُلِّ جَلْدَةٍ دَمًا فَإِذَا زالت أجندة ظهر الدَّمُ فِي مَكَانِهِ وَلَمْ يَخْرُجُ وَلَمْ يَنْتَقِلْ فِى مَوْضع الى موضع يخِلافِ الدَّم السائِلِ فَإِنَّهُ كَانَ فِي الْعُروقِ وَانْتَقَلَ الى فَوْقَ الجِلْدِ وَخَرَج مِنْ موضعه ثُمَّ بِالمَعْنى الثَّابِتِ بِالْوَصفِ دَلَالَةَ أنْ كُمْ نَدْفَعَهُ ثَانِيَا بِعَدَمِ الْمَعْنى الثابت بالوصف وَنَقُولُ لَوْ سَلْمُ أَنَّهُ وُجِدَ وَصَفُ الحُرُوج لكِنَّهُ لَمْ يَوْجِدِ الْمَعْنى الثابت بالخروج دَلالَةٌ وَهُوَ وَجُوْبُ غَسَل ذَالِكَ الْمَوْضِعِ فَإِنَّهُ يَجِبُ أَوْلاً غَسْلُ ذالك الموضع ثُمَّ يجبُ غُسْلُ الْبَدَنِ كُلِّهِ وَلِكُنْ نَقْتَصِرُ عَلَى الأَرْبَعَةِ دَفْعًا للحرج فِيْهِ أَى بِسَبَبِ وَجُوْبٍ غَسْلِ ذَالِكَ الْمَوْضِعِ صَارَ الوَصف حُجةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ أن وُجُوبَ التَّطبِيرِ فِي البَدَنِ بِاعْتِبَارِ مَا يَكُونَ مِنْهُ لايَا فَلَمَّا وَجَبَ غَسْلُ ذالك الْمَوْضِعِ وَجَبَ غَسْلُ سَائِرِ البَدَنِ البَتْه وهناك لم يَجِبُ غَسْلُ ذَالِكَ الْمَوْضِعِ فَاِنْ عَدَمُ الْحُكْمُ لِعَدَمِ الْعِلْةِ كَأَنَّهُ لَمْ يُوْجَدِ الحُرُوجُ. وَفِي الدَّفْعُ بِالْوَصفِ الخ ۔ اور وہ چاروں طریقے یہ ہیں (۱) دفع بالوصف (۲) وضع بالمعنی الثابت بالوصف (۳) دفع بالحکم (۳) دفع بالعرض۔ جیسا کہ تفصیلات منقریب آجائیں گی مصنف وقع ماتن کا مقصد ان چاروں طریقوں سے یہ نہیں ہے کہ ان پر نقض کو ان چاروں طریقوں سے دفع کرنا ضروری ہے بلکہ مراد یہ ہے کہ نقض کو ان چاروں دفعات میں سے کسی ایک سے دفع کیا جائے گا۔ یعنی بعض نقض کو بعض سے اور بعض دوسرے نقض کو ان میں سے بعض دوسرے واقع سے دفع کیا جانا چاہئے البتہ مدافعت کے طریقوں کی مجموعی تعداد چار تک پہونچ جاتی ہے پس علقہ موثرہ سے استدلال اور صور تا اس پر نقض وارد ہونے پھر اس نقض کو دفع کرنے کی تفصیلی مثال ملاحظہ کیجئے۔ جیسا کہ تَقُولُ خَارِجُ مِنْ غَيْرِ السَّبِيْنَيْنِ تم کہو نجس خارج من غیر سبیلین میں چونکہ خروج نجاست کی علت پائی جارہی ہے اس لیے وہ ناقض وضو ہے جس طرح خروج بول ناقض ، ضو ہے تو اس پر اعتراض وارد ہو سکتا ہے۔ یعنی اس تعلیل پر شوافع کی طرف نقض وارد ہو سکتا ہے۔ ما إذا لَمْ يَسلُ اس صورت میں جبکہ نجاست (پیشاب) نکل کر بدن میں نہ بہے
Some counterexamples [are refuted] by some methods, and others by other methods among them, and the total reaches four. So [the correct method is] reasoning with an effective cause, and presenting a formal counterexample against it, and refuting it, as you say regarding what exits from other than the two passages: it is an impure thing that exits, so it is an event (hadath) like urine. Then a counterexample is brought against this reasoning from the side of the Shafi'i: when it does not flow, for it is an impure thing that exits but is not an event. We refute it firstly by the characteristic – i.e., we refute this counterexample by two methods: the first by the absence of the characteristic, which is that it is not an exit but rather an appearance, because under every skin there is blood. When the skin is removed, the blood appears in its place and does not exit and does not transfer from one place to another, unlike flowing blood, for it was in the veins and transferred to above the skin and exited from its place. Then by the meaning established by the characteristic by indication: we refute it secondly by the absence of the meaning established by the characteristic, and we say: even if we concede that the characteristic of exiting exists, yet the meaning established by exiting by indication does not exist, and that is the obligation to wash that spot. For first it is obligatory to wash that spot, then it is obligatory to wash the entire body, but we suffice with the four limbs to remove hardship therein. That is, because of the obligation to wash that spot, the characteristic became a proof, because the obligation of purification in the body is indivisible. So when washing that spot became obligatory, washing the rest of the body became absolutely obligatory. And there (in that case) washing that spot is not obligatory, so the ruling is absent due to the absence of the cause, as if the exit did not occur. And regarding the refutation by the characteristic etc.: [Urdu] And these four methods are: (1) daf' bil-wasf, (2) daf' bil-ma'na al-thabit bil-wasf, (3) daf' bil-hukm, (4) daf' bil-'arad. As the details will come shortly. The author's intention is not that it is necessary to refute the counterexample by all four methods; rather, the meaning is that the counterexample will be refuted by any one of these four methods. That is, some counterexamples are refuted by some methods, and others by other methods among them. However, the total number of methods of refutation reaches four. So consider the detailed example of reasoning with an effective cause, then a formal counterexample being raised against it, then refuting that counterexample. As when you say: an impure thing exiting from other than the two passages – because the cause of the exit of impurity is present, it nullifies wudu just as the exit of urine nullifies wudu. On this reasoning, a counterexample can be raised from the Shafi'i side: the case when it does not flow – an impure thing exits but is not an event.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a methodological explanation of how to refute a counterexample (naqd) in qiyas. The author states that there are four methods of refutation, and then illustrates the first two using the example of an impure substance exiting the body from other than the two passages. The Hanafi position is that any such exit nullifies wudu because the effective cause (illa) is the exit of impurity, as in urine. The Shafi'i raises a counterexample: if the impurity (e.g., blood) does not flow but merely appears under the skin, it is still an impure exit, yet it does not nullify wudu. The Hanafi responds by two methods. First, by denying the characteristic (daf' bil-wasf): he argues that what occurred is not true 'exit' (khuruj) but mere 'appearance' (zuhur), because the blood was under the skin and did not transfer to a new place; it only became visible when the outer skin was removed. Second, by denying the meaning established by the characteristic (daf' bil-ma'na al-thabit bil-wasf): even if we accept that there was exit, the legal meaning derived from exit—namely, the obligation to wash the spot where the impurity touched—does not apply here, because in this case there is no obligation to wash that spot (since the blood did not flow to a new location). Without that obligation, the necessity of washing the entire body (which is inferred from the obligation to wash the spot) does not arise, so the nullification of wudu does not occur. The author clarifies that only one method is needed per counterexample; the example demonstrates two possible methods.

Key Terms
نقض (naqd): A counterexample raised against a qiyas to show that the claimed cause (illa) does not consistently produce the ruling.
دفع بالوصف (daf' bil-wasf): Refutation by denying that the characteristic (wasf) which constitutes the cause is present in the counterexample.
دفع بالمعنى الثابت بالوصف (daf' bil-ma'na al-thabit bil-wasf): Refutation by denying that the legal meaning (hukm or effect) established by the characteristic applies in the counterexample.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi method of refuting a naqd (counterexample), which of the following is one of the two methods demonstrated in the passage?
A) Daf' bil-hukm (refutation by the ruling)
B) Daf' bil-wasf (refutation by the characteristic)
C) Daf' bil-'arad (refutation by accident)
D) Daf' bil-ijma' (refutation by consensus)

Key Takeaway
A counterexample to qiyas can be refuted by denying either the presence of the cause (wasf) or its legal implication (ma'na), and only one method suffices.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Two Types of Qalb and How to Nullify Them
Explaining two types of qalb and how to avoid qalb harm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qalb that harms ta'lil and harmless inversion in istidlal, and apply the Hanafi qalb al-wasf technique to counter the Shafi'i argument on Ramadan intention.

Core Idea
Qalb inverts evidence; using istidlal instead of ta'lil makes qalb harmless; qalb al-wasf turns opponent's proof against him.

In Hanafi usul, qalb (inversion) is a dialectical tool that can dismantle an opponent's argument if it is based on ta'lil (causal reasoning). However, if the argument is framed as istidlal (mutual evidence), qalb loses its force. This lesson unpacks two types of qalb and illustrates them with a classic Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over the necessity of intention for the Ramadan fast. You will learn how the Hanafis inverted the Shafi'i causal link to support their own position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of qalb
From the passage, distinguish between (1) qalb that attacks ta'lil and (2) qalb al-wasf (inversion of description) where the opponent's own evidence becomes proof against him.
The first type is harmless if the argument is presented as istidlal; the second is a deliberate counter-argument.
2
Understand why ta'lil is vulnerable to qalb
In ta'lil, there is a one-way cause-effect relationship. The opponent can invert this by claiming the opposite relationship. In istidlal, the relationship is mutual, so inversion does not harm.
This is a key distinction in Hanafi munazara (dialectics).
3
Analyze the qalb al-wasf example: Ramadan intention
The Shafi'is use ta'lil: obligation requires specification of intention (analogy to make-up fasts). The Hanafis invert this by making obligation a proof that no specification is needed, because Ramadan is already specified by the Lawgiver (hadith).
The Hanafi response uses istidlal: the hadith itself specifies the time, so no additional intention is required.
4
Compare the two schools' reasoning
Identify the Shafi'i illa (obligation → need for intention) and the Hanafi counter-argument (obligation → no need for intention due to prior specification). Note the use of the hadith as a dalil.
This shows how the same source text can yield opposite rulings depending on the framing.
5
Apply the lesson to avoid qalb in your own arguments
When constructing a proof, prefer istidlal (mutual inference) over ta'lil to protect against inversion. For example, in a qiyas, if the illa is not exclusive, the opponent may invert it.
This is a practical benefit for anyone engaged in munazara or fatwa.

ہے۔ ان کی دلیل پر کہ جس حکم کو علت قرار دیا گیا ہے وہ علت بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی۔ والمُخلَص مِنْا۔ اور اس سے بچنے کی راہ یہ ہے کہ یعنی اگر کوئی شخص چاہے کہ اس کی علنیت پر قلب کا اعتراض وارد نہ ہو تو اس کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ وہ پہلے ہی سے ان يُخرج الكلامُ فَخَرجَ الاستدلال اپنے کلام کو ( تعلیل کے بجائے ) استدلال کی صورت میں پیش کرے۔ کیونکہ یہ ممکن ہے کہ ایک ھی دوسری شمی کی دلیل ہو۔ اور یہی دوسری کی معلول ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا قلب اس کے لیے مضر ہوگا۔ لیکن امام شافعی کو یہ خلاصہ نفع نہیں دے سکتا۔ کیونکہ دونوں میں مساوات نہیں پائی جاتی۔ کیونکہ رحیم بہت ہی کڑی خطرناک سزا ہے۔ اور اس کے نافذ کرنے کے لیے بڑی شرائط ہیں۔ مگر جلد کوڑوں کی سزا) میں ایسا نہیں ہے۔ وَيَنْفَعُنَا لَوْ قُلْنَا الصَّوْمُ عِبَادَةٌ تَلُومُ بِالقَدْرِ فَتَلزم بالشروع إِذْ لَو قَلْبَ الْخَصْمُ فَيَقُولُ إنَّمَا لاَمُ بالنذر لأنه يلزمُ بالشروع قُلْنَا بَيْنَهُمَا مُسارَاةٌ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَسْتَدِلُ بِحَالِ يَلْزَمُ كُلِّ مِّنْهُمَا عَلى الآخرِ وَلَاضَيْرَ فِيْهِ وَالثَّانِي قَلْبُ الْوَصفِ شاهِدًا عَلَى الْخَصْمِ بَعْدَ أَنْ كَانَ ظَهْرُهُ إِلَيْهِ وَجْهُهُ اِلَيْكَ فَهُوَ مُعَارِضَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنَّهُ يَلُ عَلَى خِلَافٍ مُدْعِى الْخَصْمَ وَفِيْهِ مَنَاقِضَةٌ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَنْ دَلِيْلَة لَمْ يَدَلُّ عَلَى مُدَّعَاهُ وَهَذَا هُوَ الَّذِى يُسمِّيْهِ أَهْلُ الْمُنَاظَرَةِ بِالْمُقَارَصَةِ بِالْقَلْبِ وَيَجْرِى فِى كَثِيرٍ مِنَ الأَحْيَانِ فِي الْمُغَالَطَةِ الْعَامَّةِ الْوُرُدِ وَكَمَا يَقْنُوْهُ فِي كُتُبِهِمْ كَقَوْلِهِمْ فِي صَوْمِ رَمَضَانَ أَنَّهُ صَوْمُ فَرَضَ فَلَا بِتَادُئ إلَّا بِتَعْيِيْنِ النُّيَةَ كَصَوْمِ الْقَضَاءِ فَجُعِلَتْ الْفَرْضِيَةُ مِلَّةَ لِلتَّعِيْنِ فَعَارَ صَنَاهُ بِالْقَلِبِ وَجَعَلْنَا الْفَرْضِيَةَ دَلِيْلاً عَلَى عَدَمِ التَّنْبِيْنِ فَقُلْنَا لَمَّا كَانَ صَوْمًا فَرْضًا اسْتَغْنَى عَنْ تَعْبِيْنِ النّيَةِ بَعْدَ تَعْيِنُه كَصَومِ الْقَضاءِ إِنَّمَا يَحتَاجُ إِلى تَشِييْنِ وَاحِدٍ فَقَطْ لَأَزَائِدٌ فِيهِ هذَا كَذَالِك لكنه انما يتعين بالشرُوعِ هَذَا تَعْيِينُ قَبْلَهُ مِنْ جَانِبِ السَّارِعُ حَيْثُ قَالَ إِذَا إِنْسَبْحَ شَعْبَانُ فَلا صَوْمَ إِلا عَنْ رَمْضَانَ فصوم رمضان وَصَوْمُ الْقَضاءِ سوَاءٌ فِى أَنَّهُ لا يَحْتَاجُ إِلى تَعْيِينِ يَعْدَ تَعَيَيْن لَكِنَّ الرَّمَضَانَ لَمَّا كَانَ مُعَيَّنًا قَبْلَ الشروعِ فَلاَ يَحْتَاجُ إِلى تَعيينِ الْعَبْدِ وَصَوْمُ الْقَضَاءِ لَمَّا لَمْ يَكْنُ مُتَعينًا قَبْلَ الشروع احتاج الى تعيين الْعَبْد مرة.

۔
ويُنْفَعْنَا لَو قُلْنَا الصَّوْمُ عِبَادَةُ الخ اور ہمارے لیے مفید ہے مثلاً اگر ہم کہتے ہیں کہ روزہ ترجمہ و تشریح ایک عبادت ہے۔ جو نذر ماننے سے واجب ہو جاتی ہے۔ لید اروزہ شروع کرنے سے لازم لہدار ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اگر خصم اور مقابل اس میں دلیل قلب پیش کرے گا تو یہی کہے گا کہ روزہ نذر ہے اس لئے واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ شروع کرنے سے واجب ہو جاتا ہے ہم جواب دیں گے کہ ان دونوں کے درمیان مساوات پائی جاتی ہے جس میں ممکن ہے کہ ایک کے حال کو دوسرے کے حال پر استدلال کر لیا جائے۔ اور اس میں کوئی حرج بھی نہیں ہے۔
وَالثَّانِي قَلْبُ الْوَصفِ شاهِداً على الخصم اور قلب کی دوسری قسم یہ ہے کہ علت کو اس طرح پلٹ دینا کہ وہ مستدل سکے دعوی کے لیے مثبت ہونے کے بجائے اس کے خلاف پر دال بن جائے یعنی خصم کے خلاف پر۔ تو یہ قلب (امور حسی میں) قلب جواب کے مشابہ ہے۔ اور قلب جواب تو شہ دان کے ظاہر کو باطن اور باطن کو ظاہر کر دینا تو گویا وصف علت کی پشت پہلے تمہاری طرف کو تھی۔ اور اس کا چہرہ خصم کی طرف تھا۔ اور اس کے بعد قلب واقع ہوا تو پیٹھ اس کی طرف ہو گئی۔ اور اس کا چہرہ تمہاری طرف کو ہو گیا۔ لہذا یہ اس حیثیت سے تو معارضہ ہے کہ خصم کے مدعاء کے خلاف میں دلالت کرتا ہے اور اس میں مناقصہ بھی پایا جارہا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی دلیل اس کے مدعا کے حق میں دلالت نہیں کرتی۔ اہل مناظرہ اسی کو اپنی اصطلاح میں معارضہ بالقلب سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں۔ اور اکثر و بیشتر یہ مغالطہ عامتہ الورود میں بھی جاری ہو جاتا ہے جیسا کہ انہوں نے اپنی کتابوں میں تفصیلات بیان کی ہیں۔ حققَوْلِهِمْ فِي صَوْمِ رَمَضَانَ۔ جیسے کے رمضان کے روزہ کے بارے میں شوافع کہتے ہیں کہ یہ روزہ چونکہ فرض ہے۔ اس لیے بغیر تعین نیست کے ارانہ ہو گا جس طرح تضاء کا روز و بغیر تعین نیست ادا نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ تو شوافع نے فرضیت (فرض ہونا) کو تعین نیت کی علت بنا دیا ہے۔ تو ہم نے شوافع کے خلاف معارضہ بالقلب کیا اور فرضیت ہی کو نخدم تعین نیت کی وليل قرار ديديا - فَقُلْنَا لَمَّا كَانَ صَوْماً فَرْضاً الخ۔ تو ہم یوں کہتے ہیں کہ رمضان شریف کا روزہ چونکہ فرض ہے۔ اس لیے خود سے تعین نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اللہ تعالی کی طرف سے تعین کر دئیے جانے کے بعد جیسا کہ قضاروزو ایک مرتبہ اس کی تعین کر دینے کے بعد دوبارہ تعین کی ضرورت نہیں ہوتی۔ اسی طرح رمضان کا روزہ بھی دوبارہ متعین کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ وَلَكِنَّهُ إِنَّمَا يَتَعَيَّنُ بِالشروع البتہ قضاء کا روزہ متعین ہوتا ہے۔ (نیت کے ساتھ ) شروع کرنے سے اور رمضان کا روزہ پہلے ہی سے متعین ہے۔ یعنی جناب شارع کی جانب سے متعین ہے کیونکہ شارع علیہ السلام نے ارشاد فرمایا ہے کہ اِذا انستل شعبان الخ۔ جب ماہ شعبان کا مہینہ پورا ختم ہو جائے تو پھر کوئی روزہ علاوہ ماہ رمضان کے کوئی دوسرا روزہ نہیں ہے۔ لہذا صوم رمضان اور صوم قضاء دونوں اس بات میں برابر ہے کہ ایک مرتبہ تعین کر دینے کے بعد دوبارہ تعین کے محتاج نہیں ہیں۔ مگر چونکہ صوم رمضان پہلے
And the escape from us is that he brings out the speech, so the argumentation comes out (as istidlal instead of ta'lil). And it benefits us if we say: Fasting is an act of worship that becomes obligatory by vow, so it becomes binding by commencement. If the opponent performs qalb and says: It is obligated only by vow because it becomes binding by commencement, we say: There is equality between them; it is possible that the condition of each may be used as evidence for the other, and there is no harm in that. The second type is qalb al-wasf (inversion of the description), making it a witness against the opponent after it was a witness for him. It is like inverting a garment, making its back its front and its front its back. If the description first faced you and its back faced the opponent, then after inversion its back faces you and its front faces the opponent. This is a contradiction in that it indicates against the opponent's claim, and there is inconsistency in that his evidence does not prove his claim. This is what the dialecticians call mu'arada bil-qalb (counter-argument by inversion). And it occurs frequently in common fallacies. For example, regarding the fast of Ramadan: The Shafi'is say it is an obligatory fast, so it is not performed except with specification of intention, like the make-up fast. So they made obligation a cause for specification. We countered by qalb and made obligation a proof for lack of specification, saying: Since it is an obligatory fast, it is free from needing specification of intention after it has been specified (by Allah), just as the make-up fast only needs one specification because there is no extra [in it]. But the Ramadan fast is specified before commencement by the Lawgiver, who said: 'When Sha'ban passes, there is no fast except for Ramadan.' So the fast of Ramadan and the make-up fast are the same in that they do not need specification after being specified, but Ramadan is specified before commencement, so it does not need specification by the servant, while the make-up fast, since it was not specified before commencement, needs one specification by the servant.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Anwar explains two types of qalb (inversion) in usul argumentation. The first part discusses a method to nullify the opponent's qalb by presenting the argument as istidlal (evidence) rather than ta'lil (causal explanation). In ta'lil, there is a specific cause-effect relationship that the opponent can invert, but in istidlal, the relationship is mutual and not vulnerable to qalb. The second part describes the second type of qalb, called qalb al-wasf (inversion of description), where a quality that was evidence for the opponent becomes evidence against him. This is like flipping a garment. The author then provides a concrete example: the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the need for a specific intention in Ramadan fasting. The Shafi'is argue that since it is obligatory, it requires intention like make-up fasts. The Hanafis invert this by arguing that since it is obligatory and already specified by the Lawgiver, no additional intention is needed, using the hadith 'When half of Sha'ban passes, there is no fast except Ramadan.' Thus, the Hanafi position is that Ramadan fast does not require a specific intention at dawn because the time itself specifies it.

Key Terms
قلب (qalb): In usul, qalb is a method of rebuttal where the opponent's evidence is inverted to support the contrary position.
تعليل (ta'lil): Ta'lil is the act of assigning a cause (illa) to a ruling, creating a necessary connection between them.
استدلال (istidlal): Istidlal is presenting evidence (dalil) without claiming a cause-effect relationship, allowing for mutual inference.
معارضة بالقلب (mu'arada bil-qalb): A dialectical technique where the opponent's evidence is turned against him by inverting its implication.
قضاء (qada'): Make-up fasts, those missed and later compensated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i argument on Ramadan fast intention, what is the crucial difference between Ramadan and make-up fasts?
A) Ramadan fast is obligatory while make-up is voluntary.
B) Ramadan fast is specified by the Lawgiver before commencement, while make-up is not.
C) Make-up fast requires intention because it is optional.
D) Ramadan fast is invalid without intention.

Key Takeaway
To protect your argument from inversion (qalb), present it as istidlal (mutual inference) rather than ta'lil (one-way causation), and use qalb al-wasf to turn the opponent's evidence against them.

Weak Qalb: Binding Voluntary Acts by Inversion
Weak qalb in Hanafi usul regarding binding of nawafil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the weak qalb argument in the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute over binding of voluntary acts, and evaluate its strength as a form of qiyas.

Core Idea
Weak qalb: The opponent's own evidence is inverted into the very cause for the opposing ruling.

When Shafi'is argue that voluntary prayers do not become binding because one need not proceed when invalidated, Hanafis turn this around: the very lack of proceeding becomes the link that equates voluntary acts with vows, which are binding. This is a subtle inversion called qalb da'if. In this lesson, we unpack this argument and see why it is considered weak yet still supports the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed issue
Clearly articulate the point of contention: Do voluntary acts (nawafil) become binding (lazim) upon commencement? The Hanafis say yes; Shafi'is say no.
2
Identify the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'is argue that voluntary acts do not bind because if invalidated, one does not have to proceed in the invalid state or make up the act, unlike Hajj.
This is based on the absence of 'imda' (proceeding) in invalidity.
3
Recognize the Hanafi response (qalb)
Hanafis invert the Shafi'i evidence: they take the same description (non-proceeding in invalidity) and make it the cause (illa) for equality between vows and commencement, which yields binding.
This is the weak qalb: it does not directly negate the opponent's claim but establishes equality implying binding.
4
Analyze why this qalb is weak
The inversion does not produce the explicit opposite (binding by commencement) but only an equality that necessitates binding. Moreover, equality is not consistently applied (e.g., wudu also has non-proceeding of invalidity but is not binding).
The weakness lies in the lack of direct contravention and inconsistency in the illa's application.
5
Distinguish weak qalb from true aks
True aks (inverse) is fully reciprocal: 'What binds by vow binds by commencement (like Hajj); what does not bind by vow does not bind by commencement (like wudu).' Weak qalb only resembles aks but is not fully reciprocal.
True aks is stronger and used for tarjih; weak qalb is accepted only in absence of stronger evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَدْ تَقَلَبَ الْعِلْةُ مِنْ وَجْهِ اخَرَ غَيْرَ الْوَجْهَيْنِ الْمَذْكُورَيْنِ وَهُوَ ضَعِيفَ كَقَوْلِهِمْ أَى السَّافَعِيَةِ فِي حَقَّ النَّوَافِلِ حَيْثُ لا تلزم بالشرُوْعِ وَلَا تُقْضَى بِالإِفْسادِ عِنْدَهُمْ هذه عِبَادَةً لأَيَمْضِي فِي فَاسِدِهَا أَنْ إِذَا فَسَدَتْ بِنُفْسِهَا مِنْ غَيْرِ إِفْسَادِ بِظُهورِ الْحَدَثِ مِنَ الْمُصَلَّى لايَجِبُ إِثْمَامُهَا وَهَذَا بِخِلافِ الْحَج فَإِنَّهُ إِذَا فَسَدَ ب فِيهِ الْمَضَى وَالْقَضاءُ بَعْدَهُ فَلا م بالشرُوْعِ كَالوَضَوْءِ فَإِنَّهُ لَمَّا لَمْ في فَاسِدُهُ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ بِالشَّرُوعِ فَيُقَالُ لَهُمْ لَمَّا كَانَ كَذَالِكَ وَجَبَ أَنْ يَسْتَوِيَ فِيْهِ أَى فِي النَّقْلِ عَمَلُ النَّدْرِ وَالشَّرُوعِ بِاللُّرُوْم كَمَا اسْتَوَىٰ عَمَلُهَا فِي الوُضُوءِ يقدم اللُّزِوْم فَالْوَصْف الَّذِي جَعَلَهُ الشَّافِعِيُّ دَلِيْلاً عَلَى عَدَمِ اللُّرُوْمِ بِالشَّرُوعِ فِى النَّقْلِ وَهُوَ عَدَمُ الإمْضَاء فِى الْفَسادِ جَعَلْنَاهُ عِلَّةٌ لاِسْتَواءِ النُّذَرَ وَالشروع ويلزم منه اللزوم بالشروع فَكَانَ قَلْبًا مِنْ هَذِهِ الْحَيْنِيَةِ وَإِنَّمَا كَانَ هَذَا القُلبُ ضَعِيفًا لأَنَّهُ مَا أَتَى بَصَرِيحٍ نَقِيْضِ الْخَصْمِ وَأَعْنِي اللُّرُوْمِ بِالشروعِ بَلْ أَتى بِمَا الاستواء اللرُّومِ لَهُ وَلان الإستَواءِ مُخْتَلِفٌ ثُبُوتًا وَدَوَالًا فَفِي الْوَضَوْءِ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ غَيْرَ لَأَزِم بالشرُوعِ وَالنُّذُورُ فِي النَّفَلِ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ لَأَزِمًا بِهِمَا وَيُسْتَمْى هَذَا عَكْسًا أى شبيها بالْعَكْس لاَعَكْسُ حَقِيقِيًا لان العكس الحقيقي هُوَ أَنْ رد الشيء عَلى سُنَنِهِ الأول كَمَا يُقَاسُ فِي قَوْلِنَا مَا يَلْزَمُ بالنذر يَلْزَمُ بالشروع كَالْجَجْ وَمَا يَلْزَمُ بِالنَّداءِ لَا يُلْزِمُ بِالشَّرُوعِ كَالْوُضُوْءِ وَهُوَ يَصْلَحُ لِلتَرْجِيْحِ عَلَى مَا سَيَاتِي لآنَ مَا يَطْرِدُ وَيَتْعَكِسُ أُولَى مِمَّا يَطْرِدُ وَلَا يَنْعَكِسُ وَهَذَا لَمَّا كَانَ رَدُّ الشَّيْءِ عَلَى خَلافِ سُنّتِهِ الأَوَّلِ كَانَ دَاخِلاً فِى الْقَلْبِ شَبِيْمًا بِالْعَكْسِ وَإِنَّما جَعَلَهُ عَكْسا اتَّبَاعًا لِفَخر الاسلام.
وَقَدْ تُغْلَبُ الْعِلْةُ مِنْ وَجْهِ اخَرَ اور بھی قلب ملت دوسرے طریقہ سے ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی ترجمہ و تشریح مذکورہ دونوں وجہوں کے علاوہ سے وَهُوَ ضعيف كقولهم لیکن یہ طریقہ ضعیف ہے جیسا کہ وہ کہتے ہیں یعنی شوافع تقبل کے بارے میں کہتے ہیں نماز شروع کرنے سے لازم نہیں ہوتی۔ اور اگر شروع
And the cause may be inverted in another way besides the two mentioned, and it is weak, like their statement (i.e., the Shafi'is) concerning voluntary acts: they do not become binding by commencement and are not made up when invalidated according to them. They say: This is a worship in which one does not proceed in its invalidated state; if it becomes invalid on its own without intentional spoiling, like the occurrence of a hadath from the praying person, its completion is not obligatory. This is unlike Hajj, for if it becomes invalid, one must proceed and then make up. So there is no binding by commencement, like wudu, for since one does not proceed in its invalidated state, it does not become binding by commencement. It is said to them: Since it is so, it should be equal in that the effect of nadhr (vow) and commencement are equal in binding, just as their effect is equal in wudu via priority of binding. So the description that the Shafi'i made a proof for non-binding by commencement in voluntary acts, namely non-proceeding in invalid state, we make it a cause for equality of vows and commencement, and from that follows binding by commencement. So it was an inversion from this aspect. This inversion is weak because it does not bring the explicit opposite of the opponent, i.e., binding by commencement, but rather brings equality which necessitates binding. And because equality differs in thubut and dawaran: in wudu, it is not binding by commencement, but in voluntary acts, vows are binding by both. This is called 'aks (inverse), i.e., resembling true inverse, but not true inverse. For true inverse is to return something to its original course, as in our saying: 'What becomes binding by vow becomes binding by commencement, like Hajj; and what becomes binding by [؟] does not become binding by commencement, like wudu.' And it is suitable for tarjih, as will come, because what applies consistently and is invertible is better than what applies consistently but is not invertible. Since this is a return of something contrary to its original course, it falls under 'qalb' resembling 'aks'. And he made it 'aks' following Fakhr al-Islam. And the cause is overcome in another way: i.e., qalb occurs in another way besides the two mentioned, and it is weak, like their statement (the Shafi'is) concerning voluntary acts: prayer does not become binding by commencement, and if one begins...
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of qalb (inversion) by presenting a weak form. The issue is whether voluntary acts (nawafil) become binding once commenced. Shafi'is argue they are not binding because if they become invalid, one does not have to make them up, unlike Hajj. Hanafis invert this: the fact that one does not proceed in invalidity is actually the cause for equality between vows and voluntary acts in binding. They analogize with wudu, which is also not binding upon commencement. This qalb is considered weak because it does not directly disprove the opponent's conclusion but rather establishes equality that implies binding. The text distinguishes between true 'aks (inverse) and this weak qalb. True 'aks would be: what binds by vow binds by commencement (like Hajj), and what does not bind by vow does not bind by commencement (like wudu). The author (Fakhr al-Islam) calls this weak form 'aks. The passage ends with the beginning of an Urdu commentary. The Hanafi position is that voluntary acts do become binding upon commencement, based on this analogy with vows and the principle of commitment.

Key Terms
قلب ضعيف (qalb da'if): A weak inversion that does not directly negate the opponent's claim but creates an implication that supports one's own view.
عكس (aks): True inverse: a proposition that and its converse both hold consistently, used for tarjih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, why do voluntary acts become binding upon commencement?
A) Because they are fard
B) Because they are analogous to vows which are binding
C) Because the Prophet said so
D) Because they are not binding at all

Key Takeaway
The weak qalb shows that even when an argument does not directly refute the opponent, it can still support one's position by reinterpreting the evidence.

The Third Weak Qalb: Equality Without Direct Contradiction
Explaining the third weak way of qalb and distinguishing it from true 'aks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the third weak form of qalb al-illa, explain why it is weak, and distinguish it from true 'aks (inverse) in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A qalb that only establishes equality—not the explicit contrary—is weak, and is called 'aks by resemblance, not a true inverse.

In Hanafi usul, qalb al-illa is a powerful method of mu'arada where the opponent's own attribute is inverted to prove the opposite. But not all inversions are equally strong. This lesson examines the third, weak form of qalb, which fails to bring the explicit contrary and only establishes a partial equality. Through the classic dispute on whether supererogatory prayers are binding upon commencement, we will see why this qalb is considered weak and how it differs from true 'aks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Opponent's Argument
The Shafi'is argue that supererogatory prayers are not binding by commencement (shuru') and if invalidated, need not be made up. Their proof is qiyas to wudu: wudu is not binding by commencement and is not completed if invalidated; similarly, supererogatory prayers are non-obligatory acts of worship.
The opponent's attribute is 'non-completion upon invalidation' (adam al-imḍā' fī al-fasād).
2
Understand the Hanafi Qalb Response
The Hanafis take the same attribute (non-completion upon invalidation) and use it to prove equality between a vow (nadhr) and commencement (shuru'). They argue: just as in wudu both vow and commencement result in non-binding, in supererogatory acts both should result in binding. From this equality, they conclude that commencement makes the prayer binding—the opposite of the Shafi'i claim.
This is a qalb because the attribute is inverted to support the opposite conclusion.
3
Analyze Why This Qalb is Weak
The qalb is weak because it does not directly prove the explicit contrary of the opponent's claim (binding by commencement). Instead, it only proves equality between vow and commencement. Moreover, equality (istiwā') differs in affirmation and negation: in wudu, both vow and commencement are non-binding; in supererogatory acts, a vow is binding but commencement is not according to the Shafi'is. Thus the equality is not consistent across all cases.
The weakness is due to lack of direct contradiction and inconsistency of the attribute's effect.
4
Distinguish Weak Qalb from True 'Aks
True 'aks (inverse) requires that the ruling be consistent both positively and negatively. For example: 'What is binding by vow is binding by commencement (like Hajj); what is not binding by vow is not binding by commencement (like wudu).' This third qalb does not meet this condition because it only works in one direction (vow to commencement) but not the other. Therefore, it is called 'aks only by resemblance, not a true inverse.
True 'aks is used for tarjih (preference) among consistent attributes.
5
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: According to the Hanafi school, a person who starts a nafl prayer and then experiences an event (e.g., breaking wudu) must complete the prayer and later make it up (qada). According to the Shafi'i school, no completion or makeup is required; the prayer simply becomes invalid. This difference stems from the dispute over whether commencement imposes binding obligation.
The thamarah shows the real-world impact of the usul disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَدْ تُقْلَبُ الْعِلَّةُ مِنْ وَجْهٍ آخَرَ غَيْرَ الْوَجْهَيْنِ الْمَذْكُورَيْنِ وَهُوَ ضَعِيفٌ كَقَوْلِهِمْ أَيِ الشَّافِعِيَّةِ فِي حَقِّ النَّوَافِلِ حَيْثُ لَا تَلْزَمُ بِالشُّرُوعِ وَلَا النَّفْلِ مِنْ حَيْثُ كَوْنِهِ لَازِمًا بِهِمَا وَيُسَمَّى هَذَا عَكْسًا أَيْ شَبِيهًا بِالْعَكْسِ لَا عَكْسًا حَقِيقِيًّا لِأَنَّ الْعَكْسَ الْحَقِيقِيَّ هُوَ أَنْ يَرِدَ الشَّيْءُ عَلَى سُنَنِهِ الْأَوَّلِ كَمَا يُقَالُ فِي قَوْلِنَا مَا يَلْزَمُ بِالنَّذْرِ يَلْزَمُ بِالشُّرُوعِ كَالْحَجِّ وَمَا لَا يَلْزَمُ بِالنَّذْرِ لَا يَلْزَمُ بِالشُّرُوعِ كَالْوُضُوءِ وَهُوَ يَصْلُحُ لِلتَّرْجِيحِ عَلَى مَا سَيَأْتِي لِأَنَّ مَا يَطَّرِدُ وَيَنْعَكِسُ أَوْلَى مِمَّا يَطَّرِدُ وَلَا يَنْعَكِسُ وَهَذَا لَمَّا كَانَ رَدَّ الشَّيْءِ عَلَى خِلَافِ سُنَّتِهِ الْأَوَّلِ كَانَ دَاخِلًا فِي الْقَلْبِ شَبِيهًا بِالْعَكْسِ وَإِنَّمَا جَعَلَهُ عَكْسًا اتِّبَاعًا لِفَخْرِ الْإِسْلَامِ. اور بھی قلب مئل دوسرے طریقہ سے ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی ترجمہ و تشریح مذکورہ دونوں وجہوں کے علاوہ سے لیکن یہ طریقہ ضعیف ہے جیسا کہ وہ کہتے ہیں یعنی شوافع نفل کے بارے میں کہتے ہیں نماز شروع کرنے سے لازم نہیں ہوتی۔ اور اگر شروع کر کے فاسد کر دی جائے تو اس کی قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی ان کے نزدیک۔ یہ نوافل ایسی عبادت ہیں کہ ان کے فاسد کے پورا کرنے کا حکم نہیں ہے۔ یعنی شروع کرنے کے بعد اگر نفل خود ہی فاسد ہو جائے مثلا نماز پڑھنے والے کو حدث ہو جائے تو اس شخص کا پورا کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ مگر حج اس کے بر خلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ حج اگر فاسد ہو جائے تو بعینہ افعال حج کو پورا کرنا واجب اور ایام حج کے بعد اگلے سال اس کی قضا واجب ہے۔ فلا تلزم بالشروع ابدا شروع کر دینے سے نفل نماز واجب نہیں ہوگی ۔ فَيُقَالُ لَهُمْ كَذَّالِكَ وَجَبَ أَنْ يَسْتَوَى فِيهِ. تو شوافع کے جواب میں ہماری طرف سے کہا جائے گا کہ (جب تم نے وضو کو فاسد ہو جانے پر پورا کرنے کا وجوب نہ قرار دیا۔ اور اس پر نفل نماز کو شروع کر کے لازم نہ ہونے کو قیاس کر لیا) تو اس سے یہ بات بھی لازم آتی ہے کہ نفل میں نذر اور شروع کا حکم بھی یکساں ہی ہو۔ یعنی ان دونوں سے نفل لازم ہو جائے۔ جس طرح وضو میں دونوں کا حکم یکساں ہے۔ یعنی ان میں سے کسی سے بھی وضوء کا اتمام واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ تو جس وصف کو حضرت امام شافعی نے نفل نماز کو شروع کرنے سے لازم نہ ہونے کی دلیل قرار دیا تھا۔ ہم نے اسی وصف کو نذر اور شروع باہم یکساں ہونے کی علت قرار دیا ہے اور ان دونوں کی برابری کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ نوافل شروع کرنے سے لازم ہو جائیں جس طرح نذر سے بالاتفاق لازم ہوتے ہیں اس توجیہ کی رو سے معارضہ بالقلب ہو گیا مگر یہ قلب اس وجہ سے ضعیف ہے معارض نے مخالف سے دعوی کی صریح نقیض یعنی شروع کرنے سے لازم ہونا اس کو ثابت نہیں کیا بلکہ صرف برابر ثابت کر دی ہے جس سے مشروع لزوم کا سبب ہونا ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ نیز چونکہ استواء کے اثرات اصل اور فرع میں وجود اور عدم وجود میں مختلف ہیں۔ اور استواء ہی سے معارض استدلال کر رہا ہے۔ لہذا معارضہ ضعیف ہے۔ پس وضوء میں اس حیثیت سے کہ شروع کرنے سے لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ اور نذر اور نفل دونوں شروع کرنے سے لازم ہو جاتے ہیں۔ وَيُسَمَّى هَذَا عَكْسًا اور اس قلب کا نام عکس ہے۔ یعنی عکس کے مشابہ ہے۔ عکس حقیقی نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ عکس حقیقی ہی کو اس پہلے اسلوب پر لوٹا دینے کے ہیں مثلا ہمارا قول کہ جو عبادت نذر ماننے سے لازم ہوتی ہے ، وہ شروع کرنے سے بھی لازم ہوتی ہے جیسے حج اور جو چیز نذر ماننے سے لازم نہیں ہوتی ہے وہ شروع کرنے سے بھی لازم نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے کہ وضوء اس عکس سے کسی وصف کے علت ہونے کو ترجیح حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ جیسا کہ عنقریب آئے گا۔ کیونکہ جس چیز کا اثر وجود اور عدم دونوں میں ظاہر ہو وہ یقینی طور پر اولی ہو گا۔ اس وصف پر جس کا اثر صرف وجود میں ظاہر ہو عدم میں ظاہر نہ ہو۔ بہر حال قلب کی اس تیسری صورت میں مخالف کے استدلال کو اس کے اول اسلوب کے خلاف میں پھیرا گیا ہے، اس لیے اس پر عکس حقیقی کی تعریف صادق نہیں آتی، تو یہ معارضہ بالقلب ہی میں داخل ہے۔ عکس کے ساتھ صرف مشابہت پائی جاتی ہے۔ اس کو عکس قرار دیا جانا فقط
And the cause may be inverted from another perspective other than the two mentioned perspectives, and it is weak, like their saying, meaning the Shafi'is, regarding supererogatory acts: they are not binding by commencing and are not made up if invalidated according to them. This is an act of worship that is not completed in its invalid state: that if it becomes invalid by itself without intentional invalidation, like the occurrence of an event from the prayer, its completion is not obligatory. And this is contrary to Hajj, for if it becomes invalid, proceeding in it and then making it up are obligatory. So it is not binding by commencement like ablution, for since it is not proceeded with in its invalid state, it is not binding by commencement. So it is said to them: Since it is so, it is necessary that the effect of a vow and commencement be equal in supererogatory acts in terms of binding, just as their effect is equal in ablution in terms of non-binding. So the attribute that al-Shafi'i made a proof for non-binding by commencement in supererogatory acts, which is non-proceeding in invalidity, we made it a cause for the equality of vow and commencement, and from it binding by commencement follows. So it is an inversion from this aspect. And this inversion is only weak because it did not bring the explicit contrary of the opponent, meaning binding by commencement, but rather brought what entails binding for it. And because equality differs in affirmation and negation. For in ablution, from the aspect that it is not binding by commencement, and in supererogatory acts, from the aspect that it is binding by both. And this is called 'aks, meaning similar to the true inverse, not a true inverse, because the true inverse is that the thing goes back to its original course, as in our saying: what is binding by a vow is binding by commencement, like Hajj; and what is not binding by a vow is not binding by commencement, like ablution. And it is suitable for tarjih as will come, because what is consistent and has an inverse is better than what is consistent but has no inverse. And this, since it turns the thing against its original course, is included in qalb, similar to the inverse. And he only called it 'aks following Fakhr al-Islam. And there is also a second way of inversion from another perspective, i.e., the translation and commentary: besides the two mentioned perspectives, but this way is weak, as they say, i.e., the Shafi'is say regarding supererogatory prayers: they are not binding by commencing, and if one starts and then invalidates it, its recompense is not obligatory according to them. These supererogatory acts are such that there is no command to complete their invalid state. That is, after starting, if the supererogatory act becomes invalid by itself, e.g., the prayer experiences an event, then completing it is not obligatory for that person. But Hajj is contrary to this, because if Hajj becomes invalid, then performing the actions of Hajj exactly is obligatory, and after the days of Hajj, its recompense the following year is obligatory. 'So it is not binding by commencement at all' - starting a supererogatory prayer does not make it obligatory. Then it is said to them: 'Since it is so, it is necessary that the effect of vow and commencement be equal in supererogatory acts in terms of binding, just as their effect is equal in ablution in terms of non-binding.' So in response to the Shafi'is, we say: since you made ablution not obligatory to complete upon invalidation and analogized supererogatory prayer to it in non-binding by commencement, then from this it also follows that in supererogatory acts, the ruling of vow and commencement should be the same, i.e., both make the supererogatory act binding. Just as in ablution the ruling of both is the same: neither makes completion of ablution obligatory. So the attribute that Imam al-Shafi'i made a proof for supererogatory prayer not being binding by commencement, we made that same attribute a cause for the equality of vow and commencement, and the requirement of this equality is that supererogatory acts become binding by commencement, just as they are binding by vow by consensus. By this reasoning, a mu'arada by qalb occurs, but this qalb is weak because the opponent did not prove the explicit contrary of the claim, i.e., binding by commencement, but only proved equality, from which the cause of binding might be proven. Also, because the effects of equality differ in existence and non-existence in the original and branch. And the opponent is arguing based on equality itself, so the mu'arada is weak. So in ablution, from the aspect that it is not binding by commencement, and in supererogatory acts, both vow and commencement are binding. And this is called 'aks, i.e., resembling the inverse, not a true inverse, because the true inverse is to return the thing to its original course, e.g., our statement: whatever act of worship is binding by a vow is binding by commencement, like Hajj; and whatever is not binding by a vow is not binding by commencement, like ablution. From this 'aks, preference is obtained for a description being a cause, as will come, because whatever is consistent and has an inverse is better than whatever is consistent but has no inverse. In any case, in this third form of qalb, the opponent's argument is turned against his original course, so the definition of true 'aks does not apply to it; it is included in mu'arada bi-l-qalb. It only has resemblance to 'aks. Calling it 'aks is merely...
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar explains the third, weak method of qalb al-illa (inverting the cause) in Hanafi usul. The author describes how the Shafi'is argue that supererogatory (nafl) prayers are not binding upon commencement (shuru'), and if invalidated, they need not be made up, unlike Hajj. In response, the Hanafis attempt to invert the argument: they take the same attribute (non-completion upon invalidation) that the Shafi'is use to prove non-binding, and instead use it to establish equality between vow (nadhr) and commencement—arguing that since both vow and commencement lead to invalidation being ignored, they should both be binding. However, this qalb is weak because it does not directly prove the opposite of the opponent's claim (binding by commencement), but only proves equality, which may not hold consistently. The Shafi'is can respond that in ablution, neither vow nor commencement makes it binding, while in supererogatory acts, a vow does make it binding but commencement does not—so the equality is not universal. Therefore, this method is called 'aks (resembling a true inverse) rather than a true inverse, because a true inverse would both affirm and negate consistently (e.g., whatever is binding by vow is binding by commencement, and whatever is not binding by vow is not binding by commencement). The passage emphasizes that this weak qalb is still valid for tarjih (preference) and follows the authority of Fakhr al-Islam (al-Pazdawi). The Urdu commentary then expands on the argument, reiterating that the Shafi'i position on supererogatory prayers not being binding by commencement is analogized to ablution, but the Hanafi counter-argument based on equality of vow and commencement is weak because it only establishes partial equivalence, and thus does not force the opponent to accept binding by commencement.

Key Terms
القلب (al-qalb): Inversion of the cause: using the opponent's own attribute to prove the opposite or a parallel ruling, often in usul disputes.
العكس (al-'aks): A true inverse where a ruling is reversed both positively and negatively (e.g., if A then B, if not A then not B).
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship, which makes the act obligatory once made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the third form of qalb described in this passage considered weak?
A) It relies on a hadith that is not authentic.
B) It does not prove the explicit contrary of the opponent's claim; it only establishes equality, which may be inconsistent in affirmation and negation.
C) It contradicts the consensus of the Companions.
D) It is based on qiyas which is not a valid source in Hanafi usul.

Key Takeaway
A strong qalb must bring the explicit contrary of the opponent's claim and maintain consistency in both affirmation and negation; otherwise, it is weak and only resembles a true inverse ('aks).

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Qalb and 'Aks in Counter-Arguments
Explains qalb and 'aks as weak forms of counter-argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qalb and true 'aks and evaluate the strength of a qalb argument in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Qalb reverses analogy but proves only equality, not opposite; true 'aks tests causality consistently.

In Hanafi jadal, counter-arguments aim to refute an opponent's qiyas. Two common methods are al-qalb (inversion) and al-‘aks (reverse). While they may appear similar, Hanafi usul treats them distinctly: qalb is considered weak unless it directly negates the opponent's claim, whereas true ‘aks provides stronger evidence by showing consistent causal effect. This passage illustrates the difference through a debate on whether starting a supererogatory act makes it obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's original analogy
The Shafi'i argues that since starting wudu does not obligate completion, starting nafl prayer also does not obligate completion. Recognize this as a straightforward qiyas.
The attribute in the Shafi'i analogy is 'lack of obligation upon starting'.
2
Trace the Hanafi qalb response
The Hanafi responds by using the same attribute (equality between vow and start) to claim that if vow makes nafl obligatory, then starting should also. This is qalb because it reverses the direction of the analogy.
The qalb does not directly prove the opposite; it merely asserts equality.
3
Assess the weakness of the qalb
The text notes two flaws: (1) it only shows equality, not that start directly obligates; (2) the effect of equality differs between wudu and Hajj, so the attribute is not consistent.
A strong counter-argument would produce a true opposite ruling, not just a parallel.
4
Distinguish qalb from true 'aks
True 'aks requires that the effect of an attribute be present in both existence and non-existence. Example: Hajj becomes obligatory by both vow and start; wudu does not by either. This consistency strengthens causality.
The passage clarifies that the Hanafi qalb here is merely analogous to 'aks, not true 'aks.
5
Apply the principle to other cases
Practice identifying whether a given counter-argument is qalb (weak) or true 'aks (strong) by checking if it directly negates the original claim and if the causal effect is consistent.
This skill is critical for usul analysis and fatwa derivation.

فَيُقَالُ لَهُمْ كَذَّالِكَ وَجَبَ أَنْ يَسْتَوَى فِيهِ. تو شوافع کے جواب میں ہماری طرف سے کہا جائے گا کہ (جب تم نے وضو کو فاسد ہو جانے پر پورا کرنے کا وجوب نہ قرار دیا۔ اور اس پر نفل نماز کو شروع کر کے لازم نہ ہونے کو قیاس کر لیا) تو اس سے یہ بات بھی لازم آتی ہے کہ نفل میں نذر اور شروع کا حکم بھی سیکساں ہی ہو۔ یعنی ان دونوں سے نقل لازم ہو جائے۔ جس طرح وضو میں دونوں کا حکم یکساں ہے۔ یعنی ان میں سے
