اور ان دونوں کی برابری کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ نوافل شروع کرنے سے لازم ہو جائیں جس طرح نذر سے بالا تفاق لازم ہوتے ہیں اس توجیہ کی رو سے معارضہ بالقلب ہو گیا مگر یہ قلب اس وجہ سے ضعیف ہے معارض نے مخالف سے دعوی کی صریح نقیض یعنی شروع کرنے سے لازم ہونا اس کو ثابت نہیں کیا بلکہ صرف برابر ثابت کر دی ہے جس سے مشروع لزوم کا سبب ہونا ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ نیز چونکہ استواء کے اثرات اصل اور فرع میں وجود اور عدم وجود میں مختلف ہیں۔ اور استواء ہی سے معارض استدلال کر رہا ہے۔ لہذا معارضہ ضعیف ہے۔ تھی الوضوء پس وضوء میں اس حیثیت سے کہ شروع کرنے سے لازم نہیں ہوتا۔ اور نذر اور نقل دونوں شروع کرنے سے لازم ہو جاتے ہیں۔ وَيُسَمَّيْ هَذَذ اعكسنا اور اس قلب کا نام عکس ہے۔ یعنی عکس کے مشابہ ہے۔ عکس حقیقی نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ عکس حقیقی ہی کو اس پہلے اسلوب پر لوٹا دینے کے ہیں مثلا ہمارا قول کہ جو عبادت نذر ماننے سے لازم ہوتی ہے ، وہ شروع کرنے سے بھی لازم ہوتی ہے جیسے حج اور جو چیز نذر ماننے سے لازم نہیں ہوتی ہے وہ شروع کرنے سے بھی لازم نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے کہ وضوء اس عکس سے کسی وصف کے علت ہونے کو ترجیح حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ جیسا کہ عنقریب آئے گا۔ کیونکہ جس چیز کا اثر وجود اور عدم دونوں میں ظاہر ہو وہ یقینی طور پر اولی ہو گا۔ اس وصف پر جس کا اثر صرف وجود میں ظاہر ہو عدم میں ظاہر نہ ہو۔ وَهَذَا إِذَا كَانَ رَد الشئي اليخ بہر حال قلب کی اس تیسری صورت میں مخالف کے استدلال کو اس کے اول اسلوب کے خلاف میں پھیرا گیا ہے، اس لیے اس پر عکس حقیقی کی تعریف صادق نہیں آتی، تو یہ ، معارضہ بالقلب ہی میں داخل ہے۔ عکس کے ساتھ صرف مشابہت پائی جاتی ہے۔ اس کو عکس قرار دیا جانا فقط
So it will be said to them: likewise, it became necessary that they be equal in it. To the Shafi'is, from our side it will be said: (When you did not make wudu obligatory to complete upon becoming invalid, and upon that you analogized that nafl prayer upon starting does not become incumbent), then from this it also follows that in nafl, the ruling of vow and start should also be alike. That is, from both, nafl becomes incumbent. Just as in wudu, the ruling of both is the same, i.e., from neither is the completion of wudu obligatory. So the attribute that Imam al-Shafi'i made the proof for nafl prayer not being incumbent upon starting, we made that same attribute the cause for the alignment of vow and start, and the requirement of their equality is that supererogatory acts become incumbent upon starting just as they become incumbent by vow by consensus. By this reasoning, the counter-argument becomes qalb (inversion), but this qalb is weak because the objector did not prove the clear opposite of the opponent's claim—i.e., that starting makes it obligatory—rather he only proved equality, which establishes that [the act] is a cause for obligation. Also because the effects of equality in the original and branch differ in existence and non-existence, and the objector is arguing by equality itself, therefore the counter-argument is weak. So wudu: from the perspective that starting does not make it obligatory, and vow and naql both become obligatory upon starting. And this is called 'aks (reverse). It resembles 'aks but is not true 'aks, because true 'aks is to return to the previous pattern, e.g., our statement: any act of worship that becomes obligatory by vow becomes obligatory by starting as well, like Hajj; and anything that does not become obligatory by vow does not become obligatory by starting, like wudu. By this 'aks, preference is given to an attribute being the cause, as will come soon. Because a thing whose effect appears in both existence and non-existence will definitely be superior over an attribute whose effect appears only in existence and not in non-existence. And this is when the return of the thing [is such...]. In any case, in this third form of qalb, the opponent's argument is turned against its original pattern, so the definition of true 'aks does not apply to it; it is only included in mu'āraḍa bi al-qalb. It has mere resemblance to 'aks; it is only called 'aks.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific type of counter-argument in Hanafi usul known as al-qalb (inversion) and its weaker form al-‘aks (reverse). The context is a debate between Hanafis and Shafi‘is regarding whether a supererogatory (nafl) act becomes obligatory once started. The Shafi‘i argument analogizes nafl prayer to wudu: just as wudu, once started, does not become obligatory to complete if invalidated, so too nafl prayer does not become obligatory once started. The Hanafi response uses a qalb argument: they take the same attribute (equality between vow and start) and claim that if the Shafi‘i insists on equality between wudu and nafl, then by analogy, nafl should be like Hajj, where both vow and start make it obligatory. However, this qalb is considered weak because it does not prove the direct opposite (that start makes nafl obligatory) but merely proves equality; also the effects of equality differ between original and branch. The author then distinguishes this from true ‘aks, which would require consistent behavior across all cases: if an act becomes obligatory by vow, it becomes obligatory by start (like Hajj), and if not by vow, then not by start (like wudu). True ‘aks is stronger because its effect is visible in both existence and non-existence. The passage clarifies that the third form of qalb is merely analogous to ‘aks, not true ‘aks.

Key Terms
القلب (al-qalb): A form of counter-argument where the opponent's analogy is reversed to derive a different ruling from the same attribute.
العكس (al-‘aks): A method where consistency of causality is shown: if a cause is present, the ruling follows; if absent, the ruling is absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the qalb argument in the nafl prayer example considered weak according to the Hanafi usul text?
A) It uses a different attribute than the opponent's.
B) It only proves equality between vow and start, not that start makes it obligatory directly.
C) It relies on consensus which is not present.
D) It contradicts a clear text from the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Qalb is a weak counter-argument in Hanafi usul because it fails to establish the direct opposite of the original claim and lacks consistency in causal effects.

Pure Counter-Argument (Mu'āraḍa Khālisa) in Hanafi Usul
Defines and classifies mu'āraḍa khālisa in usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mu'āraḍa khālisa, distinguish its two types, identify the first two divisions of counter-argument in the ruling of the branch, and apply the classification to the masḥ example.

Core Idea
A pure counter-argument presents a different proof to overturn the opponent's ruling without direct contradiction.

This passage introduces mu'āraḍa khālisa, a key tool in Hanafi uṣūl for contesting analogical reasoning. Unlike qalb, it brings a fresh proof. We will focus on its definition and the first two divisions, using the classic masḥ debate to illustrate how a different cause yields an opposite ruling.

Guided Path
1
Map the taxonomy
Identify the two main types of mu'āraḍa khālisa: counter-argument in the ruling of the branch (al-far‘) and counter-argument in the cause (al-‘illa). The passage focuses on the first type, which itself has five divisions.
Only the first two divisions are detailed.
2
Isolate the first division
Extract the definition: the objector presents a different ‘illa (cause) that directly indicates the opposite ruling without any addition or reduction. The example is the masḥ debate where Hanafi counters Shafi‘i by stating that masḥ is mustaḥab, not a rukn.
3
Analyze the second division
The objector adds a condition or qualification (ziyādah) that is an explanation (tafsīr). Example: saying 'after its completion' clarifies the scope of the ruling. Note the author’s problematization: this example may actually belong to qalb.
The author distinguishes between tafsīr (harmless) and taghyīr (change).
4
Trace the author’s correction
The author criticizes some commentators who split 'taghyīr' and the negation/proof into separate divisions. The correct view is that 'taghyīr' is a subcase of the second division, applicable to the third and fourth divisions as a state and restriction.
This highlights the importance of precise textual reading.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثانِى الْمُعَارَضَةُ الْخَالِصةُ عَنْ مَعْنَى الْمُنَاقَضَةِ وَيُسمَّى هَذَا فِي عُرُفِ الْمُنَاظِرَةِ مُعَارَضَةٌ بِالغَيْرِ وَهِيَ نَوْعَانِ أَحَدُهُمَا الْمُعَارَضَةً فِي حُكْمُ الفَرْع بان يَقُولُ الْمُعْتَرِضُ لَنَا دَلِيْلٌ يَدُلُّ عَلَى خِلافِ حُكْمِكَ فِي الْمَقِيسِ وَلَهُ خَمْسَةُ أَقْسامٍ كُلَّهَا صَحِيْحَةٌ مُسْتَعْمَلَةٌ فِي عِلْمٍ الأَصُولِ عَلى مَاقَالَ وَهُوَ صَحِيحٌ سَواءٌ عَارِضَةٌ بَصْدٌ ذَالِكَ الْحُكُم بِلازِيَادَةِ وَهذَا هُوَ الْقِسمُ الأَوَّلُ مِنْهَا وَذالك بأن يَذْكُرُ عِلْةٌ دَالَّةٌ عَلَى نَقِيض حُكم المُعَلَّلٍ صَرِيحًا بِلاَزِيَادَةٍ وَتُقْصَانِ نَظِيرُهُ مَا إِذَا قَالَ الشافعى الْمَسحُ رُكْنٌ فِي الْوَضَوْءِ فَيُسَنُ تَثْلِيةٌ كَالْغَسْلِ فَتَقُولُ الْمَسَحُ فِي الرَّاسِ مَستح فَلا يُسَنُ تَثْلِيْتُه كَمَسحِ الْخُفْ أَوْ بِزِيَادَةٍ هِيَ تَفْسِيرٌ وَهَذَا وَهُوَ الْقِسمُ الثَّانِي مِنْهَا ونظيره أَنْ نَقُولَ فِي الْمِثَال المذكور وقت الْمُعَارَةِ إِنَّ الْمَسَحَ رُكُن فِي الْوَضوء فَلا يُسَنُ تَثْلِيتُه بَعْدَ إِكْمَالِهِ فَقَوْلُنَا بَعْدَ إِكْمَالِهِ زِيَادَةٌ عَلَى قَدْرِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ وَلَكِنَّهُ تَفْسِيرُ لِلْمَقْصُودِ وَلكِنْ يُشكل أَنْ هَذَا الْمِثَالَ لَيْسَ لِلْمُعَارَضَةِ الْخَالِصة بَلْ لِلْقِسمُ الثَّانِي مِنَ الْقَلْبِ عَلى قَيَاسِ مَا قُلْنَا فِي مَسْألَةٍ صَوْمِ رَمَضَانَ بَعْدَ تَعَيِنِهِ وَلَمْ أَرَمتَالاً لِهَذَا الْقِسم مِنَ الْمُعَارَضَةِ الخَالِصة أن تَغْيِيْرٌ عَطَفٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ تَفْسِيرٌ أَيْ زِيَادَةٌ هِيَ تَغْيِيْرٌ وَقَدْ بَيْنَهُ لِقَوْلِهِ وَفَيْهِ نَفَى لِمَالَمْ يَثْبُتُهُ الأَول أَوْ إِثْبَات لِمَا لَمْ يَنْفِه الأوّلُ لَكِنْ تَحْتَهُ مُعَارَضَةٌ لِلأول فَهُوَ حَالٌ عَنْ قَوْلِهِ تَغْبِيرٌ وَقَيْدٌ لَهُ فَيَكُونُ مُسْتَمِلاً عَلى القِسم الثالث والرابع وهذا هُوَ الْحَقُّ وَقَدْ فَهِمَ بَعْضَ الشَّارِحِينَ إِنْ قَوْلَهُ أَوْتَغْسِيرُ وَقِسم ثالث وقَوْلُهُ أوْ فِيهِ تَفى لما لم يُثبته الأوّل أو إثْبَاتٌ لِمَا لَمْ يَنْفِه الأولُ بِكَلِمَةٍ أَوْ دُونَ الوَاءِ وَكُلُّ مِنْهُمَا قِسْمٌ رَابِعُ وَهَذا خَطَاءً فاحش نشأ مِنْ تَحْرِيفِ الْوَاءِ إِلَى أَوْ
The second is the pure counter-argument free from the meaning of contradiction, and in the terminology of disputation it is called mu'āraḍa bi al-ghayr (counter-argument by another). It is of two types. One of them is the counter-argument in the ruling of the branch, where the objector says: 'We have a proof that indicates the opposite of your ruling in the maqīs (the analogized branch).' It has five divisions, all of which are valid and used in the science of uṣūl according to what he said, and it is correct: whether the objection concerns that ruling without addition – this is the first division, and that is by mentioning a cause that explicitly indicates the opposite of the ruled-upon ruling without addition or reduction. Its example: when al-Shafi'i says: 'Masḥ (wiping) is a pillar in wuḍū', so its repetition three times is recommended like ghusl (washing).' Then you say: 'Masḥ on the head is recommended (mustaḥab), so its repetition three times is not recommended, like masḥ on the khuff.' Or with an addition that is an explanation – this is the second division. Its example: we say in the mentioned example at the time of counter-argument: 'Masḥ is a pillar in wuḍū', so its repetition three times is not recommended after its completion.' Our statement 'after its completion' is an addition beyond the measure of the counter-argument, but it is an explanation of the intended meaning. But it is problematic that this example is not for pure counter-argument but for the second type of qalb, analogous to what we said in the issue of fasting in Ramaḍān after its determination. And I have not seen an example for this division of pure counter-argument that is a change – this 'change' is an appositive to his statement 'explanation', i.e., an addition that is a change. He clarified it by his statement: 'In it, it negates what the first did not prove, or proves what the first did not negate.' But under it there is a counter-argument to the first, so it is a state (ḥāl) from his statement 'change' and a restriction for it, so it becomes applicable to the third and fourth divisions. This is the truth. Some commentators understood that his statement 'or a change' is a third division, and his statement 'or in it, it negates what the first did not prove, or proves what the first did not negate' with the word 'or' without the wāw, and each of them is a fourth division. This is a gross mistake arising from altering the wāw to 'or'.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage defines the second major type of counter-argument in Hanafi usul: mu'āraḍa khālisa (pure counter-argument), also known as mu'āraḍa bi al-ghayr (counter-argument by another proof). It is free from the meaning of contradiction (munāqaḍa). It has two types: (1) counter-argument in the ruling of the branch (al-far'), which itself has five divisions; (2) counter-argument in the cause (al-'illa), not covered here. The text focuses on the first type and its first two divisions. The first division is when the objector presents a cause (illah) that directly indicates the opposite of the opponent's ruling without any addition or reduction. The example: Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since wiping (masḥ) is a pillar in wuḍū', it should be recommended to do it three times, like washing (ghusl). The Hanafi objector responds by presenting a cause: wiping on the head is merely recommended (mustaḥab), not obligatory, so its threefold repetition is not recommended – analogizing to wiping on the khuff (leather socks), which is also recommended and not done three times. The second division is when the objector adds a condition or qualification (ziyādah) that is an explanation (tafsīr) of the intended meaning. The example: in response to al-Shafi'i, the objector says: after completing the wiping (i.e., with the intention of fulfilling the pillar), threefold repetition is not recommended. The addition 'after its completion' clarifies that the ruling applies only after the pillar is fulfilled. However, the author notes a problem: this example belongs to the second type of qalb, not pure counter-argument. The author then clarifies the terminology: 'change' (taghyīr) is an addition that modifies the opponent's ruling, and it is a subcategory of the second division. Some commentators mistakenly divided this into separate types, but the author corrects them, stating that the correct view is that 'change' applies to the third and fourth divisions of the first type.

Key Terms
المعارضة الخالصة (al-mu'āraḍa al-khālisa): A counter-argument that presents a different proof (dalil) against the ruling in the branch or the cause, without directly contradicting the opponent's proof.
الزيادة (al-ziyādah): An addition to the counter-argument that is either explanatory (tafsīr) or a change (taghyīr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first division of mu'āraḍa khālisa in the ruling of the branch?
A) The objector presents a cause that indicates the opposite of the opponent's ruling without any addition or reduction.
B) The objector adds a condition that changes the ruling completely.
C) The objector uses the opponent's own cause to derive the same ruling.
D) The objector rejects the analogy entirely.

Key Takeaway
Mu'āraḍa khālisa is a valid counter-argument in Hanafi usul where the objector presents a different proof (cause) to oppose the opponent's ruling, free from direct contradiction.

Types of Mu'arada with Ziyada in Hukm
Classifying mu'arada with addition in ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a counter-argument (mu'arada) that includes an addition (ziyada) as either tafsir (explanatory) or taghyir (changing) and identify the practical consequence in Hanafi-Shafi'i disputes.

Core Idea
A counter-argument with addition is valid in Hanafi usul—it either explains or changes the original ruling.

Understanding how the Hanafi school deals with counter-arguments in qiyas is essential for grasping the depth of legal reasoning. In this lesson, we examine a passage that classifies mu'arada that involves an addition to the ruling. We will see that such additions are not automatically rejected; they are categorized as either explanatory (tafsir) or changing (taghyir). By working through the examples—wiping in wudu, orphan girl’s guardianship, and the disbeliever’s purchase of a Muslim slave—you will learn how to identify and apply these distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of ziyada
The passage states that additions in mu'arada are either tafsir (explanatory) or taghyir (changing). Note the key phrases: 'أو زيادة هي تفسير' and 'أو تغيير'.
Tafsir clarifies without altering the ruling; taghyir introduces a change.
2
Analyze the first example: wiping in wudu
The Hanafi makes an analogy: wiping is a pillar, so tathlith is not sunna, like wiping over khuffs. This is a straightforward qiyas without addition. The passage introduces it as a base for the mu'arada types.
This example is referenced but not the main focus; it sets the stage for the counter-arguments.
3
Analyze the second example: orphan girl's guardianship
The Hanafi argues for general guardianship. The Shafi'i counters by adding 'by the brother', negating brother's guardianship via analogy to property. This addition is tafsir because it explains which guardianship is negated without changing the original claim.
The addition introduces a negation of something not originally asserted, but it is still a valid counter-argument.
4
Analyze the third example: disbeliever's purchase of Muslim slave
The Hanafi analogizes purchase to sale. The Shafi'i adds a distinction between initiation and continuation of ownership, claiming they must be equal. This addition is taghyir because it introduces a new condition that changes the ruling: purchase is invalidated.
The addition affirms equality between initiation and continuation, which was not negated in the original reasoning.
5
Summarize the usul rule
From these examples, the usul rule emerges: mu'arada with ziyada is valid and falls into two categories. The particular addition may negate or affirm something not in the original, but it still constitutes a valid counter-argument if it challenges the original analogy.
Hanafi usul accepts both types; Shafi'is may disagree on the validity of some additions, but the classification remains.

فَقَوْلُهُ أو زِيَادَةٌ هِيَ تَفْسِيرٌ: يَعْنِي مَعَارَضَةً بِزِيَادَةٍ هِيَ كَالتَّفْسِيرِ لِلْحُكْمِ. وَهَذَا هُوَ الْقِسْمُ الثَّانِي مِنْ أَقْسَامِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ فِي الْحُكْمِ. نَظِيرُهُ: مَا مَثَّلَ بِهِ الْمُصَنِّفُ فِي الْمَسْأَلَةِ السَّابِقَةِ، وَهُوَ قَوْلُنَا: الْمَسْحُ رُكْنٌ فِي الْوُضُوءِ، فَلِذَلِكَ لا يُسَنُّ التَّثْلِيثُ فِيهِ، كَالْمَسْحِ عَلَى الْخُفَّيْنِ.

قَوْلُهُ أو تَغْيِيرٌ: وَهُوَ الْقِسْمُ الثَّالِثُ، وَفِيهِ نَفْيٌ لِمَا لَمْ يُثْبِتْهُ الأَوَّلُ أَوْ إِثْبَاتٌ لِمَا لَمْ يَنْفِهِ الأَوَّلُ، لَكِنْ تَحْتَهُ مُعَارَضَةٌ لِلأَوَّلِ. نَظِيرُ الْقِسْمِ الثَّالِثِ: قَوْلُنَا فِي الْيَتِيمَةِ إِنَّهَا صَغِيرَةٌ يُولَى عَلَيْهَا بِوِلاَيَةِ الأَنْكَاحِ كَالَّتِي لَهَا أَبٌ. فَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ: هَذِهِ صَغِيرَةٌ فَلا يُولَى عَلَيْهَا بِوِلاَيَةِ الأَخَوَةِ، قِيَاسًا عَلَى الْمَالِ، إِذْ لا وِلاَيَةَ لِلأَخِ عَلَى مَالِ الصَّغِيرَةِ بِالاِتِّفَاقِ. فَهَذِهِ مُعَارَضَةٌ بِزِيَادَةٍ هِيَ تَفْسِيرٌ، وَفِيهَا نَفْيٌ لِمَا لَمْ يُثْبِتْهُ الأَوَّلُ، لأَنَّا مَا أَثْبَتْنَا فِي التَّعْلِيلِ وِلاَيَةَ الأَخَوَةِ بَلْ مُطْلَقَ الْوِلاَيَةِ، حَتَّى يَنْفِيَ الْمُعَارِضُ إِيَّاهَا. وَلَكِنْ تَحْتَهُ مُعَارَضَةٌ لِلأَوَّلِ، لأَنَّهُ إِذَا انْتَفَتْ وِلاَيَةُ الأَخَوَةِ انْتَفَى سَائِرُهَا، إِذْ لا قَائِلَ بِالْفَصْلِ بَيْنَ الأَخِ وَغَيْرِهِ.

نَظِيرُ الْقِسْمِ الرَّابِعِ: قَوْلُنَا إِنَّ الْكَافِرَ يَمْلِكُ شِرَاءَ الْعَبْدِ الْمُسْلِمِ لأَنَّهُ يَمْلِكُ بَيْعَهُ، فَيَمْلِكُ شِرَاءَهُ كَالْمُسْلِمِ. فَعَارَضَهُ أَصْحَابُ الشَّافِعِيِّ وَقَالُوا: إِنَّ الْكَافِرَ لَمَّا مَلَكَ بَيْعَهُ وَجَبَ أَنْ يَسْتَوِيَ فِيهِ ابْتِدَاءُ الْمِلْكِ وَبَقَاؤُهُ كَالْمُسْلِمِ، لَكِنَّهُ لا يَمْلِكُ الْقَرَارَ عَلَيْهِ شَرْعًا، بَلْ يُجْبَرُ عَلَى إِخْرَاجِهِ عَنْ مِلْكِهِ، فَكَذَلِكَ لا يَمْلِكُ ابْتِدَاءَ مِلْكِهِ. فَفِي هَذِهِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ تَغْيِيرٌ وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ: وَجَبَ أَنْ يَسْتَوِيَ. وَفِيهِ إِثْبَاتٌ لِمَا لَمْ يَنْفِهِ الأَوَّلُ، لأَنَّا مَا نَفَيْنَا الاسْتِوَاءَ بَيْنَ الابْتِدَاءِ وَالْبَقَاءِ فِي التَّعْلِيلِ حَتَّى يُثْبِتَهُ الْخَصْمُ فِي الْمُعَارَضَةِ، وَإِنَّمَا أَثْبَتْنَا الاسْتِوَاءَ بَيْنَ الْبَيْعِ وَالشِّرَاءِ. وَلَكِنْ تَحْتَهُ مُعَارَضَةٌ لِلأَوَّلِ، لأَنَّهُ إِذَا أَثْبَتَ الاسْتِوَاءَ بَيْنَ الابْتِدَاءِ وَالْبَقَاءِ ظَهَرَتِ الْمُفَارَقَةُ بَيْنَ الْبَيْعِ وَالشِّرَاءِ، فَيَصِحُّ الْبَيْعُ دُونَ الشِّرَاءِ لأَنَّهُ يُوجِبُ الْمِلْكَ ابْتِدَاءً، فَيَنْدَفِعُ مَوْضِعُ النِّزَاعِ مِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ.
His statement 'or an addition that is explanatory': i.e., a counter-argument with an addition that is like an explanation of the ruling. This is the second type of counter-argument in the ruling. Its example is what the author gave in the previous issue, namely our statement: 'Wiping is a pillar in ablution, therefore repeating it three times is not recommended, like wiping over the khuffs.'

His statement 'or a change': and this is the third type, and in it is a negation of what the first did not affirm or an affirmation of what the first did not negate, but under it is a counter-argument to the first. The example of the third type: our statement concerning the orphan girl: 'She is a minor, her marriage guardianship is exercised like one who has a father.' So al-Shafi'i said: 'She is a minor, so she is not subject to guardianship of the brother, by analogy to property, since there is no guardianship for the brother over the minor's property by consensus.' So this is a counter-argument with an addition that is explanatory, and in it is a negation of what the first did not affirm, because we did not affirm in the reasoning the guardianship of the brother, but rather absolute guardianship, so that the opponent negates it. But under it is a counter-argument to the first, because if the guardianship of the brother is negated, then all other guardianship is negated, since no one distinguishes between a brother and others.

The example of the fourth type: our statement that the disbeliever owns the purchase of the Muslim slave because he owns his sale, so he owns his purchase like a Muslim. So the followers of al-Shafi'i countered and said: 'Since the disbeliever owns his sale, it is necessary that the initiation and continuation of ownership be equal in it, like a Muslim, but he does not own permanent ownership over it legally, rather he is compelled to remove it from his ownership, so likewise he does not own initiation of ownership.' So in this counter-argument there is a change, i.e., his statement 'it is necessary that they be equal', and in it is an affirmation of what the first did not negate, because we did not negate equality between initiation and continuation in the reasoning such that the opponent affirms it in the counter-argument; rather we affirmed equality between sale and purchase. But under it is a counter-argument to the first, because when he affirms equality between initiation and continuation, the difference between sale and purchase becomes apparent, so sale is valid without purchase because it initiates ownership, thus the point of dispute is removed from this aspect.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the types of mu'arada (counter-argument) that involve an addition (ziyada) to the original ruling. The commentator distinguishes three subtypes: (1) addition that is explanatory (tafsir), (2) addition that changes (taghyir) the ruling, and (3) an addition that implies negation or affirmation of something not originally claimed. The text provides examples from actual Hanafi-Shafi'i disputes to illustrate each. The first subtype (addition as explanation) is shown in the wiping in ablution example: the Hanafi says wiping is a pillar, therefore tathlith (three times) is not sunna, analogizing to wiping over khuffs. The second subtype (addition that changes) is exemplified by the orphan girl's guardianship: the Hanafi claims general guardianship, the Shafi'i responds by specifying the brother's guardianship is negated by analogy to property. The third subtype involves an addition that reverses the ruling, as in the case of a disbeliever purchasing a Muslim slave: the Hanafi analogizes purchase to sale, but the Shafi'i introduces a distinction between initiation and continuation of ownership, thereby changing the ruling. The commentator notes that the added statement often contains a negation or affirmation not present in the original reasoning, but still results in a valid counter-argument. This analysis follows the Hanafi usul framework for evaluating qiyas objections.

Key Terms
معارضة (mu'arada): A counter-argument against the 'illah or hukm in qiyas, showing inconsistency or providing a competing analogy.
زيادة (ziyada): An addition to the original ruling that either explains it (tafsir) or changes it (taghyir).
تفسير (tafsir): An addition that clarifies or explains the original ruling without contradicting it.
تغيير (taghyir): An addition that changes the original ruling, effectively replacing it with a new one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of the orphan girl's guardianship, what type of addition does the Shafi'i counter-argument contain?
A) An addition that is tafsir (explanatory)
B) An addition that is taghyir (changing)
C) An addition that is negation of the original
D) An addition that is irrelevant

Key Takeaway
Mu'arada with ziyada is a valid counter-argument in Hanafi usul; it is either tafsir or taghyir, depending on whether it explains or changes the original ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
The Fifth Type of Mu'arada: Indirect Negation in Qiyas
Definition and example of indirect mu'arada with tarjih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fifth type of mu'arada and apply the Hanafi rules of tarjih when a valid bed conflicts with a defective one.

Core Idea
Indirect negation: objecting by establishing a different ruling that logically negates the original.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, mu'arada (objection) in qiyas is not always a direct attack on the original ruling. The fifth type involves bringing an alternative ruling that, once established, necessarily negates the first. This lesson unpacks this subtle form of objection through Imam Abu Hanifa's famous example of a woman whose deceased husband returns after she remarries. You will learn how the child's lineage is resolved by tarjih between a valid bed (firash sahih) and a defective one (firash fasid).

Guided Path
1
State the definition of the fifth mu'arada
Read the opening lines: the objector does not attack the original ruling directly, but brings a different ruling that implies its negation.
Key phrase: 'في حكم غير الأول لكن فيه نفي الأول'.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's example
Identify the facts: a woman hears of her husband's death, marries another, has a child, then the first husband returns. Abu Hanifa rules the child belongs to the first husband (valid bed).
The original ruling is: child goes to first husband.
3
Construct the objector's counter-analogy
The objector argues: the second husband has a defective bed, and by analogy with a marriage without witnesses (where lineage is established), the child should be his. This is not a direct negation but an indirect one.
This is the fifth type: objector establishes a different ruling (child to second husband) that indirectly negates the first.
4
Apply tarjih between the two rulings
Both rulings cannot stand (a child has one father). The Hanafi response: a valid bed (reality) outweighs a defective bed (doubt). The objector's counter-argument (presence and biological material) is weaker.
Tarjih resolves the conflict: validity > presence.
5
Extract the usul principle
The principle: when two analogies conflict, the one based on a stronger illa (validity vs doubt) prevails. Ownership and soundness of the marriage bed take precedence over physical presence.
This illustrates the hierarchy of proofs in Hanafi usul.

أَوْ فِي حُكْم غَيْرِ الأَوْلِ لَكِنْ فِيْهِ نَفى الأَوْلِ عَطَفٌ عَلَى قَوْلِهِ بِضَدُ ذَالِكَ الْحُكْمِ أَنْ لَمْ يُعَارِضة بعيد الحكم الأولِ بِلْ يُعَارِضَهُ فِي حُكْم آخَرَ غَيْرَ الْأَوْلِ لَكِنْ فِيْهِ نَفَى الأَوْلِ وَهَذَا هُوَ القِسْسْمُ الخَامِسَ مِنْهَا نَظِيرُهُ مَا قَالَ أَبُو حَنَيْفَة فِي الْمَرْأَةِ الَّتِي تُعِي إِلَيْهَا نَعْيُ زَوْجِهَا أَى أُخْبِرَتْ بِمَوْتِهِ فَاعْتَدَتْ وَتَزَوَّجَتْ بِزَوْجٍ آخَرَ فَجَاءَتْ بِوَلَدٍ ثُمَّ جَاءَ الزَّوْجُ الأَوَّلُ حَيًّا إِنَّ الْوَلَدَ لِلزَّوْجِ الأَوَّلِ لأَنَّهُ صَاحِبُ فِرَاشٍ صَحِيحٍ بِقِيَامِ النِّكَاحِ بَيْنَهُمَا فَإِنْ عَارَضَهُ الْخَصْمُ بِأَنَّ الثَّانِى صَاحِبُ فِرَاشٍ فَاسِدٍ فَيَسْتَوْجِبُ بِهِ النَّسَبَ كَمَا لَوْ تَزَوَّجَتِ امْرَأَةٌ بِغَيْرِ شُهُودٍ وَوَلَدَتْ مِنْهُ يَثْبُتُ النَّسَبُ مِنْهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ الْفَرَاشُ فَاسِدًا فَهَذِهِ الْمُعَارَضَةُ لَمْ تَكُنْ لِنَفْيِ النَّسَبِ عَنِ الأَوَّلِ بَلْ لِإِثْبَاتِ النَّسَبِ مِنَ الثَّانِى لَكِنْ فِيهَا نَفْيُ الأَوَّلِ لأَنَّهُ إِذَا ثَبَتَ مِنَ الثَّانِي يَنْتَفِى عَنِ الأَوَّلِ لِعَدَمِ تَصَوُّرِ النَّسَبِ مِنْ شَخْصَيْنِ فَيَحْتَاجُ حِينَئِذٍ إِلَى التَّرْجِيْحِ فَنَقُولُ الْأَوَّلُ صَاحِبُ فِرَاشٍ صَحِيحٍ وَالثَّانِى صَاحِبُ فِرَاشٍ فَاسِدٍ وَالصَّحِيحُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْفَاسِدِ فَيُعَارِضُ الْخَصْمُ بِأَنَّ الثَّانِيَ حَاضِرٌ وَالْمَاءُ مَاؤُهُ وَهُوَ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْغَائِبِ فَيَظْهَرْ حِينَئِذٍ فِقْهُ الْمَسْأَلَةِ وَهُوَ أَنَّ الْمِلْكَ وَالصِّحَّةَ أَحَقُّ بِالاعْتِبَارِ مِنَ الْحَضْرَةِ وَالْمَاءِ فَإِنَّ الْقَاسِدَ يُوجِبُ الشُّبْهَةَ وَالصَّحِيحُ يُوجِبُ الْحَقيقَةَ وَالْحَقيقَةُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الشُّبْهَةِ.
أَوْفِي حُكْمِ غَيْرِ الأَوَّلِ لَكِنْ فِيْهِ نَفْى الاول یا ایسے حکم میں جو کہ حکم اول کا غیر ہو لیکن اس ترجمہ تشریح سے اولی کی تھی ہوئی ہو منصف کے سابق قول " بضد ذالك الحكم " پر اس جملہ کا عطف ہے اور مطلب یہ ہے کہ معترض حکم اول کی ضد سے معارضہ کرے بلکہ کسی دوسرے علم سے معارضہ کرے جو محکم اول کے ماسواہ ہو لیکن اس حکم میں عظیم اول کی نفی ثابت ہوتی ہو یہ معارضه في الحکم پانچویں صورت ہے اس کی نظیر امام ابو حنفیہ کا وہ قول ہے جو انھوں نے ایک عورت کے بارے میں فرمایا تھا وہ عورت جس کو اپنے شوہر کے مرجانے کی خبر پہونچی تو اس نے عدت کے دن پورے کر لئے اس کے بعد اس عورت نے دوسرے سے شادی کرلی۔ پس اس شوہر ثانی سے ایک لڑکا بھی پید ا ہو گیا اس کے بعد زوج اول زندہ گھر پہونچ کیا صورت مذکورہ میں امام صاحب نے فرمایا تھا کہ یہ لڑکا (جو دوسرے نکاح کے بعد زوج جانی کے یہاں پیدا ہوا) زوج اول کا ہے کیونکہ وہی صحیح صاحب فراش ہے کہ نکہ میاں بیوی کے درمیان نکاح قائم ہے۔ اب اگر کوئی شخص اس پر معارضہ کرے کہ زوج تانی صاحب فراش فاسدہ ہے اس سے بھی وہ نسب کا مستحق ہو گا اور اس پر قیاس کرے کہ جس طرح اگر کوئی عورت بغیر گواہوں کی موجودگی کے اپنا نکاح کسی شخص سے کرلے اور اس سے لڑکا پیدا ہو تو اس لڑکے کا نسب اسی شوہر سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اگر چہ یہ شوہر صاحب (مالک) فراش فاسد ہے تو یہ معارضہ نسب اول کی نفی پر قائم نہیں ہے بلکہ ثانی شوہر سے نسب ثابت کرنے کے لئے ہے البتہ اس سے اول کی نسب کی نفی ثابت ہو جاتی ہے کیو نکہ جب بچہ کا نسب زوج ثانی سے ثابت ہو جائے گا تو اول زوج سے خود نفی ہو جائیگی کیونکہ ایک بچہ کا نسب دو مردوں سے ثابت نہیں ہوا کرتا ہے لہذا اس میں ترجیح کی احتیاج ہو گی۔ فَتَقُولُ الأول صاحب فراش صحيح :- پس ہم کہتے ہیں کہ زوج اول صاحب فراش صحیح ہے اور دوسرا شوہر صاحب فراش فاسد ہے اور صحیح اولی اور بہتر ہوا کرتا ہے بمقابلہ فاسد کے پس اس تخصم معارضہ کرے۔ زوج ثانی موجود ہے اور بائی (منی) بھی اس کی ہے درانحالیکہ وہ شوہر غائب (غیر موجود) کے مقابلے میں اولی ہے اب ان دونوں ترجیحات کے بعد ایک فقہی مسئلہ نمایاں ہو گیا اور وہ یہ ہے کہ ملکیت نکاح اور صاحب فراش کا صحیح ہو نا زیادہ بہتر ہے بمقابلہ موجود شوہر اور اس کے پانی (منی) کے کیونکہ فاسد شبہ پیدا کرتا ہے اور صحیح حقیقت کو واضح کرتا ہے اور حقیقت اولی ہوتی ہے بمقابلہ شبہ کے۔
Or in a ruling other than the first, but wherein there is negation of the first. This is conjunction to his statement 'contrary to that ruling' that he does not object by opposing the first ruling, but rather he objects in another ruling other than the first, but in it there is negation of the first. And this is the fifth type. Its example is what Abu Hanifa said regarding the woman who receives news of her husband's death, so she observes iddah and marries another husband, then gives birth to a child, then the first husband comes alive: the child belongs to the first husband because he is the owner of a valid bed, due to the marriage between them being intact. If the opponent objects that the second is the owner of a defective bed, and thus he deserves lineage through it, just as if a woman marries without witnesses and gives birth from him, lineage is established despite the defective bed—this objection is not to negate lineage from the first, but to establish lineage from the second; however, in it there is negation of the first, because if lineage is established from the second, it is negated from the first due to impossibility of lineage from two persons. So then preference is needed. We say: the first is owner of a valid bed, the second is owner of a defective bed, and valid is better than defective. Then the opponent objects that the second is present and his water belongs to him, and he is better than the absent one. Then the fiqh of the matter becomes clear: that ownership and validity are more deserving of consideration than presence and water, for the defective causes doubt and the valid causes reality, and reality is better than doubt. [Then Urdu commentary follows.]
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage explains the fifth type of mu'arada (objection) in qiyas, as part of a classification of objections. The author first states the definition: the objector does not directly attack the original ruling but instead brings up a different ruling that indirectly implies the negation of the original. He then provides a famous example from Imam Abu Hanifa: a woman is informed of her husband's death, completes her iddah, marries another man, and has a child. The first husband then returns alive. Abu Hanifa rules that the child belongs to the first husband because the marriage between them is still valid (valid bed, firash sahih). An objector might argue that the second husband also has a defective bed (firash fasid) and, by analogy with a marriage without witnesses (which establishes lineage despite defective bed), the child's lineage should be from the second husband. The author clarifies that this objection does not directly negate the first husband's claim; rather, it seeks to establish lineage from the second, which necessarily negates the first (since a child can have only one father). This necessitates tarjih (preference). The Hanafi response is that the valid bed takes precedence over the defective one because validity (reality) outweighs doubt. The objector's counterargument (that the second husband is present and his sperm is used) is overridden by the strength of the valid marriage. The lesson concludes that ownership and soundness are more significant than mere presence and physical elements.

Key Terms
مُعَارَضَة (mu'arada): An objection in qiyas where the opponent brings a counter-daleel or analogy to challenge the original ruling.
فِرَاش صَحِيح (firash sahih): A valid marriage bed that establishes lineage and inheritance.
تَرْجِيح (tarjih): The process of giving preference to one proof over another when they conflict.
نفي الأول (nafi al-awwal): Negation of the first ruling, which occurs indirectly when establishing another ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key characteristic of the fifth type of mu'arada?
A) The objector directly negates the original ruling.
B) The objector brings a different ruling that indirectly implies negation of the original.
C) The objector denies the existence of the original analogy.
D) The objector accepts the original ruling but adds an exception.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, indirect negation (the fifth type of mu'arada) requires tarjih between the original and the alternative ruling, and the valid bed (reality) prevails over the defective one (doubt).

Mu'arada fi al-Hukm: The Case of the Woman and Her Husbands
Presents fifth type of mu'arada fi al-hukm with a concrete example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a flawed mu'arada fi al-hukm and apply the Hanafi tarjih principle to resolve conflicting claims of lineage.

Core Idea
A valid counter-argument must directly negate the original ruling; indirect negation requires tarjih, where valid marriage outweighs defective marriage.

Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on a woman who remarried after her husband's apparent death presents a classic case of mu'arada fi al-hukm. An objector might argue that the second husband's presence and biological paternity should determine lineage. This lesson unpacks why such a counter-argument fails under Hanafi usul, teaching you how to critically evaluate objections and apply tarjih (preference) correctly.

Guided Path
1
Understand the factual scenario
Read the case: a woman receives news of her husband's death, completes 'idda, marries another man, and bears a son. Then the first husband returns alive. Identify the legal question: to whom does the child belong?
The child's lineage is at stake; both husbands have a claim.
2
Identify Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling and its basis
Imam Abu Hanifa ruled the child belongs to the first husband. His dalil: the first husband is the sahib al-firash al-sahih (valid marriage bed owner) because the nikah sahih remains intact. The second marriage was done without certainty of the first husband's death, making it fasid (defective).
Valid marriage (sahih) takes precedence over defective (fasid) in establishing firash.
3
Analyse the objector's qiyas
The objector argues: the second husband is present and his semen led to the child, just as in a marriage without witnesses, the child's lineage is attributed to the husband despite the marriage being fasid. They claim this establishes lineage from the second husband, indirectly negating the first.
This qiyas is an attempt at mu'arada fi al-hukm because it presents a ruling (lineage from second husband) that conflicts with the original ruling (lineage from first husband).
4
Evaluate why the counter-argument fails and apply tarjih
The objector's ruling does not directly negate the first ruling; it only establishes a second ruling that indirectly causes negation. Since direct negation is required for valid mu'arada, this is insufficient. Moreover, tarjih is needed: the first husband's firash is sahih (valid) while the second is fasid (defective). The sahih is stronger than the fasid. Also, the first husband's marriage subsisted, so his right is prior. Even though the second husband is present and his semen used, the valid marriage outweighs these factors.
Thus the objector's mu'arada is invalid; the original ruling stands.

Source Text

أَوْفِي حُكْمِ غَيْرِ الأَوَّلِ لَكِنْ فِيْهِ نَفْى الاول یا ایسے حکم میں جو کہ حکم اول کا غیر ہو لیکن اس ترجمہ تشریح سے اولی کی تھی ہوئی ہو منصف کے سابق قول " بضد ذالك الحكم " پر اس جملہ کا عطف ہے اور مطلب یہ ہے کہ معترض حکم اول کی ضد سے معارضہ کرے بلکہ کسی دوسرے علم سے معارضہ کرے جو محکم اول کے ماسواہ ہو لیکن اس حکم میں عظیم اول کی نفی ثابت ہوتی ہو یہ معارضه في الحکم پانچویں صورت ہے اس کی نظیر امام ابو حنفیہ کا وہ قول ہے جو انھوں نے ایک عورت کے بارے میں فرمایا تھا وہ عورت جس کو اپنے شوہر کے مرجانے کی خبر پہونچی تو اس نے عدت کے دن پورے کر لئے اس کے بعد اس عورت نے دوسرے سے شادی کرلی۔ پس اس شوہر ثانی سے ایک لڑکا بھی پید ا ہو گیا اس کے بعد زوج اول زندہ گھر پہونچ کیا صورت مذکورہ میں امام صاحب نے فرمایا تھا کہ یہ لڑکا (جو دوسرے نکاح کے بعد زوج جانی کے یہاں پیدا ہوا) زوج اول کا ہے کیونکہ وہی صحیح صاحب فراش ہے کہ نکہ میاں بیوی کے درمیان نکاح قائم ہے۔ اب اگر کوئی شخص اس پر معارضہ کرے کہ زوج تانی صاحب فراش فاسدہ ہے اس سے بھی وہ نسب کا مستحق ہو گا اور اس پر قیاس کرے کہ جس طرح اگر کوئی عورت بغیر گواہوں کی موجودگی کے اپنا نکاح کسی شخص سے کرلے اور اس سے لڑکا پیدا ہو تو اس لڑکے کا نسب اسی شوہر سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اگر چہ یہ شوہر صاحب (مالک) فراش فاسد ہے تو یہ معارضہ نسب اول کی نفی پر قائم نہیں ہے بلکہ ثانی شوہر سے نسب ثابت کرنے کے لئے ہے البتہ اس سے اول کی نسب کی نفی ثابت ہو جاتی ہے کیو نکہ جب بچہ کا نسب زوج ثانی سے ثابت ہو جائے گا تو اول زوج سے خود نفی ہو جائیگی کیونکہ ایک بچہ کا نسب دو مردوں سے ثابت نہیں ہوا کرتا ہے لہذا اس میں ترجیح کی احتیاج ہو گی۔ فَتَقُولُ الأول صاحب فراش صحيح :- پس ہم کہتے ہیں کہ زوج اول صاحب فراش صحیح ہے اور دوسرا شوہر صاحب فراش فاسد ہے اور صحیح اولی اور بہتر نمایاں ہو گیا اور وہ یہ ہے کہ ملکیت نکاح اور صاحب فراش کا صحیح ہو نا زیادہ بہتر ہے بمقابلہ موجود شوہر اور اس کے پانی (منی) کے کیونکہ فاسد شبہ پیدا کرتا ہے اور صحیح حقیقت کو واضح کرتا ہے اور حقیقت اولی ہوتی ہے بمقابلہ شبہ کے۔
Or in the ruling of other than the first, but in it is negation of the first, that is, a ruling that is other than the first ruling but in this translation explanation the first is confirmed. The author's previous statement 'opposite of that ruling' is the attachment of this sentence, and the meaning is that the objector should counter the first ruling with its opposite, rather counter with another knowledge that is other than the first ruling, but in this ruling the negation of the first is proven. This is the fifth form of mu'arada fi al-hukm. Its example is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa about a woman: she received news of her husband's death, completed her 'idda, then married another man. She gave birth to a son from the second husband. Then the first husband returned alive. In this case, Imam Abu Hanifa ruled that the child (born after the second marriage) belongs to the first husband, because he is the valid owner of the marriage bed (sahih firash) since the marriage between them is still valid. Now if someone objects that the second husband is a defective owner of the marriage bed (fasid firash) and he too is entitled to lineage, and makes qiyas: just as if a woman marries without witnesses and gives birth, the child is attributed to that husband even though he is a defective owner of the marriage bed. This objection is not based on negating the first lineage, but rather on establishing lineage from the second husband. However, it does negate the first lineage because when the child's lineage is established from the second husband, it is automatically negated from the first, since a child cannot have lineage from two men. Therefore, a preference (tarjih) is needed. So we say: the first husband is the valid owner of the marriage bed, and the second is defective. The valid is stronger and better than the defective. So this is an invalid counter. The second husband is present and his semen is also his, while the first husband is absent (non-existent) in comparison, he is stronger. After these two preferences, a fiqh issue emerges: that ownership of marriage and validity of firash is stronger than present husband and his semen, because the defective creates doubt (shubha) while the valid clarifies reality, and reality is stronger than doubt.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage explains the fifth type of mu'arada fi al-hukm (counter-argument in the ruling). The author presents a concrete example from Imam Abu Hanifa's fatwa regarding a woman who remarried after her husband's presumed death, then the original husband returned. Imam Abu Hanifa attributed the child to the first husband based on the priority of a valid marriage (nikah sahih) over a defective one (nikah fasid). The hypothetical objector uses qiyas to argue that the second husband, being present and the biological father, should also be considered. However, this counter-argument is invalid because it does not directly negate the first ruling; rather, it establishes a second ruling that indirectly negates the first. The passage then explains why the first husband's claim is stronger: his marriage is valid, and valid marriage is superior to defective marriage. Even though the second husband is present and his semen is used, the first husband's marriage rights take precedence. This illustrates the concept of tarjih (preference) in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
معارضة في الحكم (mu'arada fi al-hukm): Counter-argument in the ruling, where the objector presents a ruling from another source that negates the original ruling.
صاحب فراش (sahib al-firash): The husband who is legally considered the owner of the bed (right to paternity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that a valid marriage bed (sahih firash) takes precedence over a defective one (fasid firash) resolves conflicting claims in mu'arada fi al-hukm.

Three Types of Mu'arada fi al-Illa
Classifies three forms of mu'arada fi al-illa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify the three types of mu'arada fi al-illa according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Mu'arada fi al-illa has three subtypes; all are invalid because they fail to negate the ruling.

In this lesson, we examine the second major category of mu'arada: counter-argument in the cause itself. The author classifies three subtypes based on the transitivity of the claimed cause: non-transitive, transitive to a consensus branch, and transitive to a disputed branch. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for properly assessing qiyas arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three subtypes
List the three types: ghayr muta'addi, muta'addi to a mujma' alayh branch, and muta'addi to a mukhtalaf fih branch.
This classification is based on whether the objector's cause extends beyond the original case.
2
Examine each example
For each subtype, note the example given: iron with thamaniyya (first), plaster with ifta'at and iddikhar (second), plaster with ta'm (third).
These examples are drawn from Hanafi discussions on sales of weighed and measured items.
3
Understand the structure
Observe that the objector proposes a different cause that is claimed not to apply to the branch in question.
This is a challenge to the mu'allil's analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالثَّانِي فِي عِلة الأصل (۳) اور معارضہ کی دوسری قسم اصل کی علت میں یعنی معارضہ خالصہ کی دوسری قسم وہ معارضہ ہے جو کہ مقیس علیہ کی علت ہو بایں طور کہ معارض یوں کہے کہ میرے پاس ایسی دلیل ہے جو انس بات پر دلالت کرتی ہے کہ حکم مقیس علیہ میں طلبہ (وہ نہیں ہے جس کو تم نے غلط قرار دی ہے) بلکہ علت دوسری چیز ہے جو فروع میں نہیں پائی جاتی اس کی تین قسمیں ہیں اور مینوں باطل ہیں جیسا کہ مصنف ماتن نے بیان فرمایا ہے۔ وذَالِكَ بَاطِلٌ سَوَاءٌ كَانَتْ بِمَعْنى لا يَتَعَدَى هَذَا هُوَ الْقِسمُ الأول كَمَا إذا عَلَلْنَا بَيْعِ الْحَديد بأنه مَوْزَوْنَ قَويل بجنسه فَلا يَجوز بيعة مُتَفَاضِلا كَذهَب وَالْفِضة

فيما رهنة السائل بِأَنَّ الْعِلَّةَ عِنْدَنَا فِي الأَصْلِ فِى الثَّمَنِيَةُ وَتِلْكَ لا تَتَعَدَّى إلى الْحَدِيدِ أَوْ يَتَعَدى إلى قَرْعٍ مُجْمَعِ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ الْقِسمُ الثَّانِي كَمَا إِذَا عَلَلْنَا فِي حُرْمَةِ بَيْعِ الْجَمَ بِجنسه مُتَفَاضِلاً بِالْكَيْلِ وَالْجِنْسِ كَالْحِنْطَة والشعير فَيُعَارِضة السائِلُ بِأَنَّ الْعِلَّةَ فِي الأَصْلِ لَيْسَت ماقلت بَلْ فِى الأَفْتِيَاتِ والإنْخَار وَهُوَ مَعْدُوم فى الحصن وَإِنْ كَانَ يَتَعَدَّى إِلَى قَرْعٍ مُجْمِع عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ الرز وَالدَّخَنُ أوْ مُخْتَلِفٌ فِيْهِ أَنْ يَتَّعَدَى إِلى فَرْع مُختلِف فِيهِ وَهُوَ القِسم الثالث مِثَالُهُ مَالَوْ عَارِضَ السَّائِلُ فِي الْمَسْأَلَةِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ بأن العلة في الأصل هو الطَّعْمُ وَلَمْ يَوْجَدْ فِى الْجَصَ وَهُوَ يَتَعَدُّى إلى فرع مُختلِف فِيهِ أَعْنِي الْفَوَاكِهِ وَمَا دُوْنَ الْكِيْلِ وَهَذِهِ الأَقْسَامُ كُلْهَا بَاطِلَةٌ لأَنْ الْوَصَفَ الَّذِي يَدْعِيْهِ السَّائِلُ لأينَافِى الْوَصَفَ الَّذِئ يَدْعِيْهِ عَلَةٍ الْمُعَلِّلِ إِذَا اظْلَمَ يَثْبُتُ بِعِلل شتى فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُن وَصفة مُتعدِّيًا فَفَسَادُهُ ظَاهِرٌ لأَن المَقْصُودُ بِالتَّعْلِيلِ التَّفْدِيَةُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُتَعَدِّيَا كَانَ الْمُعَارَضَةُ أَيْضًا فَاسِدَةٌ لانها لاتعلقَ لَهَا بِالْمُتَنَازِعَ فِيهِ إِلا أَنَّهَا تُفِيدَ عَدَمَ تِلكَ العِلْةِ فِيهِ وَهُوَ لا يُوجِبُ عَدَمَ الْحُكْمِ وَكُلُّ كَلام صَحِيحَةٍ فِي الأَصل أَيْ فِي أَصْلِ وَضْعِهِ وَجَوْهَرِهِ وَلَكِنْ يُذكرُهُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الْمُفَارَقَةِ التي هي بَاطِلَةٌ عِنْدَ اهْلِ الأَصُولِ فَاذْكُرُهُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الْمُمَانَعَةِ لِيَخْرُجَ مِنْ حَيْرِ الْفَسَادِ إلى خَيْرُ الصَّحَةِ وَيَكُونُ مَقْبُولاً بأصلِه وَوَصعَه مَعا .
ترجم و تشریح وذالك بناطيل الخ : اور معارضہ کی یہ نوع باطل ہے خواہ اسی علت سے معارضہ کیا جائے جو متعدی نہ ہو یہ مُعارضه في العلة کی پہلی قسم ہے جیسے لوہے کی بیع لوہے کے بدلے کرنے کے سلسلے میں ہم دلیل پیش کریں کہ لوہا موزونی چیز ہے جو ایک موزونی چیز کے بدلے میں بیچا جا رہا ہے لہذ ا تفاضل سے بیع جائز نہیں ہے جیسے سونا اور چاندی میں تو اس استدلال پر سائل معترضین معارضہ کرے کہ اصل میں علت ہمارے نزد یک تعنیت ہے اور ثمنیت حدید (لوہے) میں نہیں پائی جاتی۔ أوْ يَتعدى إلى فرع مُجْمَع عَلَيْهِ - (۲) یا متعدی ہو اس فرع کی طرف سے جس کے حکم پر اتفاق ہو معارضه فى العلة کی یہ دوسری قسم ہے جیسے ہم استدلال کریں کہ جص (چون ) کی بیع جس کے بدلے میں متفاضل کیل اور جنس کے متحد ہونے کی وجہ سے حرام ہے جس طرح خطہ اور شعیر کی بیج اتحاد کیل و جنس کیوجہ سے متفاضلا حرام ہے تو اس پر مخالف معارفہ کرے کہ اصل میں علت وہ نہیں ہے جو تم نے بیان کی ہے بلکہ علیہ اختیات (قوت کے قابل ہونا) اور از دخار (جسکو بطور ذخیرہ جمع کیا جا سکے ) ہے اور یہ علت جبھی میں نہیں پائی جاتی
And the second is in the cause of the original: this is the second type of mu'arada, which is counter-argument in the cause of the analogized original. It is such that the objector says: I have evidence indicating that the ruling in the original case is not what you claimed, but rather the cause is another attribute that is not found in the branches. It has three subtypes, and all are invalid, as the author of the matn stated. And that is invalid, whether the claimed cause is non-transitive. This is the first subtype: as if we offer an analogy for the sale of iron stating that it is a weighed commodity sold for its own kind, so it is not permissible to sell it with excess, like gold and silver. Then the objector counters: the cause in the original according to us is the property of being a price (thamaniyya), and that does not apply to iron. Or if it is transitive to a branch upon which there is consensus, that is the second subtype: as if we offer an analogy for the prohibition of selling plaster (jiss) for its kind with excess, based on measure and kind, like wheat and barley. Then the objector counters: the cause in the original is not what you said, but rather it is the potential to be consumed as a staple (ifta'at) and storage (iddikhar), and that is not present in plaster. And if it is transitive to a branch upon which there is disagreement, that is the third subtype: an example is if the objector counters in the mentioned case that the cause in the original is the taste (ta'm), and it is not found in plaster, and it is transitive to a disputed branch, meaning fruits and items not measured. And all these types are invalid, because the attribute claimed by the objector does not negate the attribute claimed by the one making the analogy (mu'allil) when the ruling is established by multiple causes. If it is non-transitive, its invalidity is apparent because the purpose of ta'lil is extension (ta'diya). And if it is transitive, the counter is also invalid because it has no connection to the disputed matter; rather it only indicates the absence of that cause in the branch, and that does not necessitate the absence of the ruling. And every speech that is correct in its origin (i.e., in its foundational placement and essence) but is mentioned by way of mu'araqa (contradiction) is invalid according to the people of usul. Therefore mention it by way of mumana'a (denial) so that it exits from the circle of invalidity to the good of correctness, and becomes acceptable in its origin and placement together. Translation and commentary: 'And that is invalid' etc.: So this type of mu'arada is invalid. Whether the counter is with a cause that is non-transitive—this is the first type of mu'arada fi al-illa. For example, in the sale of iron for iron, we give evidence that iron is a weighed commodity sold for its own kind, so sale with excess is not permissible like gold and silver. Then the objector counters: in the original, the cause according to us is thamaniyya (price-ness), and that is not found in iron. Or it is transitive to a branch upon which there is consensus: this is the second type. For example, we offer analogy that the sale of plaster (jiss) for its kind with excess is prohibited due to unity of measure and kind, like wheat and barley. Then the objector counters: the cause in the original is not what you said, but rather it is the potential to be consumed as a staple and storage, and this cause is not present in plaster. It is transitive to a branch upon which there is consensus, like rice and millet.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage explains the second major type of mu'arada: counter-argument in the cause (mu'arada fi al-illa). It has three subtypes, all of which are invalid. First: the objector claims a cause that is non-transitive (ghayr muta'addi), meaning it does not extend beyond the original case. Example: in the sale of iron, the mu'allil uses the attribute 'weighed good' as the cause, but the objector counters that the true cause is 'price-ness' (thamaniyya), which only applies to gold and silver, not iron. This is invalid because the purpose of ta'lil is to extend the ruling to new cases. Second: the cause is transitive to a branch that is unanimously agreed upon. Example: in the prohibition of selling plaster for its kind with excess, the mu'allil uses unity of measure and kind, but the objector says the cause is the potential for being a staple and storage. This is also invalid because the objector's cause, even if transitive to an agreed branch like rice, does not negate the mu'allil's cause. Third: the cause is transitive to a disputed branch. Example: the objector claims the cause is taste (ta'm), not found in plaster, but this cause would apply to fruits and non-measured items, which are disputed. All three are invalid because the objector's attribute does not negate the mu'allil's attribute—a ruling can be based on multiple causes, so negating one cause does not negate the ruling. The passage concludes that a mu'arada is only valid if presented as mumana'a (denial) rather than mu'araqa (contradiction).

Key Terms
معارضة في العلة (mu'arada fi al-illa): Counter-argument in the cause, where the objector challenges the cause (illa) of the original legal case.
متعدي (muta'addi): A cause that is transitive, i.e., applicable to other branches.
غير متعدي (ghayr muta'addi): A cause that is non-transitive, i.e., confined to the original case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of mu'arada fi al-illa involves a cause that does not apply to any other branch?
A) First type (ghayr muta'addi)
B) Second type (muta'addi to an agreed branch)
C) Third type (muta'addi to a disputed branch)
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
There are three types of mu'arada fi al-illa: non-transitive, transitive to an agreed branch, and transitive to a disputed branch; all are invalid in Hanafi usul.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Invalidity of Mu'arada fi al-Illa and the Correct Approach
Explains the invalidity of the three types and introduces mumana'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why all three forms of mu'arada fi al-illa are invalid and describe the correct method of challenge (mumana'a).

Core Idea
Mu'arada fi al-illa fails because it does not negate the original cause; the proper counter-argument is mumana'a.

In the previous lesson we identified the three types. Now we delve into the reasoning: why are all these invalid? The author argues that the objector's attribute does not negate the mu'allil's attribute because a ruling can have multiple causes. Moreover, mu'arada as mu'araqa (contradiction) is invalid; the correct form is mumana'a (denial), which accepts the cause but denies its presence or effect.

Guided Path
1
Understand the core reasoning
The passage states: 'because the attribute claimed by the objector does not negate the attribute claimed by the mu'allil when the ruling is established by multiple causes.' This is the key principle.
A ruling can be based on more than one cause; negating one doesn't negate the ruling.
2
Analyze the two scenarios
If the objector's cause is non-transitive, invalidity is clear because ta'lil aims for extension. If transitive, it's still invalid because it only shows absence of that cause in the branch, not absence of the ruling.
The distinction hinges on the purpose of ta'lil and the nature of the counter.
3
Distinguish mu'araqa from mumana'a
Mu'araqa (contradiction) is offering a different cause in opposition; mumana'a (denial) is denying the existence or applicability of the mu'allil's cause itself.
Mumana'a is accepted because it directly challenges the cause's validity in the original case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالثَّانِي فِي عِلة الأصل (۳) اور معارضہ کی دوسری قسم اصل کی علت میں یعنی معارضہ خالصہ کی دوسری قسم وہ معارضہ ہے جو کہ مقیس علیہ کی علت ہو بایں طور کہ معارض یوں کہے کہ میرے پاس ایسی دلیل ہے جو انس بات پر دلالت کرتی ہے کہ حکم مقیس علیہ میں طلبہ (وہ نہیں ہے جس کو تم نے غلط قرار دی ہے) بلکہ علت دوسری چیز ہے جو فروع میں نہیں پائی جاتی اس کی تین قسمیں ہیں اور مینوں باطل ہیں جیسا کہ مصنف ماتن نے بیان فرمایا ہے۔ وذَالِكَ بَاطِلٌ سَوَاءٌ كَانَتْ بِمَعْنى لا يَتَعَدَى هَذَا هُوَ الْقِسمُ الأول كَمَا إذا عَلَلْنَا بَيْعِ الْحَديد بأنه مَوْزَوْنَ قَويل بجنسه فَلا يَجوز بيعة مُتَفَاضِلا كَذهَب وَالْفِضة

فيما رهنة السائل بِأَنَّ الْعِلَّةَ عِنْدَنَا فِي الأَصْلِ فِى الثَّمَنِيَةُ وَتِلْكَ لا تَتَعَدَّى إلى الْحَدِيدِ أَوْ يَتَعَدى إلى قَرْعٍ مُجْمَعِ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ الْقِسمُ الثَّانِي كَمَا إِذَا عَلَلْنَا فِي حُرْمَةِ بَيْعِ الْجَمَ بِجنسه مُتَفَاضِلاً بِالْكَيْلِ وَالْجِنْسِ كَالْحِنْطَة والشعير فَيُعَارِضة السائِلُ بِأَنَّ الْعِلَّةَ فِي الأَصْلِ لَيْسَت ماقلت بَلْ فِى الأَفْتِيَاتِ والإنْخَار وَهُوَ مَعْدُوم فى الحصن وَإِنْ كَانَ يَتَعَدَّى إِلَى قَرْعٍ مُجْمِع عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ الرز وَالدَّخَنُ أوْ مُخْتَلِفٌ فِيْهِ أَنْ يَتَّعَدَى إِلى فَرْع مُختلِف فِيهِ وَهُوَ القِسم الثالث مِثَالُهُ مَالَوْ عَارِضَ السَّائِلُ فِي الْمَسْأَلَةِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ بأن العلة في الأصل هو الطَّعْمُ وَلَمْ يَوْجَدْ فِى الْجَصَ وَهُوَ يَتَعَدُّى إلى فرع مُختلِف فِيهِ أَعْنِي الْفَوَاكِهِ وَمَا دُوْنَ الْكِيْلِ وَهَذِهِ الأَقْسَامُ كُلْهَا بَاطِلَةٌ لأَنْ الْوَصَفَ الَّذِي يَدْعِيْهِ السَّائِلُ لأينَافِى الْوَصَفَ الَّذِئ يَدْعِيْهِ عَلَةٍ الْمُعَلِّلِ إِذَا اظْلَمَ يَثْبُتُ بِعِلل شتى فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُن وَصفة مُتعدِّيًا فَفَسَادُهُ ظَاهِرٌ لأَن المَقْصُودُ بِالتَّعْلِيلِ التَّفْدِيَةُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُتَعَدِّيَا كَانَ الْمُعَارَضَةُ أَيْضًا فَاسِدَةٌ لانها لاتعلقَ لَهَا بِالْمُتَنَازِعَ فِيهِ إِلا أَنَّهَا تُفِيدَ عَدَمَ تِلكَ العِلْةِ فِيهِ وَهُوَ لا يُوجِبُ عَدَمَ الْحُكْمِ وَكُلُّ كَلام صَحِيحَةٍ فِي الأَصل أَيْ فِي أَصْلِ وَضْعِهِ وَجَوْهَرِهِ وَلَكِنْ يُذكرُهُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الْمُفَارَقَةِ التي هي بَاطِلَةٌ عِنْدَ اهْلِ الأَصُولِ فَاذْكُرُهُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الْمُمَانَعَةِ لِيَخْرُجَ مِنْ حَيْرِ الْفَسَادِ إلى خَيْرُ الصَّحَةِ وَيَكُونُ مَقْبُولاً بأصلِه وَوَصعَه مَعا .

And the second is in the cause of the original: this is the second type of mu'arada, which is counter-argument in the cause of the analogized original. This is the first subtype: as if we offer an analogy for the sale of iron stating that it is a weighed commodity sold for its own kind, so it is not permissible to sell it with excess, like gold and silver. Then the objector counters: the cause in the original according to us is the property of being a price (thamaniyya), and that does not apply to iron. Or if it is transitive to a branch upon which there is consensus, that is the second subtype: as if we offer an analogy for the prohibition of selling plaster (jiss) for its kind with excess, based on measure and kind, like wheat and barley. Then the objector counters: the cause in the original is not what you said, but rather it is the potential to be consumed as a staple (ifta'at) and storage (iddikhar), and that is not present in plaster. And if it is transitive, the counter is also invalid because it has no connection to the disputed matter; rather it only indicates the absence of that cause in the branch, and that does not necessitate the absence of the ruling. Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage explains the second major type of mu'arada: counter-argument in the cause (mu'arada fi al-illa). It has three subtypes, all of which are invalid. First: the objector claims a cause that is non-transitive (ghayr muta'addi), meaning it does not extend beyond the original case. Example: in the sale of iron, the mu'allil uses the attribute 'weighed good' as the cause, but the objector counters that the true cause is 'price-ness' (thamaniyya), which only applies to gold and silver, not iron. This is invalid because the purpose of ta'lil is to extend the ruling to new cases. Second: the cause is transitive to a branch that is unanimously agreed upon. Example: in the prohibition of selling plaster for its kind with excess, the mu'allil uses unity of measure and kind, but the objector says the cause is the potential for being a staple and storage. This is also invalid because the objector's cause, even if transitive to an agreed branch like rice, does not negate the mu'allil's cause. Third: the cause is transitive to a disputed branch. Example: the objector claims the cause is taste (ta'm), not found in plaster, but this cause would apply to fruits and non-measured items, which are disputed. All three are invalid because the objector's attribute does not negate the mu'allil's attribute—a ruling can be based on multiple causes, so negating one cause does not negate the ruling. The passage concludes that a mu'arada is only valid if presented as mumana'a (denial) rather than mu'araqa (contradiction).

Key Terms
معارضة في العلة (mu'arada fi al-illa): Counter-argument in the cause, where the objector challenges the cause (illa) of the original legal case.
ممانعة (mumana'a): Denial, a method of counter-argument where the objector denies the existence or applicability of the cause claimed by the mu'allil.
مفارقة (mu'araqa): Contradiction, a form of counter-argument where the objector presents an alternative cause in opposition to the mu'allil's cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is mu'arada fi al-illa invalid even when the objector's cause is transitive?
A) Because a transitive cause can never be used in qiyas.
B) Because it only shows the absence of that cause, not the absence of the ruling.
C) Because the objector's cause is always non-transitive.
D) Because the mu'allil's cause is always stronger.

Key Takeaway
Mu'arada fi al-illa is invalid because it does not negate the original cause; the proper counter-argument is mumana'a, which directly denies the claimed cause.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Invalid Muʿāraḍah in ʿIllah and the Mufāraqah vs Mumānaʿah Rule
Explains three invalid types of mu'aradah fi al-'illah and how to correct a valid statement presented as mufaraqah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of invalid muʿāraḍah fī ʿillat al-aṣl and apply the Hanafi rule of mufāraqah vs mumānaʿah to correct an objection.

Core Idea
A valid objection in qiyas must deny the analogist's ʿillah (mumānaʿah), not propose a different one (mufāraqah).

In Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh, when a questioner objects to an analogist's cause, not all objections are valid. This passage from Nūr al-Anwār classifies three types of invalid objections and introduces the critical distinction between mufāraqah and mumānaʿah. Understanding this distinction is essential for constructing sound qiyas arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of invalid muʿāraḍah
List the three types as described in the passage: (1) The objector's claimed ʿillah is not transitive to the branch; (2) transitive but extends to an agreed branch; (3) transitive but extends to a disputed branch.
Each type corresponds to a different scenario of the objector's proposed ʿillah.
2
Understand the reason for invalidity
For each type, note the passage's reasoning: a ruling can have multiple ʿillahs, so proposing an alternative does not negate the analogist's ʿillah. A non-transitive ʿillah fails the purpose of tadʿiyah; a transitive but unrelated ʿillah has no bearing on the contested ruling.
The key principle is that multiple ʿillahs can coexist for a single ruling.
3
Distinguish mufāraqah from mumānaʿah
Mufāraqah is the invalid objection that proposes a distinction between original and branch via a different ʿillah. Mumānaʿah is the valid objection that directly denies the presence or applicability of the analogist's own ʿillah.
The passage stresses that a sound statement must be framed as mumānaʿah, not mufāraqah.
4
Apply the rule to the Shāfiʿī example
The passage presents al-Shāfiʿī's argument that freeing a mortgaged slave is like a sale. A distinction claiming that freeing cannot be rescinded is invalid as mufāraqah. To be valid, this must be presented as mumānaʿah: deny that the cause of the sale's nullity is voidability after occurrence.
This illustrates how a correct objection can be rephrased to meet the Hanafi standard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيما رهنة السائل بِأَنَّ الْعِلَّةَ عِنْدَنَا فِي الأَصْلِ فِي الثَّمَنِيَةُ وَتِلْكَ لا تَتَعَدَّى إِلَى الْحَدِيدِ أَوْ يَتَعَدَى إِلَى فَرْعٍ مُجْمَعِ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ الْقِسمُ الثَّانِي كَمَا إِذَا عَلَلْنَا فِي حُرْمَةِ بَيْعِ الْجَصِّ بِجِنْسِهِ مُتَفَاضِلاً بِالْكَيْلِ وَالْجِنْسِ كَالْحِنْطَةِ وَالشَّعِيرِ فَيُعَارِضُهُ السَّائِلُ بِأَنَّ الْعِلَّةَ فِي الأَصْلِ لَيْسَتْ مَا قُلْتَ بَلْ فِي الاِفْتِيَاتِ وَالاِدِّخَارِ وَهُوَ مَعْدُومٌ فِي الْجَصِّ وَإِنْ كَانَ يَتَعَدَّى إِلَى فَرْعٍ مُجْمَعٍ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ الْأَرُزُّ وَالدُّخَنُ أَوْ مُخْتَلِفٌ فِيهِ أَنْ يَتَعَدَّى إِلَى فَرْعٍ مُخْتَلِفٍ فِيهِ وَهُوَ الْقِسْمُ الثَّالِثُ مِثَالُهُ مَا لَوْ عَارَضَ السَّائِلُ فِي الْمَسْأَلَةِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ بِأَنَّ الْعِلَّةَ فِي الْأَصْلِ هُوَ الطَّعْمُ وَلَمْ يُوجَدْ فِي الْجَصِّ وَهُوَ يَتَعَدَّى إِلَى فَرْعٍ مُخْتَلِفٍ فِيهِ أَعْنِي الْفَوَاكِهَ وَمَا دُونَ الْكَيْلِ وَهَذِهِ الْأَقْسَامُ كُلُّهَا بَاطِلَةٌ لِأَنَّ الْوَصْفَ الَّذِي يَدَّعِيهِ السَّائِلُ لَيْسَ مُنَافِيًا لِلْوَصْفِ الَّذِي يَدَّعِيهِ الْمُعَلِّلُ إِذَا الْحُكْمُ يَثْبُتُ بِعِلَلٍ شَتَّى فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ وَصْفُهُ مُتَعَدِّيًا فَفَسَادُهُ ظَاهِرٌ لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ بِالتَّعْلِيلِ التَّعْدِيَةُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُتَعَدِّيًا كَانَ الْمُعَارَضَةُ أَيْضًا فَاسِدَةً لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَعَلُّقَ لَهَا بِالْمُتَنَازَعِ فِيهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهَا تُفِيدُ عَدَمَ تِلْكَ الْعِلَّةِ فِيهِ وَهُوَ لَا يُوجِبُ عَدَمَ الْحُكْمِ وَكُلُّ كَلَامٍ صَحِيحٍ فِي الْأَصْلِ أَيْ فِي أَصْلِ وَضْعِهِ وَجَوْهَرِهِ وَلَكِنْ يُذْكَرُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الْمُفَارَقَةِ الَّتِي هِيَ بَاطِلَةٌ عِنْدَ أَهْلِ الْأُصُولِ فَاذْكُرْهُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الْمُمَانَعَةِ لِيَخْرُجَ مِنْ حَيِّزِ الْفَسَادِ إِلَى حَيِّزِ الصِّحَّةِ وَيَكُونَ مَقْبُولاً بِأَصْلِهِ وَوَضْعِهِ مَعًا
وَإِنَّمَا تُذْكَرُ هَذِهِ الْقَاعِدَةُ هُنَا لِأَنَّ الْمُعَارَضَةَ فِي عِلَّةِ الْأَصْلِ هِيَ الْمُسَمَّاةُ بِالْمُفَارَقَةِ عِنْدَهُمْ لِأَنَّهُ أَتَى السَّائِلُ بِعِلَّةٍ يَقَعُ بِهَا الْفَرْقُ بَيْنَ الْأَصْلِ وَالْفَرْعِ وَهُوَ فَاسِدٌ عِنْدَ الْأَكْثَرِ فَإِذَا أَتَى السَّائِلُ بِكَلَامٍ لَطِيفٍ مَقْبُولٍ فِي ضِمْنِ هَذِهِ الْمُفَارَقَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ فَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ يُذْكَرَ ذَلِكَ الْكَلَامُ بِعَيْنِهِ فِي ضِمْنِ الْمُمَانَعَةِ لِيَكُونَ ذَلِكَ الْكَلَامُ بِمَادَّتِهِ وَهَيْئَتِهِ مَعًا مِثَالُهُ مَا قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ فِي إِعْتَاقِ الرَّاهِنِ الْعَبْدَ الْمَرْهُونَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَنْفُذُ إِعْتَاقُهُ لِأَنَّ الْإِعْتَاقَ تَصَرُّفٌ مِنَ الرَّاهِنِ يُلَاقِي حَقَّ الْمُرْتَهِنِ بِالْإِبْطَالِ فَكَانَ بَاطِلاً كَالْبَيْعِ فَمَنْ جَوَّزَ مِنَّا الْمُفَارَقَةَ قَالَ فِي جَوَابِهِ إِنَّ الْإِعْتَاقَ لَيْسَ كَالْبَيْعِ لِأَنَّ الْبَيْعَ يَحْتَمِلُ الْفَسْخَ وَالْعِتْقَ لَا يَحْتَمِلُهُ فَلَا يَصِحُّ الْقِيَاسُ وَهَذَا الْفَرْقُ هُوَ الْمُعَارَضَةُ فِي عِلَّةِ الْأَصْلِ لِأَنَّ قَائِلَهُ يَقُولُ إِنَّ عِلَّةَ عَدَمِ جَوَازِ الْبَيْعِ هِيَ كَوْنُهُ قَابِلاً لِلْفَسْخِ بَعْدَ وُقُوعِهِ فَهَذَا السُّوَالُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَقْبُولاً فِي نَفْسِهِ
When the questioner objects by saying: 'The effective cause in the original case for us is being a price (thamanīyah), and that does not extend to iron,' or the cause extends to a branch agreed upon, and that is the second type, as when we base the prohibition of selling plaster (jiss) for its genus with excess due to measure (kayl) and genus, like wheat and barley, then the questioner objects by saying: 'The effective cause in the original is not what you said, but rather being consumable (iftiyāt) and stored (iddikhār), and that is absent in plaster, although it extends to a branch agreed upon, i.e., rice and millet; or it extends to a branch disputed, i.e., the third type. An example is if the questioner objects in the mentioned issue by saying: 'The effective cause in the original is taste (ṭaʿm), and it is not found in plaster, and it extends to a disputed branch, namely fruits and what is less than a measure.' All these types are invalid because the attribute claimed by the questioner does not contradict the attribute claimed by the one providing the cause, as a ruling can be established by multiple causes. If his attribute is not transitive, its invalidity is apparent because the purpose of causal reasoning is extension; if it is transitive, the objection is also invalid because it has no connection to the contested point, except that it indicates the absence of that cause in it, which does not necessitate the absence of the ruling. Any speech that is sound in origin—i.e., in its original formulation and essence—but is mentioned by way of distinction (mufāraqah), which is invalid according to the scholars of uṣūl, so mention it by way of preclusion (mumānaʿah) so that it exits from the realm of invalidity to the realm of validity and becomes acceptable in both its source and formulation.
This rule is mentioned here because the objection to the cause of the original (muʿāraḍah fī ʿillat al-aṣl) is called 'distinction' (mufāraqah) among them, since the questioner brings a cause that establishes a difference between the original and the branch, and that is invalid according to the majority. If the questioner brings a subtle and acceptable statement within this invalid distinction, that statement must be mentioned exactly as it is within the preclusion (mumānaʿah) so that the statement is acceptable in both its matter and form. An example is what al-Shāfiʿī said regarding the freeing of a mortgaged slave by the mortgagor: that his freeing is not effective because freeing is an act by the mortgagor that encounters the mortgagee's right with nullification, so it is invalid like a sale. He who among us permits the distinction said in response: Freeing is not like sale, because sale is susceptible to rescission, whereas freeing is not, so analogy is invalid. This distinction is the objection to the cause of the original because its proponent says: 'The cause for the impermissibility of sale is its being susceptible to rescission after its occurrence.' This questioning, even if acceptable in itself...
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage, from a commentary on Nūr al-Anwār, discusses the valid and invalid forms of objection (muʿāraḍah) in qiyas, specifically regarding the effective cause (ʿillah). The author identifies three types of invalid objections that a questioner might raise against the analogist's causal reasoning. 

First type: The questioner claims a different cause that does not extend to the branch at all. Example: In a case of selling iron for iron in excess, the Hanafi analogist says the cause is being a price (thamanīyah) — which applies to gold and silver but not iron. The questioner objects that the cause is thamanīyah and it is absent in iron. This objection is invalid because the cause thamanīyah is not transitive to iron, so it does not address the contested ruling.

Second type: The questioner claims a cause that extends to a branch agreed upon by scholars. Example: Selling plaster (jiss) for plaster with excess is analogous to selling wheat for wheat with excess — the cause is measure (kayl) and genus (jins). The questioner objects that the real cause is consumability (iftiyāt) and storability (iddikhār), which are absent in plaster. Even if that cause extends to rice and millet (agreed branches), the objection is invalid because it does not disprove the analogist's cause.

Third type: The questioner claims a cause that extends to a branch where there is disagreement. Example: The objector says the cause is taste (ṭaʿm), absent in plaster, but it extends to fruits and items not measured by weight/volume. This objection is also invalid because the claimed cause does not negate the analogist's cause.

The author explains that these objections are all invalid because a single ruling can be established by multiple independent causes. The objector's cause either fails to be transitive (so the objection is pointless) or is transitive but unrelated to the contested ruling (so it does not invalidate the analogist's reasoning).

The passage then introduces a key rule: A statement that is sound in itself but presented as a distinction (mufāraqah) is invalid according to uṣūl scholars. Instead, it should be presented as a preclusion (mumānaʿah) — meaning the objector should deny the analogist's cause rather than propose a different one. This ensures the argument is logically valid.

An example from Imam al-Shāfiʿī illustrates the rule: He argued that a mortgagor's freeing of a mortgaged slave is invalid because it nullifies the mortgagee's right, analogous to a sale. A Hanafi response using improper distinction would say freeing is different from sale because sale can be rescinded, but freeing cannot. That distinction, if presented as mufāraqah, is invalid. But if presented within mumānaʿah (i.e., denying that the cause of a sale's nullity is its voidability after occurrence), it becomes acceptable. The passage ends mid-sentence on page 205.

Key takeaway: In Hanafi uṣūl, a valid objection must challenge the analogist's cause directly (mumānaʿah), not propose an alternative cause that distinguishes original and branch (mufāraqah). The latter is bāṭil according to the majority.

Key Terms
مُعَارَضَة فِي عِلَّةِ الْأَصْلِ (muʿāraḍah fī ʿillat al-aṣl): An objection by the questioner against the effective cause of the original case in qiyas, typically by proposing an alternative cause.
مُفَارَقَة (mufāraqah): A type of objection where the questioner proposes a different ʿillah that distinguishes the original from the branch, claiming the analogy fails.
مُمَانَعَة (mumānaʿah): A valid form of objection in qiyas where the questioner directly denies the existence or applicability of the analogist's claimed ʿillah in the original or branch.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi uṣūl scholars, why is an objection by way of mufāraqah (distinction) invalid?
A) Because it denies the existence of the ʿillah in the branch.
B) Because the objector's proposed ʿillah does not negate the analogist's ʿillah; a ruling can have multiple ʿillahs.
C) Because it is not based on a valid text.
D) Because it involves taʿdiyah (extension) which is not allowed.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi uṣūl, an objection to an ʿillah must be a denial (mumānaʿah) and not a distinction (mufāraqah), because multiple ʿillahs can support a single ruling.
