Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
Mufaraqa: Invalid Objection and Its Conversion to Mumana'a
Explains mufaraqa as invalid and how to respond with mumana'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify mufaraqa as an invalid form of objection in qiyas and convert valid arguments within it into mumana'a.

Core Idea
Mufaraqa is invalid, but its valid content must be re-presented as mumana'a.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not every objection to a qiyas is valid. One common but invalid form is mufaraqa (differentiation), where the objector points out a difference between the original and the branch. However, if that objection contains a valid point, it cannot be ignored—it must be reshaped into a proper denial (mumana'a). This lesson walks through the rule and its application using the classical example of a mortgaged slave.

Guided Path
1
Define mufaraqa
Read the passage's statement: al-mufaraqa is an objection on the cause of the original by bringing a different cause. Identify its key feature: it points out a difference between asl and far'.
Mufaraqa is literally 'differentiation'.
2
Understand why mufaraqa is invalid
The passage states mufaraqa is invalid (fasid) according to the majority. Reason: the objector's cause does not negate the original cause; multiple causes can coexist. The analogy is not necessarily broken.
Invalid means it is not accepted as a valid objection, but the argument within may be valid.
3
Distinguish mumana'a from mufaraqa
Mumana'a is a direct denial: 'we do not accept the similarity.' It is a valid way to rebut the analogy. The passage says the objector's valid statement must be rephrased as mumana'a.
Mumana'a is prevention, not objection to the cause.
4
Analyze the al-Shafi'i example
Al-Shafi'i argued that freeing a mortgaged slave is like selling it: both are invalid because they conflict with the mortgagee's right. The response using mufaraqa would be: 'Freeing is not like sale because sale can be rescinded.' The passage says this response is valid but must be presented as mumana'a: 'We do not accept the analogy.'
The example illustrates the conversion.
5
Learn the final rule: tarjih
The passage concludes that the proper way to handle an objection is through tarjih (preponderance), not mufaraqa. This means weighing the evidences and choosing the stronger one.
Tarjih is the ultimate method for resolving conflicting evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنَّمَا تَذكَّرُ هَذِهِ الْقَاعِدَةُ فهنا لأن الْمُعَارَضَة فى علة الأصل هي الْمُسماة بالْمَفَارَقَةِ عِنْدَهُمْ لأنه أتى السَّائِلُ بِعَلَّةٍ يَقَعُ بها الفرق بين الأصلِ وَالْفَرْعِ وَهُوَ فَاسِدٌ عِنْدَ الأَكْثَرِ فَإِذَا أَتِي السَّائِلُ بِكَلام لَطَّيْفِ مَقْبُول فِي ضِمْنِ هَذِهِ الْمُفَارقَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ فَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ يُذْكَرَ ذَلِكَ الْكَلَامُ يَعْيِنِهِ فِى ضِعْنِ الْمُمَانِعَة لَيَكُونَ ذَالِكَ الْكَلامُ بِمَا دَتِهِ وَهَيْئَتِهِ مَعَا مِثَالُهُ مَا قَالَ الشَّافَعِي فِي إِعْتَاقِ الرَّاهِنِ الْعَبْدَ الْمَرْمُونَ أَنَّهُ لا يَنْقُدُ اعْتَاتُهُ لأَن الإعْتَاقِ تَصَرُّف مِنَ الرَّاهِنِ يُلاقِي حَق الْمُرْتَينِ بِالإبْطَالِ فَكَانَ بَاطِلاً كَالبَيْعِ فَمَنْ جَوْزَ مِنَّا الْمُفَارَقَةِ قَالَ فِي جَوَابِهِ إِنَّ الإِعْتَاق لَيْسَ كَالْبِيْعِ لَأَنْ البَيْعَ يَحْتَمِلُ الْفَسَبْحُ وَالْعُنُقِ لَا يَحْتَمِلُهُ فَلَا يَصِيحُ الْقَيَاسُ وَهَذَا الفَرْنَ هُوَ الْمُعَارِضَةُ فِي عِلْةِ الأَصْلِ لاِنْ قَائِلَةٌ يَقُولُ إِنَّ مِلَّةَ عَدَم جَوَازِ الْبَيْمِ هيَ كَوْنُه مُحتملاً للقسم بَعْدَ وَقُوعه فَهَذَا السَّوَال وَإِنْ كَانَ مَقْبُولاً فِي نَفْسه لكِنَّهُ لَمَّا جَاءَ بِهِ السَّائِلُ عَلَى سَبِيْلِ الْمُفَارَقَةِ لاَ يَقْبَلُ مِنْهُ فَكَانَ حَقَّه أن نُورِدُهُ نَحْنُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الْمُمَانَعَةِ فَنَقُولُ لأَنسلم أن الإعْتَاقَ كَالْبَيْعِ فَإِنْ حُكْمَ الْبَيْمِ التوقف عَلَى إِجَازَةِ الْمُرْتَينِ فِيمَا يَجُوزُ فَسَخُهُ لا إِلَّا يُطَالَ وَأَنْتَ فِي اعْتَاقِ تَبْطُلُ أَصْلاً مَا لا يَجُوزُ فَسَيْحُه بَعْدَ ثُبُوتِه حَتَّى لَوْ أَجَارَ الْمُرْتَهِنُ لا يَنْفُذُ اعْتَاقة عِنْدَكَ وَلَمَّا فَرَغَ عَنْ بَيَانِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ شُرَعَ فِي بَيانَ دَفْعِهَا فَقَالَ وَإِذَا قَامَتِ الْمُعَارَضَةُ كَانَ السَّبِيلُ فِيْهَا التَّرْجِيْعُ أَي تَرْجِيْعُ أَحَدِ الْمُعَارِضَيْنَ عَلَى الْآخَرِ بِحَيْثُ تَنْدَفِعُ الْمُعَارَضَةُ.
And this rule is mentioned here because the objection (mu'arada) on the cause of the original (asl) is called 'mufaraqa' (differentiation) among them, since the objector brings a cause that creates a difference between the original and the branch, and this is invalid according to the majority. When the objector brings an acceptable statement within this invalid mufaraqa, then that statement must be mentioned precisely within the context of prevention (mumana'a) so that the statement is acceptable in both its essence and form. An example is al-Shafi'i's statement regarding the mortgagor freeing the mortgaged slave: that his freeing is not effective because freeing is an action of the mortgagor that conflicts with the mortgagee's right by nullifying it, so it is invalid like sale. One among us who permits mufaraqa responds: freeing is not like sale because sale can be rescinded while freeing cannot, so analogy is not valid. This difference is actually an objection to the cause of the original, because the objector says that the reason for the invalidity of selling the mortgaged slave is that sale can be rescinded after its occurrence. This objection, although acceptable in itself, is not accepted when brought by the objector in the form of mufaraqa. The proper way is for us to present it as a prevention (mumana'a) and say: we do not accept that freeing is like sale, because the ruling of sale is that it is suspended on the permission of the mortgagee in matters that can be rescinded, not on nullification. As for freeing, it nullifies completely something that cannot be rescinded after establishment, so even if the mortgagee gives permission, the freeing is not effective according to you. And when he finished explaining the objection, he proceeded to explain its rebuttal and said: When an objection occurs, the way to handle it is to give preponderance (tarjih) of one of the two opposing evidences over the other such that the objection is repelled.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage discusses the principle of 'mufaraqa' (differentiation) in usul al-fiqh. It states that when an objector tries to invalidate an analogy by pointing out a difference between the original and the branch, this type of objection (mufaraqa) is generally considered invalid by the majority of usul scholars. However, if within that invalid objection the objector makes a valid point, the respondent should not reject it outright. Instead, he should rephrase that valid point as a 'mumana'a' (prevention) — that is, a direct denial of the analogy's validity. This way, the valid argument becomes acceptable in both form and substance. The text provides an example from Imam al-Shafi'i concerning a mortgaged slave. Al-Shafi'i argued that if the mortgagor frees the slave, the freeing is ineffective, just as a sale of the slave would be invalid because it conflicts with the mortgagee's right. A Hanafi who accepts mufaraqa would respond by pointing out a difference: sale can be rescinded, but freeing cannot. This response is a valid argument, but since it was presented as a mufaraqa (a difference-based objection), it is not accepted. Instead, the Hanafi should present it as a mumana'a, directly denying the similarity between freeing and sale, and explaining that sale is suspended on permission while freeing is an outright nullification. The passage concludes by noting that the correct method to refute an objection is through tarjih (preponderance), not through mufaraqa.

Key Terms
المفارقة (al-mufaraqa): An objection that distinguishes between the original and the branch by bringing a different cause
الممانعة (al-mumana'a): Prevention or denial: a direct refusal to accept the analogy's premise
المعارضة (al-mu'arada): Objection: presenting a counter-argument against the cause in qiyas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul explanation in this passage, what should be done when an objector presents a valid argument in the form of mufaraqa (differentiation)?
A) Reject the argument entirely because it is based on mufaraqa.
B) Accept the argument as it is because it is valid in itself.
C) Rephrase the valid argument as a mumana'a (prevention) and present it that way.
D) Ignore the objection and proceed with the original analogy.

Key Takeaway
Mufaraqa is an invalid objection; any valid point within it must be re-presented as a direct denial (mumana'a) to be accepted.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Mufaraqa as a Type of Mu'arada: The Hanafi Rebuttal
Explains mufaraqa rule with example of mortgaged slave emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of mufaraqa versus muman'a to critique a qiyas argument, and distinguish between acceptable and unacceptable forms of mu'arada.

Core Idea
A mere distinction (mufaraqa) is not accepted as an objection; it must be reframed as a direct denial (muman'a) to be effective.

In Hanafi usul, a mu'arida (objection) to qiyas can take several forms. One of them is mufaraqa, where the objector points out a difference between the original and the branch to invalidate the analogy. However, simply showing a difference is not sufficient; the response must be reframed as muman'a (prevention) to be legally sound. This lesson dissects the rule using the classic example of freeing a mortgaged slave.

Guided Path
1
Understand mufaraqa
Mufaraqa is when the questioner claims a distinction between the asl and far' to invalidate the qiyas. In Hanafi usul, this is considered a weak objection if left as mere distinction.
The distinction must be relevant to the 'illa.
2
Identify the Shafi'i qiyas
The Shafi'i argue that freeing a mortgaged slave is invalid by analogy with selling it, because both nullify the mortgagee's right. The analogy is 'emancipation is like sale'.
The 'illa is nullifying the mortgagee's right.
3
Follow the Hanafi mufaraqa response
The Hanafi response points out that sale can be rescinded (faskh) but emancipation cannot, thus the analogy fails. This is a mufaraqa objection based on a difference in the 'illa.
The difference in faskh possibility is the key distinction.
4
Reframe as muman'a
The author states that such an objection should be presented as muman'a: 'We do not accept that emancipation is like sale.' This reframing makes the objection valid.
The transformation from mufaraqa to muman'a is crucial for acceptance.
5
Apply the rule
The rule is that a mufaraqa objection is not accepted in its original form; the responder must convert it to muman'a to be effective. This teaches the proper method of responding to a qiyas challenge.
Always reframe distinctions as direct denials.

لكِنَّهُ لَمَّا جَاءَ بِهِ السَّائِلُ عَلَى سَبِيْلِ الْمُفَارَقَةِ لاَ يَقْبَلُ مِنْهُ فَكَانَ حَقَّه أن نُورِدُهُ نَحْنُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الْمُمَانَعَةِ فَنَقُولُ لأَنسلم أن الإعْتَاقَ كَالْبَيْعِ فَإِنْ حُكْمَ الْبَيْمِ التوقف عَلَى إِجَازَةِ الْمُرْتَينِ فِيمَا يَجُوزُ فَسَخُهُ لا إِلَّا يُطَالَ وَأَنْتَ فِي اعْتَاقِ تَبْطُلُ أَصْلاً مَا لا يَجُوزُ فَسَيْحُه بَعْدَ ثُبُوتِه حَتَّى لَوْ أَجَارَ الْمُرْتَهِنُ لا يَنْفُذُ اعْتَاقة عِنْدَكَ
ترجمه تشریح وإنما تذكر هذه القاعِدَة فهنا الخ: معارضہ کے بیان میں مفارقہ کے اس قاعدہ کو یہاں بیان اس لئے کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ معارضه فى العلة ہی کا دوسرا نام مفارقہ ہے کیونکہ سائل معترض اپنے سوال میں ایسی علت کو بیان کرتا ہے کہ جس سے اصل میں اور فرع میں فرق ظاہر ہو جاتا ہے علماء اصول کے نزدیک مگر فرق کا نہ کورہ اعتراض اکثر علماء کے نزدیک فاسد ہے پس اگر سائل مفارقہ کے ضمن میں کوئی ایسا کلام ذکر کرے جو فی نفسہ مقبول ہو تو اس کا عنوان بدل کر بطرز ممانعت اس کے کلام کو چیش کرنا چاہیے تاکہ معترض کا کلام صور ڈا اور معنی مہر طرح مقبول ہو جائے اس کی مثال امام شافعی کا یہ قول ہے کہ اگر را ہن اپنے مرہون غلام کو آزاد کر دے تو وہ آزاد نہیں ہو گا یعنی اس کا اعتماق نافذ نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اتاق (آزاد کر دیا) رہن رکھنے والے ( راہن) کی طرف سے ایک تصرف ہے جو مر تہن (جس کے پاس رہن رکھا گیا ہے) کے حق کو باطل کر رہا ہے لہذا یہ تصرف باطل ہو جائے گا جس طرح کہ بیچ باطل ہو جاتی ہے (یعنی اگر راہن اپنے غلام کو فروخت کر دے تو یہ بھی باطل ہو جاتی ہے کیونکہ اس سے مرتین کا حق مارا جاتا ہے) احناف میں سے جنہوں نے مفارقت کو جائز مانا ہے وہ اس استدلال کا جواب دیتے ہیں کہ احتیاق بیع کی مانند نہیں ہے فرق یہ ہے کہ بی صبح کا احتمال رکھتی ہے اور عشق فتح کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا لہذا بیچ پر حق کو قیاس نہیں کیا جاتا۔ بیچ یه فرق در حقیقت اصل مقیس علیہ کی علمت پر معارضہ ہے کیونکہ لأَن قَائِلَهُ يَقُولَ کیونکہ معارض کہتا ہے کہ غلام مرہون کی بیچ کے جائز نہ ہونے کی علت بیچ کے صحیح ہو جانے کے بعد فسخ ہونے کا احتمال ہے (اور حق میں یہ احتمال نہیں ہے) تو یہ سوال اعتراض اگر چہ فی نفسہ مقبول ہے لیکن چونکہ معترض نے اس کو بطور مفارقت کے پیش کیا ہے اس لئے مقبول نہ کیا جائے گا
فَكَانَ حَقَّهُ إِن نُوْرِدَهُ نَحْنُ عَلَى سَبِيلِ المَمَانَعَةِ بس حق بات یہ ہے کہ اس کو ہم بطور ممانعتہ کے پیش کریں اور کہیں کہ ہم تعلیم نہیں کرتے کہ اعتاق مانند بیچ کیسے ہے اس وجہ سے کہ بیچ مر تمہین کی اجازت پر موقوف ہوتی ہے اس چیز کی بیچ میں نسخ کا احتمال رکھتی ہے نہ ابطال کا (یعنی مرہون کو حق صیح بیچ کا حاصل انفال کا بیچ کا حق مرتہن کو نہیں ہے) اور اعتاق میں آپ راہن کے حق کو بالکل باطل کرتے ہیں اور ایسی چیز میں باطل کرتے ہیں کہ ثبوت کے بعد جس کا فتح کرنا جائزہ نہیں ہے حتی کہ اگر مر تہن غلام کے آزاد کرنے کا مالک (ران) کو اجازت بھی دیدے تب بھی آپ (شافعی) کے نزدیک اعتماق نافذ نہیں ہوتا۔
He said: But when the questioner presents it in the manner of mufaraqa, it is not accepted from him. So the right is that we present it in the manner of muman'a. So we say: We do not accept that emancipation is like sale, because the ruling of sale is suspended upon the permission of the mortgagee, in what its rescission is permissible? (unclear) And you, in emancipation, you nullify it completely? (unclear) that which cannot be rescinded after its establishment, so even if the mortgagee permits, the emancipation would not be valid according to you. The Urdu commentary explains: This rule of mufaraqa is mentioned here because mu'arada in the cause is another name for mufaraqa; the questioner presents a cause showing a difference between original and branch. Most scholars consider objection by mere difference invalid. But if the questioner's speech is acceptable in itself, it should be presented as muman'a. Example: Imam Shafi'i says freeing a mortgaged slave is invalid because it nullifies the mortgagee's right, like sale. Hanafis respond: emancipation is not like sale because sale can be rescinded, emancipation cannot; thus the analogy fails. This difference is a mu'arada on the cause. Although the objection is valid in itself, since it is presented as mufaraqa it is not accepted. The right is to present it as muman'a: we do not accept emancipation is like sale, because sale is suspended on permission in a matter that can be rescinded, not nullified; in emancipation you nullify the mortgager's right completely in something that cannot be rescinded, so even with the mortgagee's permission emancipation is not valid according to you.

Commentary
This passage discusses the rule of mufaraqa (distinction) as a type of mu'arada in qiyas. The author explains that when a questioner uses a distinction between the original and branch to attack a qiyas, his argument is not accepted in that form. Instead, the responder should reframe it as muman'a (prevention). The example is the Shafi'i position that freeing a mortgaged slave is invalid by analogy with selling it. The Hanafi rebuttal uses mufaraqa: sale can be rescinded, but emancipation cannot, so the analogy fails. This shows the importance of correctly identifying the 'illa and the difference between valid and invalid mu'arada.

Key Terms
مفارقة (mufaraqa): A type of mu'arada in qiyas where the questioner shows a distinction between the original and the branch to invalidate the analogy.
معارضة (mu'arada): Opposition or contradiction in evidence, specifically in the context of qiyas.
ممانعة (muman'a): The act of preventing or resisting an argument by reframing it as a direct denial rather than a distinction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because sale can be rescinded (faskh) while emancipation cannot
C) Because emancipation is a form of charity
D) Because the slave is owned by the mortgagee

Key Takeaway
A mufaraqa objection must be reframed as muman'a to be accepted; the distinction in the 'illa is valid but must be presented as a direct denial.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Four Methods of Tarjih and the Fasting Analogy
Explaining the four methods of preferring one qiyas over another with a fasting example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the four methods of tarjīḥ between conflicting qiyās, specifically using the criterion of 'strength of certainty' (quwwat al-thubāt) to evaluate the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on intention (niyya) in the Ramadan fast.

Core Idea
A description that applies to multiple rulings is stronger than one confined to a single issue.

This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh text presents four methods for preferring one analogy (qiyas) over another when they conflict. The focus is on the second method: strength of certainty (quwwat al-thubāt). The author illustrates this through the classic dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on whether a person must specify in their intention that they are fasting Ramadan. By tracing how each school's chosen description (ta'ayyun vs. farḍiyya) extends to other legal issues, we learn how to weigh competing analogies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested fiqh issue
Determine the exact point of disagreement: does the Ramadan fast require a specified intention (niyya) in the heart, or is it automatically valid without specifying 'Ramadan'?
The issue is not whether niyya is required, but whether one must mentally specify 'Ramadan'.
2
State the competing descriptions
The Hanafi school describes the fast as determined (mutā'ayyin) by Allah, so the worshiper does not need to specify. The Shafi'i school describes it as a duty fast (sawm farḍ), requiring specification like any duty fast.
These two descriptions (ta'ayyun vs. farḍiyya) are the core of the qiyas conflict.
3
Apply the tarjīḥ method of strength of certainty
Examine which description is more necessary (lāzim) to the ruling. A description that is intrinsic to the ruling and appears in multiple independent cases is stronger.
The text argues that ta'ayyun extends beyond fasting to deposits, usurped goods, and void sales.
4
Examine the extension of ta'ayyun
In cases of returning a deposit, returning usurped property, or returning a void-purchased item, one does not need to specify the legal reason. The act itself is determined. This shows ta'ayyun is a general principle.
Farḍiyya only appears in fasting, so it is weaker.
5
Evaluate the objection and conclude
An objection states that if the opponent's reasoning is 'sawm al-farḍ' (the duty fast) rather than abstract 'farḍiyya', the deposit analogy may be inapposite. The Hanafi response implies ta'ayyun remains broader.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Hanafi ruling, fasting without specifying Ramadan is valid; under Shafi'i, it is invalid.

فَيَتَرَجَّحُ عَلَيْهِ فَإِنْ قِيلَ فَعَلَىٰ هَذَا يَلْزَمُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الشَّاهِدُ الْأَعْدَلُ رَاجِحًا عَلَى الْعَادِلِ لِأَنْ أَثَرَهُ أَقْوَى أُجِيبَ بِأَنَّا لَا نُسَلِّمُ أَنَّ الْعَدَالَةَ قَوْلِهِمْ صَوْمُ فَرْضٍ فَيَجِبُ تَعْيِينُ النِّيَّةِ فِيهِ كَصَوْمِ الْقَضَاءِ لِأَنَّ هَذَا أَيْ وَصْفُ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ الَّذِي أَوْرَدَهُ الشَّافِعِيُّ مَخْصُوصٌ فِي الصَّوْمِ بِخِلَافِ التَّعْيِينِ الَّذِي أَوْرَدْنَاهُ فَقَدْ تَعَدَّىٰ إِلَى الْوَدَائِعِ وَالْمَغْصُوبِ وَرَدِّ الْمَبِيعِ فِي الْبَيْعِ الْفَاسِدِ أَيْ إِذَا رَدَّ الْوَدِيعَةَ إِلَى الْمَالِكِ وَالْمَغْصُوبَ إِلَى بَيْعًا فَاسِدًا لِأَنَّهُ مُتَعَيَّنٌ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ الرَّبْطَ بِجِهَةٍ أُخْرَى فَيَكُونُ ثُبَاتُ التَّعْيِينِ عَلَى حُكْمِهِ أَقْوَىٰ مِنْ ثُبَاتِ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ عَلَى حُكْمِهَا وَقِيلَ عَلَيْهِ إِنَّ هَذَا إِنَّمَا يَرِدُ لَوْ كَانَ تَعْلِيلُ الْخَصْمِ بِمُجَرَّدِ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ أَمَّا إِذَا كَانَ تَعْلِيلُهُ هُوَ صَوْمُ الْفَرْضِ فَلَا يُنَاسِبُ بِمُقَابَلَتِهِ إِرَادَةُ مَسْأَلَةِ رَدِّ ترجیح حاصل ہوتی ہے یعنی ایک قیاس کی دوسری قیاس پر ترجیح چار ہیں (۱) قوت تاثیر جیسے قیاس کے مقابلے میں استحسان (قوی) ہے کہ استحسان کا اثر زیادہ قوی ہے لہذا قیاس پر استحسان کو ترجیح دی جائے گی پس اگر اس پر کوئی اعتراض کرے کہ اس اصول پر لازم آتا ہے کہ دو گواہوں عادل میں سے جو گواہ اعدل ( زیادہ عدل والا ہو ) اس کی شہادت کو راجح قرار دیا جائے بمقابلہ عادل کی گواہی کے کیونکہ اعدل کا اثر قوی ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہم اس بات کو تسلیم نہیں کرتے ہیں کہ عدالت زیادتی و کمی میں منقسم بھی ہو جاتی ہے کیونکہ عدالت نام محظورات (ممنوعات) دین سے پر ہیز کرنے اور کبائر گناہ سے بچنے اور صغائر پر اصرار نہ کرنے کا ہے یہ مضبوط اور پختہ چیز ہے جس میں تعدد نہیں ہے ہاں اختلاف اور تفاوت ہے تو وہ تقوی اور پرہیز گاری میں ہے (جس کی حقیقت پر اصلاح پانا محال ہے) (۲) قوت ثبات وصف سے اس حکم پر جس کا یہ شاہد اور دلیل ہے یعنی ایک قیاس کا وصف اپنے حکم کے ساتھ زیادہ لازم ہو دوسرے قیاس کے وصف سے جیسے صوم رمضان کے بارہ میں ہمارا یہ قول ہے کہ یہ تعین ہے اللہ تعالی کی جانب سے لہذا بندہ پر نیت میں تعیین واجب نہیں ہے اولیٰ من قولهم صوم فرض رائج ہے شوافع کے اس قول سے کہ یہ فرض روزہ ہے لہذا اس میں نیت کی تعیین واجب ہے جیسا کہ قضاء کے روزہ میں تعیین واجب ہے کیونکہ یہ وصف (فرضیت) جس کو امام شافعی نے علت قرار دی ہے مخصوص ہے روزہ کے ساتھ بخلاف تعین سے جس کو ہم نے علت قرار دی ہے کہ اس کا تعدی پایا جاتا ہے مال ودیعت، غصب اور بیع فاسد میں یعنی جب امانت کا مال یا غصب کیا ہوا مال اس کے مالک کی طرف واپس کر دے یا بیع فاسد کی صورت میں شئی مبیع کو بائع کی جانب واپس کر دے تو جس طرح سے بھی حوالے کرے گا وہ بری الذمہ ہو جائے گا اور اس میں یہ شرط نہیں کہ دفع کرتے وقت یہ تعیین کرے کہ ودیعت ادا کر رہا ہے یا غصب کا مال یا بیع فاسد کا مال کیونکہ یہ مال تعین شدہ ہے اور اسے کسی اور حیثیت سے منسلک کرنے کا احتمال نہیں لہذا تعیین کا اپنے حکم پر ثبوت زیادہ قوی ہے فرضیت کے اپنے حکم پر ثبوت سے اور اس پر کہا گیا کہ یہ اعتراض صرف اس صورت میں وارد ہوتا ہے جب خصم کی علت محض فرضیت ہو، لیکن اگر اس کی علت 'صوم الفرض' ہے تو پھر اس کے مقابلے میں ودیعت، مغصوب اور بیع فاسد کی مثال مناسب نہیں (۳) کثرت اصول: جب ایک قیاس کے لئے ایک اصل شاہد ہو اور دوسرے قیاس کے لئے دو یا زیادہ اصول ہوں تو یہ دوسرا قیاس راجح ہوگا۔
And what tarjīḥ (preference) occurs by: that preferring one qiyas over another is four [methods]: 1) by the strength of the effect, like istiḥsān in opposing qiyas, and the effect in istiḥsān is stronger, so it is preferred over it. If it is said: then this necessitates that the more just witness should be preferred over the just, because his effect is stronger. It is answered: we do not concede that justice differs by increase and decrease, for it is abstention from prohibited things by avoiding major sins and not persisting in minor sins, and it is a fixed matter that does not multiply. Difference is only in piety. 2) By the strength of its certainty, i.e., the certainty of the description over the ruling well-known by it, so that the description is necessary for the ruling attached to it, more than the description of the other qiyas. Like our statement concerning the fast of Ramadan: it is determined by Allah, so determination in intention is not obligatory on the servant, is better than their statement: it is a duty fast, so determination of intention is obligatory, like the make-up fast. Because this – i.e., the description of obligatoriness which al-Shafi'i advanced – is specific to fasting, unlike determination (ta'ayyun) which we advanced, for it extends to deposits, usurped property, and restitution of the sold item in a void sale. That is, if one returns a deposit to its owner, or a usurped item to its taker, or a void-sold item to the seller, by any means, he is discharged from liability, and determination of the payment as deposit, usurpation, or void sale is not required, because it is determined and does not admit connection by another aspect. So the certainty of determination over its ruling is stronger than the certainty of obligatoriness over its ruling. And it was said against this: this only applies if the opponent's reasoning is by mere obligatoriness. As for if his reasoning is 'the duty fast', then it is not appropriate to counter it with the issue of returning deposits, usurped items, and void sales. 3) By multiplicity of origins: if one qiyas is supported by one origin and another qiyas by two or more origins, the latter is preferred.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage from a commentary on principles of jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh) discusses the four methods of tarjīḥ (preference) when two analogies (qiyas) conflict. The first method is 'strength of effect' (quwwat al-athar): if one proof has a stronger legal effect, it is preferred. An example is istiḥsān (juristic preference) when it opposes qiyas; istiḥsān is stronger and thus preferred. An objection arises: if justice (adāla) in witnesses varies, the more just would be preferred. The answer is that justice is a fixed state not subject to degrees; only piety (taqwā) varies. The second method is 'strength of certainty' (quwwat al-thubāt): a description that is intrinsic (lāzim) to the ruling is stronger. The example given is the fast of Ramadan: Hanafis argue it is determined (mutā'ayyin) by Allah (Ramadan is fixed), so the worshiper need not specify in intention which fast he is observing. In contrast, Shafi'is argue it is a duty fast (sawm farḍ), which requires intention specification like any duty fast (e.g., qada). The Hanafi description (ta'ayyun) extends beyond fasting to deposits, usurped goods, and void sales—no need to specify the reason when returning. The Shafi'i description (farḍiyya) is limited to fasting. The third method mentioned is multiplicity of origins (kathrat uṣūl), i.e., a qiyas supported by more foundational principles is preferred. The fourth method is not fully described in the extracted text. This passage demonstrates how usul scholars weigh competing analogies using rational criteria.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): Preferring one legal proof or analogy over another based on certain criteria
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Juristic preference, a method of choosing a ruling based on higher principles, often overriding qiyas
التعيين (al-ta'ayyun): Determination; a quality of an act that is fixed and known without need for specification

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what makes the Hanafi preference of ta'ayyun over farḍiyya stronger in the fasting example?
A) Ta'ayyun is mentioned in the Quran
B) Ta'ayyun applies to other issues like deposits and void sales, showing it is a general principle
C) Farḍiyya is rejected by all schools
D) Ta'ayyun is easier for the worshiper

Key Takeaway
The strength of a legal description is measured by its necessity (luzūm) and its applicability across multiple issues; ta'ayyun is stronger than farḍiyya because it extends beyond fasting.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Four Criteria for Tarjīh (Preferring One Qiyas Over Another)
A rule of preference among conflicting analogies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the four Hanafi criteria for tarjīh between conflicting qiyas: quwwat al-athar, quwwat al-thubāt, kaṯrat al-uṣūl, and al-ʿadam ʿinda al-ʿadam.

Core Idea
Four tests determine which qiyas prevails: effect, stability, multiplicity, and inverse consistency.

In Hanafi uṣūl, when two analogies (qiyas) conflict, the preferred one is not chosen arbitrarily. Al-Marghinani presents four objective criteria: strength of effect, strength of stability, multiplicity of origins, and absence when the cause is absent. Each is illustrated with a fiqh example—including the famous dispute over wiping the head (masḥ ar-ra's) between Hanafis and Shāfiʿīs. This lesson unpacks these four modes and how they govern the art of tarjīh.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the four criteria
Memorize the four Arabic terms: quwwat al-athar, quwwat al-thubāt, kaṯrat al-uṣūl, and al-ʿadam ʿinda al-ʿadam. Understand their rough English translations: strength of effect, strength of stability, multiplicity of origins, and absence when absent.
These are the only four modes mentioned; do not confuse with other types of tarjīh like majority of narrators.
2
Examine quwwat al-athar
The first criterion: a qiyas that produces a stronger effect (athar) is preferred. The text gives istihsān as an example: istihsān is stronger than qiyas because its effect (relief from hardship) is more pervasive.
Istihsān is itself a type of qiyas khafī, so this criterion shows that a hidden analogy can outweigh a clear one.
3
Analyze quwwat al-thubāt
The second criterion: an attribute that is more stable (thābit) across different cases is preferred. The example of ta'yīn (determination) in fasting: the attribute 'muta'ayyin' (determined) applies to trusts, usurped goods, and invalid sales, so it is more stable than 'fard' which is specific to the fast.
Stability here means generality: the attribute can be extended to many cases without exception.
4
Apply kaṯrat al-uṣūl
The third criterion: the qiyas that has more original cases (uṣūl) is preferred. In the masḥ ar-ra's dispute, the Hanafi position (masḥ) has three origins: wiping over khuff, bandage, and tayammum. The Shāfiʿī position (rukn) has only one origin: washing.
Count the number of valid aṣl cases supporting each attribute; more is stronger.
5
Test with al-ʿadam ʿinda al-ʿadam
The fourth criterion: an attribute is valid only if it is present when the ruling is present and absent when the ruling is absent (inverse consistency). The Hanafi attribute 'masḥ' inverts: wherever there is masḥ, repetition is not recommended; wherever there is washing, repetition is recommended. The Shāfiʿī attribute 'rukn' fails this test because sniffling (masmaṭ) and istinshāq are not pillars yet repetition is not recommended.
This is a logical consistency check: if the attribute is the cause, it should be absent when the ruling is absent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَا يَقَعَ بِهِ التَّرْجِيْحُ أَرْبَعَةٌ: (۱) بقوة الأثر (۲) وبقوة ثباته (۳) وبكثرة أصوله (۴) وبالعدم عند العدم. فقوة الأثر: كاستحسان مع القياس. وقوة ثباته: كقولنا في صوم رمضان إنه متعين فلا يجب تعيين النية، أولى من قولهم إنه فرض فيجب، لأن التعيين يتعدى إلى الودائع والمغصوب والبيع الفاسد فلا يشترط تعيين الدفع. وكثرة الأصول: كقولنا في مسح الرأس إنه مسح فلا يسن تثليثه، أصله مسح الخف والجبيرة والتيمم، بخلاف قول الشافعي إنه ركن فيسن تثليثه فإن لا أصل له إلا الغسل. والعكس: كقولنا في مسح الرأس إنه مسح فلا يسن تكراره لأنه ينعكس إلى ما ليس بمسح فيسن تكراره، بخلاف قول الشافعي إنه ركن فلا ينعكس.
And that by which preference (tarjīh) is achieved are four: (1) By strength of effect; (2) By strength of its stability; (3) By multiplicity of its origins; (4) By absence when absent. Strength of effect: like istihsan against qiyas. Strength of stability: like our saying regarding the fast of Ramadan that it is determined (muta'ayyin), so specifying the intention is not obligatory, is preferable to their saying that it is obligatory (fard), so specifying is obligatory, because determination (ta'yin) extends to trusts, usurped goods, and invalid sales, so specifying the handover is not required. Multiplicity of origins: like our saying regarding wiping the head (masḥ ar-ra's) that it is wiping (masḥ), so repeating it three times is not recommended; its origins are wiping over the khuff, the bandage, and tayammum, contrary to al-Shafi'i's saying that it is a pillar (rukn), so repeating three times is recommended, for it has no origin except washing. And the inverse: like our saying regarding wiping the head that it is wiping, so repeating it is not recommended because it is inversely consistent: what is not wiping requires repetition, contrary to al-Shafi'i's saying that it is a pillar, so it does not invert.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a rule of preference (tarjīh) among conflicting analogies (qiyas). The author enumerates four criteria, each illustrated with a Hanafi example. First, strength of effect (quwwat al-athar): istihsan is stronger than qiyas because its effect is more pervasive. Second, strength of stability (thubāt): the attribute of determination (ta'yin) applied to the fast of Ramadan is more stable than the attribute of obligation (fard), because it can be generalized to cases like returning trusts, whereas obligation is specific to the fast. Third, multiplicity of origins (kaṯrat al-uṣūl): for wiping the head, the Hanafi position relies on multiple analogies (khuff, bandage, tayammum) while the Shafi'i position relies only on washing. Fourth, inverse consistency (al-ʿadam ʿinda al-ʿadam): a valid attribute must be present when the ruling is present and absent when the ruling is absent. The Hanafi attribute of 'wiping' for masḥ ar-ra's meets this condition, while the Shafi'i attribute of 'pillar' does not.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjīh): Preferring one qiyas over another based on specific criteria.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical deduction extending a ruling from an original case (aṣl) to a new case (farʿ) due to a common ʿillah.
استحسان (istihsan): Preferring a stronger evidence over qiyas due to a more compelling effect; a form of qiyas khafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT one of the four modes of tarjīh between qiyas?
A) Strength of effect (quwwat al-athar)
B) Strength of stability (quwwat al-thubāt)
C) Multiplicity of origins (kaṯrat al-uṣūl)
D) Majority of scholars (kaṯrat al-ʿulamā)

Key Takeaway
Tarjīh in Hanafi uṣūl is governed by four objective tests, not subjective preference.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Valid Tarjih Methods: Multiplicity of Asls and the Inverse (Aks)
Explains two valid tarjih criteria with example of wiping the head

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the two Hanafi criteria for tarjih in qiyas—multiplicity of asls and the inverse relation (aks)—to evaluate competing analogies.

Core Idea
A description that both consistently produces a ruling and inversely implies its opposite is stronger than one that only shows consistency.

In Hanafi usul, not all multiplicity of evidence strengthens an analogy. The scholar distinguishes between valid multiplicity (of asls) and invalid forms. Similarly, a description that both 'exists when the ruling exists' (itrad) and 'vanishes when the ruling vanishes' (aks) is preferred. This passage explains both criteria through the classical dispute over wiping the head in wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two criteria
Read the passage to find the two valid tarjih methods: (1) multiplicity of asls, (2) the inverse relation (aks). Note how the author contrasts them with invalid forms.
2
Define 'asl' and 'multiplicity of asls'
Understand that asl here means the maqis 'alayh (basis of analogy). Valid multiplicity means having several distinct original cases that all share the same description, not multiple analogical proofs or aspects of similarity.
The author explicitly says 'multiplicity of analogical evidences' is invalid.
3
Apply the criteria to the masah example
Work through the Hanafi reasoning: wiping the head is 'masah' (not ghusl), so its ruling is that triple repetition is not sunnah. List the asls: wiping over khuff, jabirah, and tayammum. Contrast with Shafi'i who only has washing as an asl.
This demonstrates multiplicity of asls.
4
Understand itrad and aks
Define itrad (consistency: ruling exists when description exists) and aks (inverse: ruling absent when description absent). See how the passage explains them.
5
Evaluate the masah example with aks
Show that the description 'masah' passes the aks test: what is not masah (e.g., washing face) has triple repetition as sunnah. Then show that the Shafi'i description 'rukn' fails the aks test because madmadah and istinshaq are not rukn yet their repetition is not sunnah.
This is the heart of the tarjih: a description that both ittard and in'akas is preferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قانة
عَلى الأَوَّلِ وَالْمُرَادُ بالاَصلِ الْمَقِيْسَ عَلَيْهِ وَلا يَكُونُ هَذَا مِنْ قَبيْل كَثُرَةِ الأدلة اَلْقَيَاسِيَةِ أَوْ كَثْرَةِ أَوْجه الشبه لشيءٍ فَإِنْ هَذِهِ كُلَّهَا فَاسِدَةً وَكَثْرَةُ الأصول صَحِيْحَةٌ كَقَوْلِنَا فِي مَسَبْحٍ الرَّاسِ إِنَّهُ مَسَحٌ فَلا يُسَنُ تَثْلِيتُهُ فَإِنْ أَصْلَهُ مَسَبْحُ الْخُفْ وَالْجَبَيْرَةِ وَالتَّيَمُ بِخِلافِ قَوْل الشَّافَعِى إِنَّهُ رُكْنُ فَيُسَنُ تَثْلِيْتُهُ فَإِنَّهُ لاَ أَصْلَ لَهُ إِلَّا الْغَسْلُ وَبِالْعَدَم عِنْدَ الْعَدَم وَهُوَ الْعَكْسُ أَيْ إِذَا كَانَ وَصَفٌ يَطْرِدُ وَيَنْعَكِسُ كَانَ أَوْلَى مِنْ وَصْفِ يَطْرِدُ وَلَا يَنْعَكِسُ فَالْاطْرَاد حِينَئِذٍ هُوَ الْوُجُودُ عِنْدَ الْوُجُوْدِ فَقَط وَالأَنْعِكَاسُ هُوَ الْعَدَمُ عِنْدَ الْعَدَم مِثْلُ قَوْلِنَا فِي مَسَبْحٍ الرَّاسِ إِنَّهُ مَسحٌ فَلاَيُسنُ تَكْرَارُهُ فَإِنَّهُ يَنْعَكِسُ إلى قَوْلِنَا مَالاً يَكُونُ مَسَبْحًا فَيُسن تَكْرَارُهُ كَستَغلِ الْوَجْهِ وَتَحْرِهِ بِخِلافِ قَوْلِ الشَّافَعِى أَنَّهُ رَكْنٌ فَيُسَنُ تَكْرَارُهُ . فَإِنَّهُ لايَنْعَكِسُ إِلَى قَوْلِهِ مَالَيسَ يرُكُن لأيُسنُ تَكْرَارُهُ فَإِنَّ الْمَصْمَد والاستنشاق لَيْسَ برُكُن وَمَعَ ذَالِكَ لَيُسَنُ تَكْرَارُهُ.
On the first: and what is meant by asl is the thing measured against. And this is not from the category of multiplicity of analogical evidences or multiplicity of aspects of similarity for something, for all these are invalid. And multiplicity of asls is valid, like our statement regarding wiping of the head: it is wiping, so its triple repetition is not sunnah, for its asl is wiping over khuff, over jabirah, and tayammum, contrary to the saying of al-Shafi'i that it is a rukn, so its triple repetition is sunnah, for he has no asl except washing. And by absence at absence, and it is the inverse: i.e., when a description is consistent and inversely consistent, it is better than a description that is consistent but not inversely consistent. So consistency here is existence at existence only, and inverse is absence at absence. Like our statement regarding wiping of the head: it is wiping, so its repetition is not sunnah, for it inverts to our statement: what is not wiping, its repetition is sunnah, like washing the face and hands, contrary to the saying of al-Shafi'i that it is a rukn, so its repetition is sunnah, for it does not invert to his statement: what is not a rukn, its repetition is not sunnah, for madmadah and istinshaq are not a rukn, yet with that, their repetition is not sunnah.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage presents two valid criteria for tarjih (preference) in qiyas: (1) multiplicity of asls (usul) and (2) the inverse relation (aks) between description and ruling. The author first defines asl as the maqis 'alayh (the basis of analogy). He distinguishes between invalid multiplicity (of analogical evidences or aspects of similarity) and valid multiplicity of asls. The Hanafi example is wiping the head (masah al-ra's) in wudu: we consider it masah (wiping), not ghusl, so triple repetition is not sunnah. Its asls are wiping over khuff, jabirah, and tayammum. Al-Shafi'i considers it a rukn, so triple repetition is sunnah, but he has only washing as an asl. The second criterion: a description that both persists (itrad) and inverts (aks) is better than one that only persists. Itrad means the ruling exists when the description exists; aks means the ruling is absent when the description is absent. The same masah example illustrates: because it is masah, repetition is not sunnah; conversely, what is not masah (like washing the face) has repetition sunnah. al-Shafi'i's view fails the aks test because madmadah and istinshaq are not rukn yet repetition is sunnah.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-asl): The maqis 'alayh (basis of analogy) in qiyas.
الاطراد (al-itrad): Consistency: the ruling exists when the description exists.
الانعكاس (al-in'ikas): Inverse: the ruling is absent when the description is absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the second valid tarjih criterion described in the passage, and what Arabic term is used for it?
A) Multiplicity of asls; كَثْرَةُ الأصول
B) Absence at absence; العَكْس
C) Consistency; الإطْراد
D) Analogy; القياس

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul uses multiplicity of asls and the inverse relation (aks) to prefer one description in qiyas over another, as illustrated by the masah example.

Intention Specification in Restitution: The Hanafi Rule
Ruling that intention specification is not required when returning property under a known legal cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that intention specification is not required when returning property under a known legal cause, and apply the usul principle that context determines the illah.

Core Idea
When the cause is clear, intention specification is unnecessary; the context determines the ruling.

This passage addresses whether a person returning property that was in their possession as a trust, usurpation, or invalid sale must verbally specify which category they intend. The Hanafi position is that no specification is required because the legal reality (haqiqah) of the payment is self-determined by the context. The author strengthens this ruling by comparing it to the obligatoriness of fasting, where the intention is automatically attached to the act itself. This lesson explores the usul principle that when the cause (illah) is evident, the intention (niyyah) is effectively implied, and examines the Shafi'i objection that this comparison is flawed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Act and Question
The act is returning property that was held under one of three categories: trust (wadi'ah), usurpation (ghasb), or invalid sale (bay' fasad). The question is whether the person must specify which category they intend when making the return.
The categories are distinct in fiqh: trust is amanah, usurpation is daman, invalid sale requires returning the price or goods.
2
State the Hanafi Rule
Specification (ta'yin al-daf') is not required. The reason is that the reality of the payment is self-determined (mut'ayyin) – the context makes the intention clear. There is no probability of another direction (jihah) because the act of returning the specific property itself identifies the underlying cause.
This rule is based on the principle that when the cause is singular and evident, the intention is necessarily attached to it.
3
Understand the Analogy (Qiyas) Used
The author compares this to the obligatoriness (fardiyyah) of fasting: just as the intention of fasting is automatically attached to the act of fasting during Ramadan (without requiring a separate verbal specification), so too the intention of returning is automatically attached to the act of returning property under a known cause.
The analogy is that in both cases, the ruling (wujub or obligation) is inherently linked to the act, so specification is unnecessary.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i Objection and Response
The Shafi'is object that such an analogy is invalid because the obligatoriness of fasting is a pure obligation (fard) whereas returning property is a restitution. The Hanafi response is that the objection only applies if one takes mere obligatoriness as the illah; but the Hanafis do not base the rule purely on obligatoriness but on the self-determined nature of the payment.
The tarjih (preference) is that the specification is necessarily attached, as supported by the analogy.
5
Derive the Usul Principle
From this passage, we derive the usul rule: When the legal cause (sabab or illah) is singular and evident, the intention (niyyah) is automatically aligned with that cause, and no separate verbal specification is required. This is a branch of the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applied in a context where the maqsad is clear from the action itself.
This principle is used in other fiqh areas, such as differentiating acts of worship from customs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يشترط تعيين الدفع من حيث كونه الخ ۔ نیت کی تعیین کی اس ادائے گی میں کوئی شرط نہیں ہے کہ آیا بحیثیت ودیعت (امانت) کے یا غصب کے یا بیچ فاسد ہونے کی وجہ سے واپس کر رہا ہے کیونکہ اس کی بہت خود متعین ہے۔ دوسری کی جہت کا اس میں احتمال نہیں ہے لہذا تعیین کا اپنے حکم کے ساتھ لازم ہو نا زیادہ قوی ہے یہ نسبت فرضیت کا اپنے حکم کے ساتھ لازم ہونے کے ۔ ہونا وقيل عَلَيْه ترجیح کی اس وجہ پر شوافع کی جانب سے اعتراض کیا گیا ہے کہ یہ اعتراض اس وقت وارد ہو سکتا تھا جبکہ مستدل صرف فرضیت کو علت قرار دیتا اگر جب وہ فرضیت صوم کو علت قرار دیتے ہیں تو مناسب نہیں ہے کہ اس کے مقابلے میں دریعت مئی مغصوب اور بیع فاسد کے مسئلہ کو لا نا مناسب نہیں ہے۔
And specification of the payment is not required in terms of its being... [Urdu: In this payment, specification of intention is not required whether he is returning it as trust (amana), or usurped, or due to an invalid sale, because its reality is self-determined. There is no probability of another direction in it, therefore specification being necessarily attached to its ruling is stronger, like the relation of obligatoriness to its ruling. And it was said upon it tarjih, an objection by the Shafi'is, that this objection could occur when the deductor takes mere obligatoriness as the illah. If they take the obligatoriness of fasting as the illah, then it is not appropriate to bring the case of returning a trust, usurped goods, and invalid sale in comparison to it.]
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage deals with the issue of specifying intention when returning property that was in one's possession under different legal categories: trust (wadi'ah), usurpation (ghasb), or invalid sale (bay' fasad). The ruling is that the payer does not need to verbalize which category he intends because the context itself determines the nature of the payment. For example, if one is returning a borrowed item, the intention is automatically 'return of trust'. The author argues that specification is necessarily connected to the ruling, similar to how obligatoriness (fardiyyah) is necessarily connected to its ruling. This is presented as a valid tarjih (preference) against a Shafi'i objection that such cases cannot be compared to fasting. The point is that the illah (cause) is automatically present in these restitution cases.

Key Terms
تعيين الدفع (ta'yin al-daf'): Specification of the intention in making a payment/return.
الوديعة (al-wadi'ah): Trust; property left for safekeeping.
الغلبة (al-ghalb): The dominant cause or context.

Key Takeaway
Intention specification is not required in restitution when the legal cause is evident from context; this is derived from the principle that the reality of the act determines the ruling.

Tarjih by Multiplicity of Asls and Inverse
Detailed Urdu commentary on two valid tarjih criteria for qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi tarjih criteria of kathrat al-usul and al-'aks to compare conflicting qiyas arguments.

Core Idea
Multiplicity of asls and valid inverse strengthen a qiyas; a description with both itrad and in'ikas is stronger than one with only itrad.

This lesson unpacks two numbered criteria from the matn: multiplicity of basis analogies (kathrat al-usul) and the inverse relationship ('aks). These are used in Hanafi usul to weigh competing analogies. The classic example of wiping the head (masah al-ra's) illustrates how Hanafis use multiple asls and a valid inverse to argue that triple repetition is not sunnah, while the Shafi'i position fails on both counts.

Guided Path
1
Understand Kathrat al-Usul
Identify that kathrat al-usul means a qiyas is supported by multiple basis cases (asls). This gives it strength over a qiyas with fewer asls. Distinguish it from unrelated multiplicity like multiple textual proofs.
The term asl here means the original case (maqis 'alayh) in qiyas.
2
Understand Al-'Aks (Inverse)
Learn that a valid description has two properties: itrad (when description exists, ruling exists) and in'ikas (when description is absent, ruling is absent). A description that is only muttarid (lacks in'ikas) is weaker.
In'ikas is proven by showing the ruling changes when the description changes.
3
Apply to the Masah Example
Examine the Hanafi argument: wiping (masah) does not require triple repetition. The asls are wiping over khuff, jabirah, and tayammum—all without triple repetition. The inverse: what is not masah (like washing) requires repetition.
This gives both multiplicity of asls (3 asls vs Shafi'i's 1) and a valid inverse.
4
Compare with Shafi'i Position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that wiping is a rukn, so triple repetition is sunnah by analogy with washing. But his description (being a rukn) lacks a valid inverse: madmadah and istinshaq are not rukn yet repetition is sunnah there, so the inverse fails.
Thus Hanafi tarjih uses both criteria to prefer its position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اور استنشاقی دونوں رکن نہیں ہیں اور اس کے باوجو د تکرار مسنون ہے۔
And by multiplicity of its asls (3): Multiplicity of asls means that when for a single qiyas one maqis 'alayh gives testimony, and in contrast another qiyas has two asls (maqis 'alayh) testifying, or several asls witness, then preference is given to the first qiyas. And by asl is meant maqis 'alayh. And this multiplicity that is mentioned does not mean multiplicity of analogical evidences, nor multiplicity of similarities of something, because these are invalid. And multiplicity of asls is correct and reliable, like our statement regarding wiping the head: that because it is wiping, triple repetition is not sunnah, for its asl and maqis 'alayh are wiping over khuff and wiping over jabirah (where there is no triple repetition) and similarly tayammum (where it is included but not repeated). Contrary to Imam Shafi'i's statement that wiping is a rukn, therefore triple repetition is sunnah, because he has no asl and maqis except washing. And by absence at absence (4): Absence of the ruling from the description in the state of its absence, and this is called aks. That is, when a description has both itrad and in'ikas, it is better than a description that is only muttarid but not mun'akis. So itrad here means when the description exists, the ruling exists; and in'ikas means when the description is absent, the ruling is also absent. Like our statement regarding wiping the head: because it is wiping, repetition is not sunnah, because its inverse will come that what is not wiping, repetition is sunnah, like washing the face or other washed limbs. Contrary to Imam Shafi'i's statement that wiping is a rukn, so repetition is sunnah, because its inverse (if something is not a rukn, repetition is not sunnah) does not occur, because madmadah and istinshaq are not rukn, yet with that repetition is not sunnah.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This section provides a detailed Urdu commentary on two numbered points (3 and 4) from the matn regarding valid tarjih criteria. Point 3: Multiplicity of asls (kathrat al-usul). When a single qiyas has multiple asls (basis analogies), it is preferred over a qiyas with fewer asls. This is distinguished from invalid forms like multiplicity of analogical evidences or multiple similarities. The same masah al-ra's example is used: our asls are wiping over khuff, jabirah, and tayammum (none require triple repetition), while Shafi'i only has washing. Point 4: Al-'adam 'inda al-'adam (absence at absence) i.e., aks. A description that possesses both itrad (existence of ruling with description) and in'ikas (absence of ruling with absence of description) is stronger than one with only itrad. The masah example: because it is masah, no repetition; what is not masah requires repetition. Shafi'i's view fails because madmadah and istinshaq are not rukn yet repetition is sunnah, so his description lacks aks.

Key Terms
كثرة الأصول (kathrat al-usul): Multiplicity of basis analogies (asls) for a qiyas, a valid tarjih criterion.
العكس (al-'aks): Inverse relationship: ruling absent when description absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi example of wiping the head, what provides the multiplicity of asls?
A) Multiple verses from the Quran
B) Wiping over khuff, jabirah, and tayammum
C) The analogy with washing the face
D) The fact that it is a rukn

Key Takeaway
A description that is both muttarid and mun'akis is stronger than one that is only muttarid.

Conflict of Tarjih: Essence vs. Description in Usurped Sheep Case
Explains the rule when two grounds of tarjih conflict, applied to usurped sheep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that preponderance in the essence (dhāt) takes precedence over preponderance in the state (ḥāl) to resolve conflicting qiyas arguments.

Core Idea
When two grounds of tarjih conflict, the preponderance in the essence prevails over that in the description.

This lesson explores a foundational usul rule: when two considerations (tarjīḥ) conflict, the one tied to the essence (dhāt) overrides the one tied to a subordinate state (ḥāl). We will see how this rule resolves the classic case of a usurped sheep that has been cooked and roasted, and how the Hanafi school differs from al-Shāfiʿī on which aspect is 'essential'.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify the rule from the text: 'al-rujhān fī al-dhāt aḥaqqu minhu fī al-ḥāl' – the preponderance in the essence is more deserving than that in the state.
The rule is a meta-principle of tarjih in qiyas.
2
Understand the justification
The state (ḥāl) is established by the essence (dhāt) and is subordinate to it in existence; the subordinate has no standing against the predominant.
This is a logical priority.
3
Apply to the usurped sheep case
Identify the two conflicting considerations: the owner's original ownership (state) vs. the usurper's industry of cooking/roasting (essence).
Both are valid aspects but one is more fundamental.
4
Determine essence vs. state per Hanafis
The industry (ṣanʿah) is treated as the essence because it pervades the object from all aspects, while the physical object (ʿayn) is a mere description.
This is the precise meaning (al-diqah) rather than the apparent reality.
5
Compare with al-Shafi'i's view
Al-Shafi'i sees the physical sheep as the essence and the industry as subordinate, so the owner takes the sheep.
The difference stems from which aspect is considered dhāt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ أَرَادَ أَنْ يُبَيِّنَ حُكْمَ تَعَارُضِ التَّرْجِيحَيْنِ فَقَالَ وَإِذَا تَعَارَضَا ضَرْبَا تَرْجِيحٍ كَمَا تَعَارَضَا أَصْلُ الْقِيَاسَيْنِ كَانَ الرُّجْحَانُ فِي الذَّاتِ أَحَقُّ مِنْهُ فِي الْحَالِ أَيْ مِنَ الرُّجْحَانِ الْحَاصِلِ فِي الْحَالِ لِأَنَّ الْحَالَ قَائِمَةٌ بِالذَّاتِ تَابِعَةٌ لَهَا فِي الْوُجُودِ وَلَا ظُهُورَ لِلتَّابِعِ فِي مُقَابَلَةِ الْمَتْبُوعِ فَيَنْقَطِعُ حَقُّ الْمَالِكِ بِالطَّبْخِ وَالشَّيِّ تَفْرِيعٌ عَلَى الْقَاعِدَةِ الْمَذْكُورَةِ وَذَلِكَ بِأَنَّهُ إِذَا غَصَبَ رَجُلٌ شَاةَ رَجُلٍ ثُمَّ ذَبَحَهَا وَطَبَخَهَا وَشَوَاهَا فَإِنَّهُ يَنْقَطِعُ عِنْدَنَا حَقُّ الْمَالِكِ عَنِ الشَّاةِ وَيَضْمَنُ قِيمَتَهَا لِمَالِكِهَا لِأَنَّهُ تَعَارَضَ هَاهُنَا ضَرْبَا تَرْجِيحٍ فَإِنَّهُ إِنْ نُظِرَ إِلَى أَنَّ أَصْلَ الشَّاةِ كَانَ لِلْمَالِكِ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَأْخُذَهَا الْمَالِكُ وَيَصْطَنِعَ النَّقْصَ وَإِنْ نُظِرَ إِلَى أَنَّ الطَّبْحَ وَالشَّيَّ كَانَا مِنَ الْغَاصِبِ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَأْخُذَهَا الْغَاصِبُ وَيَصْمُتَ الْقِيمَةَ وَلَكِنْ عِنَايَةَ هَذَا الْجَانِبِ أَقْوَىٰ مِنْ رِعَايَةِ الْمَالِكِ لِأَنَّ الصَّنْعَةَ قَائِمَةٌ بِذَاتِهَا مِنْ كُلِّ وَجْهٍ وَالْعَيْنُ مَالِكَةٌ مِنْ وَجْهٍ فَحَقُّ الْمَالِكِ فِي الْعَيْنِ ثَابِتٌ مِنْ وَجْهٍ دُونَ وَجْهٍ وَحَقُّ الْغَاصِبِ فِي الصَّنْعَةِ ثَابِتٌ مِنْ كُلِّ وَجْهٍ كَانَتِ الصَّنْعَةُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الذَّاتِ وَالْعَيْنُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْوَصْفِ وَإِنْ كَانَ الْأَمْرُ فِي ظَاهِرِ الْحَالِ بِالْعَكْسِ إِذْ كَانَتِ الشَّاةُ أَصْلًا وَالصَّنْعَةُ وَصْفًا عَلَى مَا ذَهَبَ إِلَيْهِ الشَّافِعِيُّ وَأَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ الْمُصَنِّفُ بِقَوْلِهِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ صَاحِبُ الْأَصْلِ وَهُوَ الْمَالِكُ أَحَقُّ لِأَنَّ الصَّنْعَةَ قَائِمَةٌ بِالْمَصْنُوعِ تَابِعَةٌ لَهُ فَجَرَى الشَّافِعِيُّ عَلَى ظَاهِرِهِ وَجَرَيْنَا نَحْنُ عَلَى الدِّقَّةِ
Then he wanted to explain the ruling of conflict of the two types of tarjih, so he said: And when two types of tarjih conflict, as when the principles of two qiyases conflict, the preponderance in the essence is more deserving than that in the state, i.e., than the preponderance obtained in the state, because the state is established by the essence, subordinate to it in existence, and there is no manifestation of the subordinate in the presence of the predominant. So the owner's right is cut off by cooking and roasting, as a derivation on the mentioned rule. That is, if a person usurps another's sheep, then slaughters it, cooks it and roasts it, then according to us the owner's right to the sheep is cut off and he guarantees its value to its owner, because here two types of tarjih conflict: if one looks to the original sheep, it belonged to the owner, so the owner should take it and make good the deficiency; and if one looks to the cooking and roasting, they were from the usurper, so the usurper should take it and be silent regarding the value. But consideration of this side is stronger than consideration of the owner, because the craftsmanship is established in itself from every aspect, while the physical object is owned from one aspect. So the owner's right to the physical object is established from one aspect, not from another, and the usurper's right to the craftsmanship is established from every aspect. Thus the craftsmanship is like the essence, and the physical object like the description, even though the matter in apparent reality is the opposite, since the sheep is the origin and the craftsmanship is the description, as al-Shafi'i held and the author pointed out by his saying: And al-Shafi'i said: The owner of the origin, i.e., the owner, is more entitled, because the craftsmanship is established in the product, subordinate to it. So al-Shafi'i followed its apparent meaning, and we followed the precise meaning.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage explains the rule when two grounds of tarjih (preponderance) conflict in a qiyas. The author states that the preponderance based on the essence (dhāt) is more deserving than that based on a state (ḥāl) or description, because the state is dependent on the essence. He then applies this to the case of a usurped sheep that is slaughtered, cooked, and roasted. Two conflicting considerations arise: the owner's original ownership vs. the usurper's added work (industry). Hanafis give preponderance to the essence (the industry) over the description (the physical object), ruling that the usurper keeps the cooked sheep and pays its value. This is because the industry is established from all aspects, while the owner's right to the physical object is only from one aspect (ownership). Imam al-Shafi'i, however, considers the physical object as the essence and the industry as subordinate, so the owner should take the sheep and compensate for the work. The Hanafi view is based on a precise analysis (al-diqah), while the Shafi'i view follows the apparent reality (al-ẓāhir).

Key Terms
الذات (al-dhāt): The essence or the core attribute that is independently established.
الحال (al-ḥāl): A state or attribute that is subordinate to the essence.
الصنعة (al-ṣan'ah): The work or industry (like slaughtering, cooking, roasting) added by the usurper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a usurped sheep that is cooked, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The owner takes the cooked sheep and must pay the usurper for the work
B) The usurper keeps the sheep but pays its value to the owner
C) Both parties share the sheep equally
D) The sheep is destroyed and the usurper pays full price

Key Takeaway
The rule that the essence (dhāt) outranks the state (ḥāl) in tarjih is key to understanding Hanafi priority of transformative work over original ownership in usurpation cases.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
beginner
6 min
Invalid Forms of Tarjīḥ in Hanafī Uṣūl
Lists invalid grounds for tarjīḥ in Hanafī uṣūl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three forms of tarjīḥ deemed invalid by the Hanafīs and explain why they are rejected.

Core Idea
Hanafīs reject tarjīḥ based on counting similarities, generality, or fewness of descriptions.

In the previous lesson, we learned about valid grounds for giving preponderance in qiyās. The author now turns to invalid forms. According to the Hanafī school, three specific arguments—preponderance by number of similarities, generality of description, and simplicity of description—are not acceptable. This contrasts with the Shāfiʿī school, which accepts them. Understanding this disagreement is key to correctly applying tarjīḥ in Hanafī uṣūl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transition
Notice that the author has just completed a discussion of valid tarjīḥāt and now moves to invalid ones. This structural marker helps you organize the material.
2
List the three invalid grounds
Memorize the three Arabic terms: ghalabat al-ashbāh, al-'umūm, and qillat al-awṣāf. Each refers to a specific type of argument that Hanafīs reject for establishing preponderance.
Refer to the glossary for definitions.
3
Understand the Hanafī reasoning
These grounds are considered unreliable for indicating the true effective cause. They are not sufficient to outweigh other evidence in qiyās.
The passage does not elaborate, but the principle is that tarjīḥ must be based on intrinsic strength, not mere counting.
4
Contrast with the Shāfiʿī position
Imām al-Shāfiʿī accepts all three as valid grounds. This is a classic point of ikhtilāf between the schools.
The practical consequence: a Shāfiʿī might give preponderance where a Hanafī would not.
5
Apply in analysis of qiyās
When you encounter a qiyās argument that relies on one of these grounds, you can immediately identify it as invalid for tarjīḥ in the Hanafī school.
Practice by creating simple analogies and testing whether the proposed tarjīḥ is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لَمَّا فَرَغَ عَنْ بَيَانِ التَّرْجِيحَاتِ الصَّحِيحَةِ شَرَعَ فِي الْفَاسِدَةِ فَقَالَ وَالتَّرْجِيحُ بِغَلَبَةِ الْأَشْبَاهِ وَبِالْعُمُومِ وَقِلَّةِ الْأَوْصَافِ فَاسِدٌ عِنْدَنَا وَقَدْ ذَهَبَ إِلَى صِحَّةِ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهَا الْإِمَامُ الشَّافِعِيُّ
When he finished the explanation of the correct tarjīḥāt, he began [explaining] the invalid ones, and he said: And tarjīḥ by preponderance of similarities, and by generality, and by fewness of descriptions is invalid according to us. And Imām al-Shāfiʿī has gone to the validity of each of them.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This short passage marks the transition from valid to invalid grounds of tarjīḥ (preponderance) in qiyās. The author enumerates three invalid grounds according to the Hanafī school: (1) preponderance by the number of similarities (ghalabat al-ashbāh) between the branch and one of the two conflicting analogies; (2) preponderance by generality ('umūm) of the description; and (3) preponderance by having fewer descriptions (qillat al-awṣāf). The Hanafīs consider these as invalid (fāsid) for establishing preponderance. In contrast, Imām al-Shāfiʿī regards each of these as valid grounds for tarjīḥ. The passage is a clear statement of a school-specific rule.

Key Terms
غَلَبَةُ الأَشْبَاهِ (ghalabat al-ashbāh): Preponderance by counting the number of similarities between the branch and each analogy.
العُمُوم (al-'umūm): Preponderance by the generality of the description (i.e., the description being more general).
قِلَّةُ الأَوْصَافِ (qillat al-awṣāf): Preponderance by having fewer descriptions (i.e., the description being simpler).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT considered a valid ground for tarjih according to the Hanafis?
A) Preponderance by the number of similarities
B) Preponderance by the strength of the ‘illa
C) Preponderance by generality
D) Preponderance by fewness of descriptions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafī school explicitly rejects tarjīḥ by ghalabat al-ashbāh, al-'umūm, and qillat al-awṣāf, contrasting with the Shāfiʿī acceptance.
